where  $\mathbf{u}_i \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^k$  and  $u_i \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p$ ,  $\mathbf{d}_i$  is uniformly distributed in  $\mathsf{span}(\mathbf{B})$  if  $\beta = 0$ , and in  $\mathsf{span}(\mathbf{B}, \mathbf{b}_1)$  otherwise. Thus, the view of  $\mathcal{A}$  corresponds to  $\mathsf{G}_0^{(\zeta,\ell)\text{-KE-ind}}$  if  $\beta = 0$ , and  $\mathsf{H}_1$  otherwise. This concludes the proof.

**Lemma 5.** For all PPT adversaries A, we have

$$|\Pr[\langle \mathcal{A}, \mathsf{H}_1 \rangle = 1] - \Pr[\langle \mathcal{A}, \mathsf{H}_2 \rangle = 1]| \leq 2^{-\varOmega(\lambda)}.$$

*Proof.* We redefine  $\mathbf{W}_i = \widetilde{\mathbf{W}}_i + t_i \mathbf{a}_{\ell}^* \mathbf{b}_1^{*^{\top}}$  for  $i \in [\omega]$ ,  $\hat{\mathbf{s}}_i = \hat{\mathbf{s}}_i' + u_i \mathbf{b}_1^*$  for  $i \in [n_2]$ , and  $\hat{\mathbf{r}}_i = \hat{\mathbf{r}}_i' + v_i \mathbf{a}_{\ell}^*$  for  $i \in [m_2]$ , where  $\widetilde{\mathbf{W}}_i \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{(k+\zeta)\times(k+\zeta)}$ ,  $\hat{\mathbf{s}}_i'$ ,  $\hat{\mathbf{r}}_i' \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{k+\zeta}$ , and  $t_i, u_i, v_i \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p$ . This change clearly does not affect the distributions of  $\mathbf{W}_i$ ,  $\hat{\mathbf{s}}_i$  and  $\hat{\mathbf{r}}_i$ . This affects  $\mathcal{A}$ 's view as follows:

 $P: \mathbf{W}_i^{\top} \mathbf{A} = \widetilde{\mathbf{W}}_i^{\top} \mathbf{A}, \quad \mathbf{W}_i \mathbf{B} = \widetilde{\mathbf{W}}_i \mathbf{B}.$ 

 $\mathfrak{O}_{\mathfrak{X}} \colon \mathbf{c}(\mathbf{c}_{0}, \widehat{\mathbf{S}}, \mathbb{W}) = \mathbf{c}(\mathbf{c}_{0}, \widehat{\mathbf{S}}, \widetilde{\mathbb{W}}) + \mathbf{c}(\mathbf{a}_{\ell}^{*^{\top}} \mathbf{c}_{0}, \mathbf{u}, \mathbf{t}) \otimes \mathbf{b}_{1}^{*}, \text{ where } \widetilde{\mathbb{W}} = (\widetilde{\mathbf{W}}_{1}, \dots, \widetilde{\mathbf{W}}_{\omega}), \mathbf{u} = (u_{1}, \dots, u_{n_{2}}),$ and  $\mathbf{t} = (t_{1}, \dots, t_{\omega}).$  Note that  $\mathbf{c}(\mathbf{a}_{\ell}^{*^{\top}} \mathbf{c}_{0}, \mathbf{u}, \mathbf{t}) \otimes \mathbf{b}_{1}^{*}$  denotes  $(c_{1}\mathbf{b}_{1}^{*}, \dots, c_{n_{3}}\mathbf{b}_{1}^{*}),$  where  $(c_{1}, \dots, c_{n_{3}}) = \mathbf{c}(\mathbf{a}_{\ell}^{*^{\top}} \mathbf{c}_{0}, \mathbf{u}, \mathbf{t}).$ 

 $\mathfrak{O}_{\vartheta} \colon \mathbf{k}(\mathbf{R}, \widetilde{\mathbf{R}}, \widetilde{\mathbf{W}}) = \mathbf{k}(\mathbf{R}, \widehat{\mathbf{R}}, \widetilde{\mathbb{W}}) + \mathbf{k}(\mathbf{r}, \mathbf{v}, \mathbf{t}) \otimes \mathbf{a}_{\ell}^{*}, \text{ where } \mathbf{r} = (\mathbf{b}_{1}^{*^{\top}} \mathbf{d}_{1}, \dots, \mathbf{b}_{1}^{*^{\top}} \mathbf{d}_{m_{1}}) \text{ and } \mathbf{v} = (0, v_{1}, \dots, v_{m_{2}}).$ 

Thanks to the PMH of  $\Gamma$ , the following distributions are almost identical:

$$\{\overline{\mathbf{A}}, \overline{\mathbf{B}}, \mathbf{c}_0, \mathbf{R}, \mathbf{c}(\mathbf{a}_{\ell}^{*^{\top}} \mathbf{c}_0, \mathbf{u}, \mathbf{t}), \mathbf{k}(\mathbf{r}, \mathbf{v}, \mathbf{t})\}$$
 and  $\{\overline{\mathbf{A}}, \overline{\mathbf{B}}, \mathbf{c}_0, \mathbf{R}, \mathbf{c}(\mathbf{a}_{\ell}^{*^{\top}} \mathbf{c}_0, \mathbf{u}, \mathbf{t}), \mathbf{k}(\mathbf{r}, \mathbf{v} + (\mu, \mathbf{0}), \mathbf{t})\},$ 

<span id="page-18-0"></span>where  $\mu \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p$ . This is because  $\mathbf{a}_{\ell}^{*^{\top}} \mathbf{c}_0$  and  $\mathbf{b}_1^{*^{\top}} \mathbf{d}_i$  are distributed statistically close to being uniform in  $\mathbb{Z}_p$ . Thus,  $\mathcal{A}$ 's view is not changed even if we change the first element of  $\mathbf{v}$  from 0 to  $\mu$  except negligible probability. In other words,  $\mathbf{k}(\mathbf{R}, \widehat{\mathbf{R}}, \mathbb{W})$  and  $\mathbf{k}(\mathbf{R}, \widehat{\mathbf{R}}, \mathbb{W}) + \mathbf{k}(\mathbf{0}, (\mu, \mathbf{0}), \mathbf{0}) \otimes \mathbf{a}_{\ell}^*$  are identically distributed except negligible probability. The latter exactly corresponds to  $\mathcal{A}$ 's view in  $\mathsf{H}_2$ . This concludes the proof.

**Lemma 6.** For all PPT adversaries A, there exists a PPT adversary B such that

$$|\Pr[\langle \mathcal{A}, \mathsf{H}_2 \rangle = 1] - \Pr[\langle \mathcal{A}, \mathsf{G}_1^{(\zeta,\ell)\text{-KE-ind}} \rangle = 1]| \leq \mathsf{Adv}_{\mathcal{B}}^{\mathcal{D}_k\text{-MDDH}}(\lambda).$$

This lemma can be proven similarly to Lemma 4.

## <span id="page-19-0"></span>4 Predicate Transformations

In this section, we present several transformations for predicates, which enable us to construct a more expressive predicate from simple predicates. As shown later in §6, these transformations are sufficiently powerful to construct ABE schemes whose constructions from standard assumptions are still unknown. Concretely, we introduce four transformations called the direct sum, dual transformation, KP augmentation, and CP augmentation. Because the CP augmentation is obtained from the dual transformation and KP augmentation, the former three transformations are sufficient for our framework. We also present the corresponding transformations of PESs for each predicate transformation and prove that these PES transformations preserve the  $(\zeta, \ell)$ -KE-ind property. Starting from PESs with the single-variable PMH, which already satisfy  $(\zeta, \ell)$ -KE-ind, we can obtain a PES for a expressive predicate that satisfies  $(\zeta', \zeta')$ -KE-ind for some constant  $\zeta'$ . Finally, we show that we can use the PES with  $(\zeta', \zeta')$ -KE-ind to construct an adaptively secure ABE scheme in §5.

### <span id="page-19-1"></span>4.1 Direct Sum of Predicate Families

**Definition 13 (Direct Sum [9]).** Let  $\mathsf{P}_{\kappa_i}^{(i)}: \mathfrak{X}_{\kappa_i}^{(i)} \times \mathfrak{Y}_{\kappa_i}^{(i)} \to \{0,1\}$  be a predicate family. Let  $\kappa = (\kappa_1, \ldots, \kappa_d)$ . A predicate family for the direct sum of a predicate family set  $\mathfrak{P}_{\kappa} = (\mathsf{P}_{\kappa_1}^{(1)}, \ldots, \mathsf{P}_{\kappa_d}^{(d)})$ , denoted by  $\mathsf{DS}[\mathfrak{P}_{\kappa}]: \bar{\mathfrak{X}}_{\kappa} \times \bar{\mathfrak{Y}}_{\kappa} \to \{0,1\}$ , is defined as follows: let  $\bar{\mathfrak{X}}_{\kappa} = \bigcup_{i \in [d]} (\{i\} \times \mathfrak{X}_{\kappa_i}^{(i)}), \bar{\mathfrak{Y}}_{\kappa} = \bigcup_{i \in [d]} (\{i\} \times \mathfrak{Y}_{\kappa_i}^{(i)})$ , and define

$$\mathsf{DS}[\mathcal{P}_\kappa]((i_x,x),(i_y,y)) \Leftrightarrow (i_x=i_y) \wedge (\mathsf{P}_{\kappa_{i_y}}^{(i_y)}(x,y)=1).$$

We sometimes use another notation,  $\mathsf{P}_{\kappa_1}^{(1)} \odot \cdots \odot \mathsf{P}_{\kappa_d}^{(d)}$ , to denotes  $\mathsf{DS}[\mathcal{P}_{\kappa}]$ .

**PES** for  $\mathsf{DS}[\mathcal{P}_\kappa]$ . Let  $\Gamma_i = (\mathsf{Param}_i, \mathsf{EncCt}_i, \mathsf{EncKey}_i, \mathsf{Pair}_i)$  be a PES for  $\mathsf{P}_{\kappa_i}^{(i)}$ . We construct a PES for  $\mathsf{DS}[\mathcal{P}_\kappa]$ , denoted by  $\mathsf{DS-Trans}(\Gamma) = (\mathsf{Param}', \mathsf{EncCt}', \mathsf{EncKey}', \mathsf{Pair}')$ , where  $\Gamma = (\Gamma_1, \dots, \Gamma_d)$ .

- Param'(par)  $\rightarrow \omega'$ : Run  $\omega_i \leftarrow \text{Param}_i(\text{par})$  and output  $\sum_{i \in [d]} \omega_i$ . This specifies common variables  $\mathbf{w}' = (\mathbf{w}^{(1)}, \dots, \mathbf{w}^{(d)})$ , where  $\mathbf{w}^{(i)} = (w_1^{(i)}, \dots, w_{\omega_i}^{(i)})$ .
- $\ \mathsf{EncCt'}((i_x,x)) \to (n_1',n_2',\mathbf{c'}(\mathbf{s'},\hat{\mathbf{s}}',\mathbf{w'})) \colon$ 
  - Output  $(n_1, n_2, \mathbf{c}(\mathbf{s}, \hat{\mathbf{s}}, \mathbf{w}^{(i_x)})) \leftarrow \mathsf{EncCt}_{i_x}(x)$ .
  - Define  $n'_1 = n_1, n'_2 = n_2, \mathbf{s}' = \mathbf{s}$ , and  $\hat{\mathbf{s}}' = \hat{\mathbf{s}}$ .
- EncKey'( $(i_y, y)$ )  $\rightarrow (m'_1, m'_2, \mathbf{k}'(\mathbf{r}', \hat{\mathbf{r}}', \mathbf{w}'))$ :
  - Output  $(m_1, m_2, \mathbf{k}(\mathbf{r}, \hat{\mathbf{r}}, \mathbf{w}^{(i_y)})) \leftarrow \mathsf{EncKey}_{i_y}(y)$ .
  - Define  $m'_1 = m_1$ ,  $m'_2 = m_2$ ,  $\mathbf{r}' = \mathbf{r}$ , and  $\hat{\mathbf{r}}' = \hat{\mathbf{r}}$ .
- $\mathsf{Pair}'((i_x, x), (i_y, y)) \to (\mathbf{E}', \overline{\mathbf{E}}')$  and correctness:
  - Output  $(\mathbf{E}, \overline{\mathbf{E}}) \leftarrow \mathsf{Pair}_{i_n}(x, y)$ .
  - Correctness of  $\mathsf{Pair}'$  directly follows from that of  $\mathsf{Pair}_{i_n}$ .

<span id="page-19-2"></span>**Theorem 5** (( $\zeta, \ell$ )-KE-ind of DS-Trans( $\Gamma$ )). If  $\Gamma_i$  satisfies ( $\zeta, \ell$ )-KE-ind for all  $i \in [d]$ , then DS-Trans( $\Gamma$ ) satisfies ( $\zeta, \ell$ )-KE-ind. More precisely, for all PPT adversaries A, there exist PPT adversary B such that

$$\mathsf{Adv}_{\mathcal{A},\mathsf{DS-Trans}(\Gamma)}^{(\zeta,\ell)\text{-KE-ind}}(\lambda) \leq d \max_{i \in [d]} \mathsf{Adv}_{\mathcal{B},\Gamma_i}^{(\zeta,\ell)\text{-KE-ind}}(\lambda).$$

```
\begin{split} & \frac{\mathsf{G}_{\beta}^{(\zeta,\ell)\text{-KE-ind}}}{\omega_{i} \leftarrow \mathsf{Param}_{i}(\mathsf{par}), \ \mathbb{G} \leftarrow \mathcal{G}_{\mathsf{BG}}(1^{\lambda})}{\mathbf{A}, \overline{\mathbf{B}} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_{p}^{(k+\zeta)\times(k+\zeta)}, \ \mathbb{W}_{i} = (\mathbf{W}_{i,1}, \dots, \mathbf{W}_{i,\omega_{i}}) \leftarrow (\mathbb{Z}_{p}^{(k+\zeta)\times(k+\zeta)})^{\omega_{i}} \\ & P = (\mathbb{G}, [\mathbf{A}]_{\eta}, [\mathbf{B}]_{3-\eta}, \{\mathbf{a}_{i}^{*}\}_{i \in [\ell,\zeta]}, \{\mathbf{b}_{i}^{*}\}_{i \in [\ell+1,\zeta]}, \{[\mathbf{W}_{i,j}^{\top}\mathbf{A}]_{\eta}, [\mathbf{W}_{i,j}\mathbf{B}]_{3-\eta}\}_{i \in [d], j \in [\omega_{i}]}) \\ & \beta' \leftarrow \mathcal{A}^{\mathbb{O}_{\overline{\mathcal{X}}}(\cdot), \mathbb{O}_{\overline{\mathcal{Y}}}(\cdot, \cdot)}(P) \\ \hline & \frac{\mathcal{O}_{\overline{\mathcal{X}}}(\cdot)}{\mathsf{Input}} : (i_{x}, x) \in \overline{\mathcal{X}}_{\kappa} \\ & (n_{1}, n_{2}, \mathbf{c}(\mathbf{s}, \hat{\mathbf{s}}, \mathbf{w}^{(i_{x})})) \leftarrow \mathsf{EncCt}_{i_{x}}(x) \\ & \mathbf{c}_{0} \leftarrow \mathsf{span}(\mathbf{A}, \mathbf{a}_{1}, \dots, \mathbf{a}_{\ell}), \ \mathbf{s}_{1}, \dots, \mathbf{s}_{n_{1}} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_{p}^{k}, \ \hat{\mathbf{s}}_{1}, \dots, \hat{\mathbf{s}}_{n_{2}} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_{p}^{k+\zeta} \\ & \mathbf{S} = (\mathbf{c}_{0}, \mathbf{A}\mathbf{s}_{1}, \dots, \mathbf{A}\mathbf{s}_{n_{1}}), \ \hat{\mathbf{S}} = (\hat{\mathbf{s}}_{1}, \dots, \hat{\mathbf{s}}_{n_{2}}) \\ & \mathsf{Output}: ([\mathbf{S}]_{\eta}, [\mathbf{c}(\mathbf{S}, \hat{\mathbf{S}}, \mathbb{W}_{i_{x}})]_{\eta}) \\ & \frac{\mathcal{O}_{\overline{\mathcal{Y}}}(\cdot, \cdot)}{\mathsf{Input}} : (i_{y}, y) \in \bar{\mathcal{Y}}_{\kappa} \ \text{and} \ \mathbf{h} \in \mathbb{Z}_{p}^{k+\zeta} \\ & (m_{1}, m_{2}, \mathbf{k}(\mathbf{r}, \hat{\mathbf{r}}, \mathbf{w}^{(i_{y})})) \leftarrow \mathsf{EncKey}_{i_{y}}(y) \\ & \mu \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_{p}, \ \mathbf{r}_{1}, \dots, \mathbf{r}_{m_{1}} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_{p}^{k}, \ \hat{\mathbf{r}}_{1}, \dots, \hat{\mathbf{r}}_{m_{2}} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_{p}^{k+\zeta} \\ & \mathbf{R} = (\mathbf{Br}_{1}, \dots, \mathbf{Br}_{m_{1}}), \ \hat{\mathbf{R}} = (\mathbf{h} + \boxed{\beta}\mu\mathbf{a}_{\ell}^{*}, \hat{\mathbf{r}}_{1}, \dots, \hat{\mathbf{r}}_{m_{2}}) \\ & \mathsf{Output}: ([\mathbf{R}]_{3-\eta}, [\mathbf{k}(\mathbf{R}, \hat{\mathbf{R}}, \mathbb{W}_{i_{y}})]_{3-\eta}) \\ \end{aligned}
```

<span id="page-20-0"></span>**Fig 2.**  $(\zeta, \ell)$ -KE-ind game for DS-Trans $(\Gamma)$ .

*Proof.* For  $\beta \in \{0,1\}$ , we can describe the  $(\zeta,\ell)$ -KE-ind game  $\mathsf{G}_{\beta}^{(\zeta,\ell)$ -KE-ind} for DS-Trans( $\Gamma$ ) as shown in Fig 2. To prove the theorem, we consider an adversary  $\mathcal{B}$ , which samples  $t \leftarrow [d]$  and interacts with  $\mathcal{O}_{\chi(t)}$  and  $\mathcal{O}_{\mathcal{Y}^{(t)}}$  of the  $(\zeta,\ell)$ -KE-ind game for  $\Gamma_t$ .  $\mathcal{B}$  internally runs an adversary  $\mathcal{A}$  against  $(\zeta,\ell)$ -KE-ind of DS-Trans( $\Gamma$ ) and interacts with it as follows:

- 1. Let  $\omega_i \leftarrow \mathsf{Param}_i(\mathsf{par})$ .  $\mathcal{B}$  is given  $(\mathbb{G}, [\mathbf{A}]_{\eta}, [\mathbf{B}]_{3-\eta}, \{\mathbf{a}_i^*\}_{i \in [\ell, \zeta]}, \{\mathbf{b}_i^*\}_{i \in [\ell+1, \zeta]}, \{[\mathbf{W}_{t,j}^{\top} \mathbf{A}]_{\eta}, [\mathbf{W}_{t,j} \mathbf{B}]_{3-\eta}\}_{j \in [\omega_t]})$ . It then samples  $\mathbb{W}_i = (\mathbf{W}_{i,1}, \dots, \mathbf{W}_{i,\omega_i}) \leftarrow (\mathbb{Z}_p^{(k+\zeta) \times (k+\zeta)})^{\omega_i}$  for  $i \in [d] \setminus t$ .
- 2.  $\mathcal{B}$  gives to  $\mathcal{A}$  the following elements:  $\mathbb{G}$ ,  $[\mathbf{A}]_{\eta}$ ,  $[\mathbf{B}]_{3-\eta}$ ,  $\{\mathbf{a}_{i}^{*}\}_{i\in[\ell,\zeta]}$ ,  $\{\mathbf{b}_{i}^{*}\}_{i\in[\ell+1,\zeta]}$ , together with  $\{[\mathbf{W}_{i,j}^{\top}\mathbf{A}]_{\eta}$ ,  $[\mathbf{W}_{i,j}\mathbf{B}]_{3-\eta}\}_{i\in[d],j\in[\omega_{i}]}$
- 3. For  $\mathcal{A}$ 's query to  $\mathcal{O}_{\bar{\chi}}$  on  $(i_x, x)$ ,  $\mathcal{B}$  replies as follows:
  - If  $i_x = t$ ,  $\mathcal{B}$  queries its own oracle  $\mathcal{O}_{\mathfrak{X}^{(t)}}$  on x and gives the reply, which is  $([\mathbf{S}]_{\eta}, [\mathbf{c}(\mathbf{S}, \widehat{\mathbf{S}}, \mathbb{W}_t)]_{\eta})$ , to  $\mathcal{A}$ .
  - If  $i_x \neq t$ ,  $\mathcal{B}$  computes  $\mathbf{c}(\mathbf{s}, \hat{\mathbf{s}}, \mathbf{w}^{(i_x)})$ ,  $\mathbf{S}$ , and  $\widehat{\mathbf{S}}$  as show below, and gives  $([\mathbf{S}]_{\eta}, [\mathbf{c}(\mathbf{S}, \widehat{\mathbf{S}}, \mathbb{W}_{i_x})]_{\eta})$  to  $\mathcal{A}$ :

$$\begin{split} &(n_1,n_2,\mathbf{c}(\mathbf{s},\hat{\mathbf{s}},\mathbf{w}^{(i_x)})) \leftarrow \mathsf{EncCt}_{i_x}(x), \ \ \mathbf{c}_0 \leftarrow \mathsf{Ker}(\mathbf{a}_{\ell+1}^*,\dots,\mathbf{a}_{\zeta}^*), \\ &\mathbf{s}_1,\dots,\mathbf{s}_{n_1} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^k, \ \ \hat{\mathbf{s}}_1,\dots,\hat{\mathbf{s}}_{n_2} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{k+\zeta} \\ &\mathbf{S} = (\mathbf{c}_0,\mathbf{A}\mathbf{s}_1,\dots,\mathbf{A}\mathbf{s}_{n_1}), \ \ \hat{\mathbf{S}} = (\hat{\mathbf{s}}_1,\dots,\hat{\mathbf{s}}_{n_2}). \end{split}$$

Note that  $\mathsf{span}(\mathbf{A}, \mathbf{a}_1, \dots, \mathbf{a}_\ell) = \mathsf{Ker}(\mathbf{a}_{\ell+1}^*, \dots, \mathbf{a}_\zeta^*).$ 

- 4. For  $\mathcal{A}$ 's query to  $\mathcal{O}_{\bar{y}}$  on  $(i_y, y)$ ,  $\mathcal{B}$  replies as follows:
  - If  $i_y = t$ ,  $\mathcal{B}$  queries its own oracle  $\mathcal{O}_{y(t)}$  on y and gives the reply, which is  $([\mathbf{R}]_{3-\eta}, [\mathbf{k}(\mathbf{R}, \widehat{\mathbf{R}}, \mathbb{W}_t)]_{3-\eta})$ , to  $\mathcal{A}$ . Note that the first element of  $\widehat{\mathbf{R}}$  is  $\mathbf{h}$  (if  $\beta = 0$ ) or  $\mathbf{h} + \mu \mathbf{a}_{\ell}^*$  (if  $\beta = 1$ ).
  - If  $i_y \neq t$ ,  $\mathcal{B}$  aborts the interaction with  $\mathcal{A}$  and outputs a random bit  $\beta'$
- 5.  $\mathcal{B}$  outputs  $\mathcal{A}$ 's output as it is.

In the above experiment,  $\mathcal{B}$  correctly simulates  $\mathcal{O}_{\bar{\chi}}$ . Since  $\mathcal{B}$  aborts the experiment if  $i_y \neq t$ , we focus on the case of  $i_y = t$ , which occurs with probability 1/d. Note that since  $i_x = t \Rightarrow \mathsf{P}^{(t)}(x,y) = 0$  from the game condition for DS-Trans( $\Gamma$ ),  $\mathcal{B}$  follow the game condition for  $\Gamma_t$ . If  $\beta = 0$  in the KE-ind game for  $\Gamma_t$ ,  $\mathcal{A}$ 's view corresponds to that in  $\mathsf{G}_0^{(\zeta,\ell)\text{-KE-ind}}$ , and it corresponds to  $\mathsf{G}_1^{(\zeta,\ell)\text{-KE-ind}}$  otherwise. Thus, we have  $\Pr[i_y = t] \cdot \mathsf{Adv}_{\mathcal{A},\mathsf{DS-Trans}(\Gamma)}^{(\zeta,\ell)\text{-KE-ind}}(\lambda) + \Pr[i_y \neq t] \cdot 0 \leq \mathsf{Adv}_{\mathcal{B},\Gamma_t}^{(\zeta,\ell)\text{-KE-ind}}(\lambda) \leq \max_{i \in [d]} \mathsf{Adv}_{\mathcal{B},\Gamma_i}^{(\zeta,\ell)\text{-KE-ind}}(\lambda)$ . This concludes the proof.

#### <span id="page-21-0"></span>**Dual Predicates**

Recall that the dual of  $P_{\kappa}: \mathcal{X}_{\kappa} \times \mathcal{Y}_{\kappa} \to \{0,1\}$  is  $\mathsf{Dual}[\mathsf{P}_{\kappa}]: \bar{\mathcal{X}}_{\kappa} \times \bar{\mathcal{Y}}_{\kappa} \to \{0,1\}$  where  $\bar{\mathcal{X}}_{\kappa} = \mathcal{Y}_{\kappa}$  and  $\mathcal{Y}_{\kappa} = \mathcal{X}_{\kappa}$ , and  $\mathsf{Dual}[\mathsf{P}_{\kappa}](x,y) = \mathsf{P}_{\kappa}(y,x)$ .

**PES** for Dual $[P_{\kappa}]$ . Let  $\Gamma = (Param, EncCt, EncKey, Pair)$  be a PES for  $P_{\kappa}$ . We construct a PES for  $\mathsf{Dual}[\mathsf{P}_{\kappa}]$ , denoted by  $\mathsf{Dual}\text{-}\mathsf{Trans}(\varGamma)$  as follows.

- Param'(par)  $\rightarrow \omega'$ : Run  $\omega \leftarrow$  Param(par) and output  $\omega + 1$ . This specifies common variables  $\mathbf{w}' =$  $(w_0, w_1, \ldots, w_{\omega})$ , where  $w_0$  is a new common variable.
- $\mathsf{EncCt}'(x) \to (n'_1, n'_2, \mathbf{c}'(\mathbf{s}', \hat{\mathbf{s}}', \mathbf{w}'))$ :
  - Run  $(m_1, m_2, \mathbf{k}(\mathbf{r}, \hat{\mathbf{r}}, \mathbf{w})) \leftarrow \mathsf{EncKey}(x)$ . Let  $s_{\mathsf{new}}$  be a new special non-lone variable. Polynomials  $\mathbf{c}'(\mathbf{s}',\hat{\mathbf{s}}',\mathbf{w}')$  are defined the same as  $\mathbf{k}(\mathbf{r},\hat{\mathbf{r}},\mathbf{w})$  except that  $\alpha$  is replaced with  $s_{\mathsf{new}}w_0$ .
- Define  $n_1' = m_1$ ,  $n_2' = m_2$ ,  $\mathbf{s}' = (s_{\mathsf{new}}, \mathbf{r})$ , and  $\hat{\mathbf{s}}' = \hat{\mathbf{r}}_{-\alpha}$ . EncKey' $(y) \to (m_1', m_2', \mathbf{k}'(\mathbf{r}', \hat{\mathbf{r}}', \mathbf{w}))$ :
- - Run  $(n_1, n_2, \mathbf{c}(\mathbf{s}, \hat{\mathbf{s}}, \mathbf{w})) \leftarrow \mathsf{EncCt}(y)$ . Let  $\alpha_{\mathsf{new}}$  be a new special lone variable. Polynomials  $\mathbf{k}'(\mathbf{r}',\hat{\mathbf{r}}',\mathbf{w}')$  are defined the same as  $\mathbf{c}(\mathbf{s},\hat{\mathbf{s}},\mathbf{w})$  except that a polynomial  $\alpha_{\mathsf{new}} - s_0 w_0$  is added as the first element of  $\mathbf{k}'(\mathbf{r}', \hat{\mathbf{r}}', \mathbf{w}')$ .
  - Define  $m'_1 = n_1 + 1$ ,  $m'_2 = n_2$ ,  $\mathbf{r'} = \mathbf{s}$ , and  $\hat{\mathbf{r}}' = (\alpha_{\mathsf{new}}, \hat{\mathbf{s}})$ .
- $\mathsf{Pair}'(x,y) \to (\mathbf{E}',\overline{\mathbf{E}}')$  and correctness:
  - Run  $(\mathbf{E}, \overline{\mathbf{E}}) \leftarrow \mathsf{Pair}(y, x)$ . Define  $\mathbf{E}' = \begin{pmatrix} 1 \\ \overline{\mathbf{E}}^\top \end{pmatrix}$  and  $\overline{\mathbf{E}}' = \mathbf{E}^\top$ .
  - For correctness, we have

$$\begin{split} \mathbf{s}'\mathbf{E}'\mathbf{k}'^\top + \mathbf{c}'\overline{\mathbf{E}}'\mathbf{r}'^\top = &(s_{\mathsf{new}}, \mathbf{r}) \left(\begin{smallmatrix} 1 \\ \overline{\mathbf{E}}^\top \end{smallmatrix}\right) (\alpha_{\mathsf{new}} - s_0 w_0, \mathbf{c})^\top + \mathbf{k}|_{\alpha \mapsto s_{\mathsf{new}} w_0} \mathbf{E}^\top \mathbf{s}^\top \\ = & s_{\mathsf{new}} \alpha_{\mathsf{new}} - s_{\mathsf{new}} s_0 w_0 + s_{\mathsf{new}} s_0 w_0 = s_{\mathsf{new}} \alpha_{\mathsf{new}}. \end{split}$$

**Theorem 6** ( $(\zeta, \ell)$ -KE-ind of Dual-Trans $(\Gamma)$ ). Let  $2 \le \ell \le \zeta$ . If  $\Gamma$  satisfies  $(\zeta, \ell-1)$ -KE-ind, then Dual-Trans( $\Gamma$ ) satisfies  $(\zeta, \ell)$ -KE-ind under the  $\mathfrak{D}_k$ -MDDH assumption. More precisely, for all PPT adversaries A, there exist PPT adversaries  $B_1$  and  $B_2$  such that

$$\mathsf{Adv}_{\mathcal{A},\mathsf{Dual-Trans}(\varGamma)}^{(\zeta,\ell)\text{-KE-ind}}(\lambda) \leq \mathsf{Adv}_{\mathcal{B}_1,\varGamma}^{(\zeta,\ell-1)\text{-KE-ind}}(\lambda) + 2\mathsf{Adv}_{\mathcal{B}_2}^{\mathcal{D}_k\text{-MDDH}}(\lambda) + 2^{-\varOmega(\lambda)}.$$

*Proof.* For  $\beta \in \{0,1\}$ , we can describe the  $(\zeta,\ell)$ -KE-ind game  $\mathsf{G}_{\beta}^{(\zeta,\ell)$ -KE-ind for Dual-Trans $(\Gamma)$  as shown in Fig 3. To show this theorem, we consider two intermediate hybrids H<sub>1</sub> and H<sub>2</sub>, which are also described in Fig 3. That is,  $H_1$  (resp.  $H_2$ ) is defined the same as  $G_0^{(\zeta,\ell)-KE-ind}$  (resp.  $G_1^{(\zeta,\ell)-KE-ind}$ ) except that  $\mathbf{d}_0$ , the first elements of  $\mathbf{R}$  generated in  $\mathcal{O}_{\bar{y}}$ , is set as  $\mathbf{d}_0 \leftarrow \mathsf{span}(\mathbf{B}, \mathbf{b}_1, \dots, \mathbf{b}_{\ell-1})$  instead of  $\mathbf{Br}_0$  where  $\mathbf{r}_0 \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^k$ . From Lemma 7,8,9 below, we have  $\mathsf{G}_0^{(\zeta,\ell)\text{-KE-ind}} \approx_c \mathsf{H}_1 \approx_c \mathsf{H}_2 \approx_c \mathsf{G}_1^{(\zeta,\ell)\text{-KE-ind}}$ . This concludes the proof.

<span id="page-21-1"></span>**Lemma 7.** For all PPT adversaries  $\mathcal{A}$ , there exists a PPT adversary  $\mathcal{B}$  such that  $|\Pr[\langle \mathcal{A}, \mathsf{G}_0^{(\zeta,\ell)\text{-KE-ind}} \rangle =$  $|1| - \Pr[\langle \mathcal{A}, \mathsf{H}_1 \rangle = 1]| \leq \mathsf{Adv}_{\mathcal{B}}^{\mathcal{D}_k - \mathsf{MDDH}}(\lambda).$ 

*Proof.* We describe the reduction algorithm  $\mathcal{B}$ .  $\mathcal{B}$  is given an instance of  $\mathcal{U}_{k+\ell-1,k}$  problem,  $(\mathbb{G}, [\mathbf{M}]_{3-\eta}, \mathbb{G})$  $[\mathbf{t}_{\beta}]_{3-\eta})$  where  $\mathbf{t}_0 = \mathbf{M}\mathbf{u}$  and  $\mathbf{t}_1 = \mathbf{v}$ , where  $\mathbf{u} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^k$  and  $\mathbf{v} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{k+\ell-1}$ . Then,  $\mathcal{B}$  chooses  $\mathbf{X} \leftarrow \mathsf{GL}_{k+\zeta}(\mathbb{Z}_p)$ 

$$\overline{\mathbf{B}} = \mathbf{X} \begin{pmatrix} \widehat{\overline{\mathbf{M}}} \ \mathbf{I}_{\ell-1} \\ \underline{\mathbf{M}} \ \mathbf{I}_{\zeta-\ell+1} \end{pmatrix}, \ \ (\overline{\mathbf{B}}^\top)^{-1} = (\mathbf{X}^\top)^{-1} \begin{pmatrix} (\widehat{\mathbf{M}}^\top)^{-1} \ -(\widehat{\mathbf{M}}^\top)^{-1} \underline{\mathbf{M}}^\top \\ \mathbf{I}_{\ell-1} \\ \mathbf{I}_{\zeta-\ell+1} \end{pmatrix},$$

where  $\mathbf{M}$  is the matrix consisting of the first k rows of  $\mathbf{M}$ , and  $\mathbf{M}$  is that consisting of the last  $\ell-1$ rows of M. Then, B can compute

$$[\mathbf{B}]_{3-\eta} = \left[\mathbf{X} \begin{pmatrix} \mathbf{M} \\ \mathbf{O} \end{pmatrix}\right]_{3-\eta}, \ (\mathbf{b}_{\ell+1}^*||\dots||\mathbf{b}_{\zeta}^*) = (\mathbf{X}^\top)^{-1} \begin{pmatrix} \mathbf{O} \\ \mathbf{I}_{\zeta-\ell} \end{pmatrix}.$$

```
\begin{split} & \qquad \qquad \mathsf{G} \in \left\{ \mathsf{G}_{0}^{(\zeta,\ell)\text{-KE-ind}}, \boxed{\mathsf{H}_{1}}, \boxed{\mathsf{H}_{2}}, \mathsf{G}_{1}^{(\zeta,\ell)\text{-KE-ind}} \right\} \\ & \qquad \qquad \subseteq \mathsf{Param}(\mathsf{par}), \ \ \mathbb{G} \leftarrow \mathcal{G}_{\mathsf{BG}}(1^{\lambda}) \\ & \qquad \qquad \qquad \qquad \qquad \qquad \qquad \qquad \qquad \qquad \qquad \qquad \qquad \qquad \qquad \qquad \qquad \qquad
```

<span id="page-22-0"></span>**Fig 3.**  $(\zeta, \ell)$ -KE-ind game for Dual-Trans $(\Gamma)$ .

 $\mathfrak{B}$  generates  $\overline{\mathbf{A}}$  and  $\mathbb{W}$  by itself and computes the input P for  $\mathcal{A}$  from them. When  $\mathcal{A}$  queries  $\mathfrak{O}_{\bar{\chi}}$ ,  $\mathfrak{B}$  replies honestly as shown in Fig 3. When  $\mathcal{A}$  queries  $\mathfrak{O}_{\bar{y}}$ ,  $\mathfrak{B}$  replies honestly except that it sets

$$[\mathbf{d}_0]_{3-\eta} = \left[\mathbf{X} \begin{pmatrix} \mathbf{t}_\beta \\ \mathbf{0} \end{pmatrix}\right]_{3-\eta}, \ \ [\mathbf{R}]_{3-\eta} = [(\mathbf{d}_0, \mathbf{Br}_1, \dots, \mathbf{Br}_{m_1})]_{3-\eta}.$$

Now since we can write  $\mathbf{t}_{\beta} = \left( \widehat{\mathbf{M}} \right) \mathbf{u}_1 + \beta \left( \mathbf{I}_{\ell-1}^{\mathbf{O}} \right) \mathbf{u}_2$ , where  $\mathbf{u}_1 \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^k$  and  $\mathbf{u}_2 \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{\ell-1}$ , we have that  $\mathbf{d}_0$  is uniformly distributed in  $\mathsf{span}(\mathbf{B})$  if  $\beta = 0$ , and in  $\mathsf{span}(\mathbf{B}, \mathbf{b}_1, \dots, \mathbf{b}_{\ell-1})$  otherwise. Thus, the view of  $\mathcal{A}$  corresponds to  $\mathsf{G}_0^{(\zeta,\ell)\text{-KE-ind}}$  if  $\beta = 0$ , and  $\mathsf{H}_1$  otherwise. This concludes the proof.

<span id="page-22-1"></span>**Lemma 8.** For all PPT adversaries  $\mathcal{A}$ , there exists a PPT adversary  $\mathcal{B}$  such that  $|\Pr[\langle \mathcal{A}, \mathsf{H}_1 \rangle = 1] - \Pr[\langle \mathcal{A}, \mathsf{H}_2 \rangle = 1]| \leq \mathsf{Adv}_{\mathcal{B}, \Gamma}^{(\zeta, \ell-1)\text{-KE-ind}}(\lambda) + 2^{-\Omega(\lambda)}$ .

*Proof.* We show that the outputs of  $\mathcal{O}_{\bar{y}}$  in  $\mathsf{H}_1$  and  $\mathsf{H}_2$  are computationally indistinguishable if the PES  $\Gamma$  for  $\mathsf{P}_{\kappa}$  satisfies  $(\zeta,\ell-1)$ -KE-ind. We construct a PPT adversary  $\mathcal{B}$  against  $(\zeta,\ell-1)$ -KE-ind of  $\Gamma$  that internally runs a PPT distinguisher  $\mathcal{A}$  between  $\mathsf{H}_1$  and  $\mathsf{H}_2$ .  $\mathcal{B}$  behaves as follows.

- 1.  $\mathcal{B}$  is given an input of  $(\zeta, \ell-1)$ -KE-ind game for  $\Gamma$ ,  $(\mathbb{G}, [\mathbf{M}]_{3-\eta}, [\mathbf{N}]_{\eta}, {\{\mathbf{m}_i^*\}_{i \in [\ell-1,\zeta]}, \{\mathbf{n}_i^*\}_{i \in [\ell,\zeta]}, {\{\mathbf{N}_i^*\}_{i \in [\ell]}, {\{\mathbf{N}_i^*\}_{i \in [\ell]}, {\{\mathbf{N}_i^*\}_{i \in [\ell]}, {\{\mathbf{N}_i^*\}_{i \in [\ell]}, {\{\mathbf{N}_i^*\}_{i \in [\ell]}, {\{\mathbf{N}_i^*\}_{i \in [\ell]}, {\{\mathbf{N}_i^*\}_{i \in [\ell]}, {\{\mathbf{N}_i^*\}_{i \in [\ell]}, {\{\mathbf{N}_i^*\}_{i \in [\ell]}, {\{\mathbf{N}_i^*\}_{i \in [\ell]}, {\{\mathbf{N}_i^*\}_{i \in [\ell]}, {\{\mathbf{N}_i^*\}_{i \in [\ell]}, {\{\mathbf{N}_i^*\}_{i \in [\ell]}, {\{\mathbf{N}_i^*\}_{i \in [\ell]}, {\{\mathbf{N}_i^*\}_{i \in [\ell]}, {\{\mathbf{N}_i^*\}_{i \in [\ell]}, {\{\mathbf{N}_i^*\}_{i \in [\ell]}, {\{\mathbf{N}_i^*\}_{i \in [\ell]}, {\{\mathbf{N}_i^*\}_{i \in [\ell]}, {\{\mathbf{N}_i^*\}_{i \in [\ell]}, {\{\mathbf{N}_i^*\}_{i \in [\ell]}, {\{\mathbf{N}_i^*\}_{i \in [\ell]}, {\{\mathbf{N}_i^*\}_{i \in [\ell]}, {\{\mathbf{N}_i^*\}_{i \in [\ell]}, {\{\mathbf{N}_i^*\}_{i \in [\ell]}, {\{\mathbf{N}_i^*\}_{i \in [\ell]}, {\{\mathbf{N}_i^*\}_{i \in [\ell]}, {\{\mathbf{N}_i^*\}_{i \in [\ell]}, {\{\mathbf{N}_i^*\}_{i \in [\ell]}, {\{\mathbf{N}_i^*\}_{i \in [\ell]}, {\{\mathbf{N}_i^*\}_{i \in [\ell]}, {\{\mathbf{N}_i^*\}_{i \in [\ell]}, {\{\mathbf{N}_i^*\}_{i \in [\ell]}, {\{\mathbf{N}_i^*\}_{i \in [\ell]}, {\{\mathbf{N}_i^*\}_{i \in [\ell]}, {\{\mathbf{N}_i^*\}_{i \in [\ell]}, {\{\mathbf{N}_i^*\}_{i \in [\ell]}, {\{\mathbf{N}_i^*\}_{i \in [\ell]}, {\{\mathbf{N}_i^*\}_{i \in [\ell]}, {\{\mathbf{N}_i^*\}_{i \in [\ell]}, {\{\mathbf{N}_i^*\}_{i \in [\ell]}, {\{\mathbf{N}_i^*\}_{i \in [\ell]}, {\{\mathbf{N}_i^*\}_{i \in [\ell]}, {\{\mathbf{N}_i^*\}_{i \in [\ell]}, {\{\mathbf{N}_i^*\}_{i \in [\ell]}, {\{\mathbf{N}_i^*\}_{i \in [\ell]}, {\{\mathbf{N}_i^*\}_{i \in [\ell]}, {\{\mathbf{N}_i^*\}_{i \in [\ell]}, {\{\mathbf{N}_i^*\}_{i \in [\ell]}, {\{\mathbf{N}_i^*\}_{i \in [\ell]}, {\{\mathbf{N}_i^*\}_{i \in [\ell]}, {\{\mathbf{N}_i^*\}_{i \in [\ell]}, {\{\mathbf{N}_i^*\}_{i \in [\ell]}, {\{\mathbf{N}_i^*\}_{i \in [\ell]}, {\{\mathbf{N}_i^*\}_{i \in [\ell]}, {\{\mathbf{N}_i^*\}_{i \in [\ell]}, {\{\mathbf{N}_i^*\}_{i \in [\ell]}, {\{\mathbf{N}_i^*\}_{i \in [\ell]}, {\{\mathbf{N}_i^*\}_{i \in [\ell]}, {\{\mathbf{N}_i^*\}_{i \in [\ell]}, {\{\mathbf{N}_i^*\}_{i \in [\ell]}, {\{\mathbf{N}_i^*\}_{i \in [\ell]}, {\{\mathbf{N}_i^*\}_{i \in [\ell]}, {\{\mathbf{N}_i^*\}_{i \in [\ell]}, {\{\mathbf{N}_i^*\}_{i \in [\ell]}, {\{\mathbf{N}_i^*\}_{i \in [\ell]}, {\{\mathbf{N}_i^*\}_{i \in [\ell]}, {\{\mathbf{N}_i^*\}_{i \in [\ell]}, {\{\mathbf{N}_i^*\}_{i \in [\ell]}, {\{\mathbf{N}_i^*\}_{i \in [\ell]}, {\{\mathbf{N}_i^*\}_{i \in [\ell]}, {\{\mathbf{N}_i^*\}_{i \in [\ell]}, {\{\mathbf{N}_i^*\}_{i \in [\ell]}, {\{\mathbf{N}_i^*\}_{i \in [\ell]}, {\{\mathbf{N}_i^*\}_{i \in [\ell]}, {\{\mathbf{N}_i^*\}_{i \in [\ell]}, {\{\mathbf{N}_i^*\}_{i \in [\ell]}, {\{\mathbf{N}_i^*\}_{i \in [\ell]}, {\{\mathbf{N}_i^*\}_{i \in [\ell]}, {\{\mathbf{N}_i^*\}_{i \in [\ell]}, {\{\mathbf{N}_i^*\}_{i \in [\ell]}, {\{\mathbf{N}_i^*\}_{i \in [\ell]}, {\{\mathbf{N}_i^*\}$
- 2.  $\mathcal{B}$  samples  $\mathbf{W}_0 \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{(k+\zeta)\times(k+\zeta)}$  and gives  $P = (\mathbb{G}, [\mathbf{A}]_{\eta}, [\mathbf{B}]_{3-\eta}, \{\mathbf{a}_i^*\}_{i\in[\ell,\zeta]}, \{\mathbf{b}_i^*\}_{i\in[\ell+1,\zeta]}, \{[\mathbf{W}_i^{\top}\mathbf{A}]_{\eta}, [\mathbf{W}_i\mathbf{B}]_{3-\eta}\}_{i\in[\omega]^+})$  to  $\mathcal{A}$ .
- 3. For  $\mathcal{A}$ 's query to  $\mathcal{O}_{\bar{\mathcal{X}}}$  on x,  $\mathcal{B}$  samples  $\mathbf{c}_0 \leftarrow \mathsf{Ker}(\mathbf{a}_{\ell+1}^*, \dots, \mathbf{a}_{\zeta}^*)$  and queries its own oracle  $\mathcal{O}_{\mathcal{Y}}$  on  $(x, \mathbf{W}_0^{\mathsf{T}} \mathbf{c}_0)$  to obtain  $([\mathbf{T}]_{\eta}, [\mathbf{k}(\mathbf{T}, \widehat{\mathbf{T}}, \mathbb{V})]_{\eta})$ , where

$$\mathbf{T} = (\mathbf{N}\mathbf{t}_0, \mathbf{N}\mathbf{t}_1, \dots, \mathbf{N}\mathbf{t}_{m_1}) = (\mathbf{A}\mathbf{t}_0, \mathbf{A}\mathbf{t}_1, \dots, \mathbf{A}\mathbf{t}_{m_1}),$$

$$\hat{\mathbf{T}} = (\mathbf{W}_0^{\top}\mathbf{c}_0 + \beta\hat{\mu}\mathbf{m}_{\ell-1}^*, \hat{\mathbf{t}}_1, \dots, \hat{\mathbf{t}}_{m_2}) = (\mathbf{W}_0^{\top}\mathbf{c}_0 + \beta\hat{\mu}\mathbf{b}_{\ell-1}^*, \hat{\mathbf{t}}_1, \dots, \hat{\mathbf{t}}_{m_2}),$$

$$\mathbb{V} = (\mathbf{V}_1, \dots, \mathbf{V}_{\omega}) = (\mathbf{W}_1^{\top}, \dots, \mathbf{W}_{\omega}^{\top}).$$

Note that  $\hat{\mu}$  is a random value in  $\mathbb{Z}_p$  chosen by  $\mathcal{O}_{\mathcal{Y}}$ .  $\mathcal{B}$  implicitly defines that  $\mathbf{s}_i = \mathbf{t}_i$  for  $i \in [m_1]^+$ ,  $\hat{\mathbf{s}}_i = \hat{\mathbf{t}}_i$  for  $i \in [m_2]$ ,  $\mathbf{S} = \mathbf{T}$ ,  $\hat{\mathbf{S}} = \hat{\mathbf{T}}$ , and  $\mathbb{W} = \mathbb{V}$ .  $\mathcal{B}$  replies  $([\mathbf{c}_0]_{\eta}, [\mathbf{S}]_{\eta}, [\mathbf{k}(\mathbf{S}, \hat{\mathbf{S}}, \mathbb{W})]_{\eta})$  to  $\mathcal{A}$ . Note that  $\mathsf{span}(\mathbf{A}, \mathbf{a}_1, \dots, \mathbf{a}_{\ell}) = \mathsf{Ker}(\mathbf{a}_{\ell+1}^*, \dots, \mathbf{a}_{\ell}^*)$ .

4. For  $\mathcal{A}$ 's query to  $\mathcal{O}_{\bar{y}}$  with y and  $\mathbf{h}$ ,  $\mathcal{B}$  queries its own oracle  $\mathcal{O}_{\mathfrak{X}}$  on y to obtain  $([\mathbf{U}]_{3-\eta}, [\mathbf{c}(\mathbf{U}, \widehat{\mathbf{U}}, \mathbb{V})]_{3-\eta})$ , where

$$\mathbf{U} = (\mathbf{o}_0, \mathbf{M}\mathbf{u}_1, \dots, \mathbf{M}\mathbf{u}_{n_1}) = (\mathbf{o}_0, \mathbf{B}\mathbf{u}_1, \dots, \mathbf{B}\mathbf{u}_{n_1}), \quad \widehat{\mathbf{U}} = (\hat{\mathbf{u}}_1, \dots, \hat{\mathbf{u}}_{n_2}).$$

Note that  $\mathbf{o}_0$  is randomly distributed in  $\operatorname{span}(\mathbf{M}, \mathbf{m}_1, \dots, \mathbf{m}_{\ell-1})$ , which equals to  $\operatorname{span}(\mathbf{B}, \mathbf{b}_1, \dots, \mathbf{b}_{\ell-1})$ .  $\mathcal{B}$  implicitly defines that  $\mathbf{r}_i = \mathbf{u}_i$  for  $i \in [n_1]$ ,  $\hat{\mathbf{r}}_i = \hat{\mathbf{u}}_i$  for  $i \in [n_2]$ ,  $\mathbf{R} = \mathbf{U}$ ,  $\hat{\mathbf{R}} = \hat{\mathbf{U}}$ , and  $\mathbf{d}_0 = \mathbf{o}_0$ .  $\mathcal{B}$  replies  $([\mathbf{h} - \mathbf{W}_0 \mathbf{d}_0]_{3-\eta}, [\mathbf{R}]_{3-\eta}, [\mathbf{c}(\mathbf{R}, \hat{\mathbf{R}}, \mathbb{W})]_{3-\eta})$  to  $\mathcal{A}$ .

5.  $\mathcal{B}$  outputs  $\mathcal{A}$ 's output as it is.

At a glance, this simulation seems that the distribution of the reply from  $\mathcal{O}_{\widetilde{\mathcal{X}}}$  is changed. However, entire views of  $\mathcal{A}$  correspond to  $\mathsf{H}_1$  and  $\mathsf{H}_2$ . To see this, we redefine  $\mathbf{W}_0$  as  $\mathbf{W}_0 = \widetilde{\mathbf{W}}_0 - \frac{\beta \hat{\mu}}{\mathbf{a}_*^* \mathbf{l}_0} \mathbf{a}_\ell^* \mathbf{b}_{\ell-1}^*$ 

where  $\widetilde{\mathbf{W}}_0 \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{(k+\zeta)\times(k+\zeta)}$ . Clearly, this does not change the distribution of  $\mathbf{W}_0$ . This affects  $\mathcal{A}$ 's view as follows:

$$\begin{split} P: \ \mathbf{W}_0^{\top} \mathbf{A} &= \widetilde{\mathbf{W}}_0^{\top} \mathbf{A}, \ \mathbf{W}_0 \mathbf{B} &= \widetilde{\mathbf{W}}_0 \mathbf{B}. \\ \mathfrak{O}_{\widetilde{\chi}}: \ \mathbf{W}_0^{\top} \mathbf{c}_0 + \beta \widehat{\mu} \mathbf{b}_{\ell-1}^* &= \widetilde{\mathbf{W}}_0^{\top} \mathbf{c}_0. \\ \mathfrak{O}_{\widetilde{y}}: \ \mathbf{h} - \mathbf{W}_0 \mathbf{d}_0 &= \mathbf{h} - \widetilde{\mathbf{W}}_0 \mathbf{d}_0 + \frac{\beta \widehat{\mu} \mathbf{b}_{\ell-1}^{*^{\top}} \mathbf{d}_0}{\mathbf{a}_{\ell}^{*^{\top}} \mathbf{c}_0} \mathbf{a}_{\ell}^* &= \mathbf{h} - \widetilde{\mathbf{W}}_0 \mathbf{d}_0 + \beta \mu \mathbf{a}_{\ell}^*. \end{split}$$

Because  $\hat{\mu}$  is randomly distributed in  $\mathbb{Z}_p$ , we can set  $\mu = \frac{\hat{\mu} \mathbf{b}_{\ell-1}^{*} \mathbf{d}_0}{\mathbf{a}_{\ell}^{*} \mathbf{c}_0}$  if  $\mathbf{b}_{\ell-1}^{*} \mathbf{d}_0 \neq 0$  and  $\mathbf{a}_{\ell}^{*} \mathbf{c}_0 \neq 0$ . Since  $\mathbf{c}_0$  and  $\mathbf{d}_0$  are randomly distributed in  $\mathsf{span}(\mathbf{A}, \mathbf{a}_1, \dots, \mathbf{a}_{\ell})$  and  $\mathsf{span}(\mathbf{B}, \mathbf{b}_1, \dots, \mathbf{b}_{\ell-1})$ , respectively, this is the case with an overwhelming probability. Thus,  $\mathcal{A}$ 's view corresponds to  $\mathsf{H}_1$  if  $\beta = 0$  in the  $(\zeta, \ell)$ -KE-ind game of  $\Gamma$ , and it corresponds to  $\mathsf{H}_2$  otherwise. This concludes the proof.

<span id="page-23-1"></span>**Lemma 9.** For all PPT adversaries  $\mathcal{A}$ , there exists a PPT adversary  $\mathcal{B}$  such that  $|\Pr[\langle \mathcal{A}, \mathsf{H}_2 \rangle = 1] - \Pr[\langle \mathcal{A}, \mathsf{G}_1^{(\zeta,\ell)\text{-KE-ind}} \rangle = 1]| \leq \mathsf{Adv}_{\mathcal{B}}^{\mathcal{D}_k\text{-MDDH}}(\lambda).$ 

The proof of Lemma 9 is similar to Lemma 7, and hence we omit it here.

### <span id="page-23-0"></span>4.3 Key-Policy Augmentation

<span id="page-23-2"></span>**Definition 14 (Key-Policy Augmentation).** A predicate family for key-policy Boolean formula augmentation over a single predicate family  $P_{\kappa}: \mathfrak{X}_{\kappa} \times \mathfrak{Y}_{\kappa} \to \{0,1\}$ , denoted by  $\mathsf{KBF1}[P_{\kappa}]: \bar{\mathfrak{X}}_{\kappa} \times \bar{\mathfrak{Y}}_{\kappa} \to \{0,1\}$ , where  $\bar{\mathfrak{X}}_{\kappa} = \mathfrak{X}_{\kappa}$  and  $\bar{\mathfrak{Y}}_{\kappa} = \bigcup_{i \in \mathbb{N}} (\mathfrak{Y}_{\kappa}^{i} \times \mathfrak{F}_{i})$ , where  $\mathfrak{F}_{i}$  consists of all monotone Boolean formulae with input length i, is defined as follows. For  $x \in \bar{\mathfrak{X}}_{\kappa}$  and  $y = ((y_{1}, \ldots, y_{n}), f) \in \bar{\mathfrak{Y}}_{\kappa}$  where  $f: \{0,1\}^{n} \to \{0,1\}$ , we define

$$\mathsf{KBF1}[\mathsf{P}_{\kappa}](x,y) = f\big(\,\mathsf{P}_{\kappa}(x,y_1),\ldots,\mathsf{P}_{\kappa}(x,y_n)\,\big).$$

We use  $\mathsf{KBF1}_{\mathsf{OR}}[\mathsf{P}_\kappa]$  (resp.  $\mathsf{KBF1}_{\mathsf{AND}}[\mathsf{P}_\kappa]$ ) to denote a predicate family that is the same as  $\mathsf{KBF1}[\mathsf{P}_\kappa]$  except that  $\mathcal{F}_i$  in  $\bar{\mathcal{Y}}_\kappa$  consists of monotone Boolean formulae whose all gates are OR (resp. AND) gates. The "1" in  $\mathsf{KBF1}$  refers to the property that the augmentation is over *one* predicate family. An augmentation over a *set* of predicate families follows analogously to [9], and we defer to §6 (and §6.2). In *dynamic* compositions, f can be chosen freely (as opposed to static ones, where f is fixed). Unbounded compositions mean n is unbounded.

**PES** for KBF1[P<sub> $\kappa$ </sub>]. Let  $\Gamma = (\mathsf{Param}, \mathsf{EncCt}, \mathsf{EncKey}, \mathsf{Pair})$  be a PES for P<sub> $\kappa$ </sub>. We construct a PES for KBF1[P<sub> $\kappa$ </sub>], denoted by KBF1-Trans( $\Gamma$ ) as follows. Let Share<sub>p</sub> be the linear secret sharing algorithm on polynomials defined in Fig 4.

#### $\mathsf{Share}_{\mathsf{p}}(f,\alpha,\mathbf{u})$

Input: A monotone Boolean formula f = (n, w, m, G) with  $\tau$  AND gates, a variable  $\alpha$ , and  $\tau$  variables  $\mathbf{u} = (u_1, \dots, u_{\tau})$ .

- 1. Set a variable  $\sigma_{\sf out} = \alpha$  on the output wire.
- 2. Let  $\phi : [m] \to [\tau]$  be a function such that  $\phi(i) = |\{j \mid j \leq i \land G_1(j) = \text{AND}\}|$ , where  $G_1(j)$  denotes the first element of G(j). For each AND gate g with incoming wires a, b and an outgoing wire c where a polynomial  $\sigma_c$  is set on c, set new polynomials  $\sigma_a = \sigma_c u_{\phi(g)}$  and  $\sigma_b = u_{\phi(g)}$  on a and b, respectively.
- 3. For each OR gate g with incoming wires a, b and an outgoing wire c where a vector  $\sigma_c$  is set on c, set new polynomials  $\sigma_a = \sigma_c$ ,  $\sigma_b = \sigma_c$  on a, b, respectively.
- 4. Output polynomials  $\sigma_1, \ldots, \sigma_n$ , which are set on the input wires  $1, \ldots, n$ .

<span id="page-24-0"></span>Fig 4. Linear secret sharing scheme for Boolean formulae on polynomials.

- Param'(par) = Param(par) and EncCt'(x) = EncCt(x)
- EncKey' $((y_1,\ldots,y_n),f) \rightarrow (m'_1,m'_2,\mathbf{k}'(\mathbf{r}',\hat{\mathbf{r}}',\mathbf{w}))$ :
  - For  $i \in [n]$ , run  $\mathsf{EncKey}(y_i)$  to obtain n sets of polynomials  $\mathbf{k}^{(1)}, \dots, \mathbf{k}^{(n)}$ , where  $\mathbf{k}^{(i)} = \mathbf{k}(\mathbf{r}^{(i)}, \hat{\mathbf{r}}^{(i)}, \mathbf{w})$ .
  - Let  $\tau$  be a number of AND gates in f. Let  $\alpha_{\mathsf{new}}$  be a new special lone variable and  $\mathbf{u} = (u_1, \dots, u_\tau)$  be new lone variables. Let  $\sigma_1, \dots, \sigma_n$  be polynomials that are an output of  $\mathsf{Share}_{\mathsf{p}}(f, \alpha_{\mathsf{new}}, \mathbf{u})$ . A new set of polynomials  $\mathbf{k}'^{(i)}$  is defined the same as  $\mathbf{k}^{(i)}$  except that the variable  $\alpha^{(i)}$  in each polynomial is replaced with  $\sigma_i$ .
  - Define  $m_1' = nm_1$ ,  $m_2' = \tau + nm_2$ , and  $\mathbf{k}'(\mathbf{r}', \hat{\mathbf{r}}', \mathbf{w}) = (\mathbf{k}'^{(1)}, \dots, \mathbf{k}'^{(n)})$ . Note that  $\mathbf{r}' = (\mathbf{r}^{(1)}, \dots, \mathbf{r}^{(n)})$  and  $\hat{\mathbf{r}}' = (\alpha_{\mathsf{new}}, \mathbf{u}, \hat{\mathbf{r}}_{-\alpha^{(1)}}^{(1)}, \dots, \hat{\mathbf{r}}_{-\alpha^{(n)}}^{(n)})$ .
- $\mathsf{Pair}'(x,y) \to (\mathbf{E}',\overline{\mathbf{E}}')$  and correctness:
  - Let polynomials  $\sigma_1, \ldots, \sigma_n$  be an output of  $\mathsf{Share}_\mathsf{p}(f, \alpha_\mathsf{new}, \mathbf{u})$ . It is not hard to see that, for all  $b = (b_1, \ldots, b_n) \in \{0, 1\}^n$  such that f(b) = 1, there exists a set  $S \subseteq \{i \mid b_i = 1\}$  such that  $\sum_{i \in S} \sigma_i = \alpha_\mathsf{new}$ . Thus, if x and  $y = ((y_1, \ldots, y_n), f)$  satisfy  $\mathsf{KBF1}[\mathsf{P}_\kappa](x, y) = 1$ , there exists  $S \subseteq \{i \mid \mathsf{P}_\kappa(x, y_i) = 1\}$  such that  $\sum_{i \in S} \sigma_i = \alpha_\mathsf{new}$ .
  - For  $i \in S$ , run  $\mathsf{Pair}(x, y_i) \to (\mathbf{E}^{(i)}, \overline{\mathbf{E}^{(i)}})$ , satisfying  $\mathbf{s} \mathbf{E}^{(i)} \mathbf{k}^{(i)^{\top}} + \mathbf{c} \overline{\mathbf{E}}^{(i)} \mathbf{r}^{(i)^{\top}} = \sigma_i s_0$ . Then, we can obtain  $\sum_{i \in S} \sigma_i s_0 = \alpha_{\mathsf{new}} s_0$  by the linear combination.

<span id="page-24-1"></span>**Theorem 7** (( $\zeta, \ell$ )-KE-ind of KBF1-Trans( $\Gamma$ )). Let B be the maximum depth of f chosen by A in the ( $\zeta, \ell$ )-KE-ind game for KBF1-Trans( $\Gamma$ ). If  $\Gamma$  satisfies ( $\zeta, \ell$ )-KE-ind, then KBF1-Trans( $\Gamma$ ) satisfies ( $\zeta, \ell$ )-KE-ind as long as  $B = O(\log \lambda)$ . That is, for all PPT adversaries A, there exists a PPT adversary B such that

$$\mathsf{Adv}_{\mathcal{A},\mathsf{KBF1-Trans}(\varGamma)}^{(\zeta,\ell)\text{-KE-ind}}(\lambda) \leq 2^{9B+1}\mathsf{Adv}_{\mathcal{B},\varGamma}^{(\zeta,\ell)\text{-KE-ind}}(\lambda).$$

We prove Theorem 7 by extending the techniques regarding pebbling arguments that Kowalczyk-Wee [29] have introduced in proving adaptive security of their ABE schemes for formulae with multiuse.

*Proof.* We utilize the piecewise guessing framework (Section 2.3) by Kowalczyk and Wee [29] to prove Theorem 7. However, they use a secret sharing scheme that puts shares on all nodes of Boolean formula, whereas our transformation puts shares on only input nodes Fig 4 and 5. Very recently, Tomida et al. presented an improved technique that allows us to use the piecewise guessing framework with shares on only input nodes [38]. Hence, we proceed the proof following their improved strategy.

<span id="page-24-2"></span>Let  $\mathsf{G}_0^{(\zeta,\ell)\text{-}\mathsf{KE}\text{-}\mathsf{ind}}$  and  $\mathsf{G}_1^{(\zeta,\ell)\text{-}\mathsf{KE}\text{-}\mathsf{ind}}$  be the  $(\zeta,\ell)\text{-}\mathsf{KE}\text{-}\mathsf{ind}$  games for  $\mathsf{KBF1\text{-}Trans}(\varGamma)$ . First, we define a linear secret sharing algorithm Share on vectors as shown in Fig 5. Then, we have Lemma 10 for the secret sharing scheme.

#### $Share(f, \mathbf{z})$

Input: A monotone Boolean formula f = (n, w, m, G) and a secret  $\mathbf{z} \in \mathbb{Z}_p^{\gamma}$ , where  $\gamma$  is arbitrary natural number.

- 1. Set a vector  $\sigma_{\text{out}} = \mathbf{z}$  on the output wire.
- 2. For each AND gate g with incoming wires a, b and an outgoing wire c where a vector  $\sigma_c$  is set on c, choose  $\mathbf{u}_g \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{\gamma}$  and set  $\sigma_a = \sigma_c \mathbf{u}_g$  and  $\sigma_b = \mathbf{u}_g$  on a and b, respectively.
- 3. For each OR gate g with incoming wires a, b and an outgoing wire c where a vector  $\sigma_c$  is set on c, set  $\sigma_a = \sigma_c$  and  $\sigma_b = \sigma_c$  on a and b, respectively.
- 4. Output shares  $\sigma_1, \ldots, \sigma_n$ , which are set on the input wires  $1, \ldots, n$ .

<span id="page-25-0"></span>Fig 5. Linear secret sharing scheme for Boolean formulae.

**Lemma 10.** For all  $\gamma, n \in \mathbb{N}$ , monotone Boolean formulae f = (n, w, m, G),  $\mathbf{h}, \mathbf{a} \in \mathbb{Z}_p^{\gamma}$ , and  $\mu \in \mathbb{Z}_p$ , we define the following distribution.

$$\mathbf{h}_1, \dots, \mathbf{h}_n \leftarrow \mathsf{Share}(f, \mathbf{h} + \mu \mathbf{a}), \ \mathbf{h}_1', \dots, \mathbf{h}_n' \leftarrow \mathsf{Share}(f, \mathbf{h}), \\ \mu_1, \dots, \mu_n \leftarrow \mathsf{Share}(f, \mu).$$

Then, the two distributions are identical:

$$\{\mathbf{h}_1, \dots, \mathbf{h}_n\}$$
 and  $\{\mathbf{h}'_1 + \mu_1 \mathbf{a}, \dots, \mathbf{h}'_n + \mu_n \mathbf{a}\}.$ 

*Proof.* Let  $\mathbf{z}_i$  for  $i \in [w]$  be values set on a wire i in the execution of  $\mathsf{Share}(f, \mathbf{z})$ . From the procedure of the scheme, we have  $\mathbf{z}_i = b_\mathsf{out}\mathbf{z} + \sum_{g \in S} b_g\mathbf{u}_g$  for some subset S of all gates in f,  $b_\mathsf{out} \in \{0, 1\}$ , and  $b_g \in \{-1, 1\}$ . Note that S,  $b_\mathsf{out}$ ,  $b_g$  are determined by f and i.

Let  $\mathbf{h}_i$ ,  $\mathbf{h}'_i$ , and  $\mu_i$  for  $i \in [w]$  be values set on wire i in the execution of  $\mathsf{Share}(f, \mathbf{h} + \mu \mathbf{a})$ ,  $\mathsf{Share}(f, \mathbf{h})$ , and  $\mathsf{Share}(f, \mu)$ , respectively. Then, we have

$$\mathbf{h}_i = b_{\mathsf{out}}(\mathbf{h} + \mu \mathbf{a}) + \sum_{g \in S} b_g \mathbf{u}_g, \quad \mathbf{h}_i' = b_{\mathsf{out}} \mathbf{h} + \sum_{g \in S} b_g \mathbf{u}_g', \quad \mu_i = b_{\mathsf{out}} \mu + \sum_{g \in S} b_g u_g,$$

for some randomly chosen  $\mathbf{u}_g$ ,  $\mathbf{u}_g'$ , and  $u_g$ . Defining  $\mathbf{u}_g = \mathbf{u}_g' + u_g \mathbf{a}$  does not change the joint distribution of all  $\mathbf{u}_g$ . In this case, we have  $\mathbf{h}_i = \mathbf{h}_i' + \mu_i \mathbf{a}$  for  $i \in [w]$ . This concludes the proof.

We can describe  $\mathsf{G}_{\beta}^{(\zeta,\ell)\text{-KE-ind}}$  for  $\beta \in \{0,1\}$  using the secret sharing algorithm Share as shown in Fig 6. By applying Lemma 10,  $\mathbf{h}_i$  in  $\mathcal{O}_{\bar{y}}$  can be replaced with  $\mathbf{h}_i' + \mu_i \mathbf{a}_1^*$  where  $\mathbf{h}_1', \dots, \mathbf{h}_n' \leftarrow \mathsf{Share}(f, \mathbf{h})$  and  $\mu_1, \dots, \mu_n \leftarrow \mathsf{Share}(f, \beta \mu)$ . In what follows, we use the latter definition for  $\mathcal{O}_{\bar{y}}$ .

Following the piecewise guessing framework, we define a series of selective hybrids  $\widehat{\mathsf{H}}^{h_0}$  to  $\widehat{\mathsf{H}}^{h_L}$ , where  $L=8^B$ , and two intermediate games  $\mathsf{G}_{\mathsf{M}0}^{(\zeta,\ell)\text{-KE-ind}}$  and  $\mathsf{G}_{\mathsf{M}1}^{(\zeta,\ell)\text{-KE-ind}}$ , which satisfy

$$\begin{array}{l} - \ \widehat{\mathsf{G}}_{0}^{(\zeta,\ell)\text{-KE-ind}} = \widehat{\mathsf{H}}^{h_0} \approx_c, \dots, \approx_c \widehat{\mathsf{H}}^{h_L} = \widehat{\mathsf{G}}_{\mathsf{M}0}^{(\zeta,\ell)\text{-KE-ind}} \\ - \ \mathsf{G}_{\mathsf{M}0}^{(\zeta,\ell)\text{-KE-ind}} = \mathsf{G}_{\mathsf{M}1}^{(\zeta,\ell)\text{-KE-ind}}. \end{array}$$

The function  $h_{\iota}$  for  $\iota \in [L]$  is defined as follows. Let  $z = (x, y) \in \{0, 1\}^R$  on which  $\mathcal{A}$  queries  $\mathcal{O}_{\bar{\mathcal{X}}}$  and  $\mathcal{O}_{\bar{\mathcal{Y}}}$  respectively. Let  $b \in \{0, 1\}^n$  be a string computed from z following Definition 14. Note that f(b) = 0 because the game imposes the condition  $\mathsf{KBF1}[\mathsf{P}_{\kappa}](x, y) = 0$  on  $\mathcal{A}$ . Let  $\mathcal{R} = (r_1, \ldots, r_L) = \mathsf{PebRec}(f, b)$  be a pebbling record generated as shown in Lemma 2. Then, we define  $h_{\iota} : \{0, 1\}^R \to \{0, 1\}^{3B}$  as  $h_{\iota}(z) = r_{\iota}$ . Note that  $h_0$  and  $h_L$  are constant functions because they specify the pebbling configurations where no pebbles on it and a pebble is placed on only the output gate, respectively.

The hybrids and intermediate games only differ in the part  $\mathsf{Share}(f,\beta\mu)$  in  $\mathcal{O}_{\bar{y}}$  from  $\mathsf{G}_{\beta}^{(\zeta,\ell)\mathsf{-KE-ind}}$ . That is,  $\widehat{\mathsf{H}}^{h_\iota}$  is the same as  $\widehat{\mathsf{G}}_0^{(\zeta,\ell)\mathsf{-KE-ind}}$  except that  $\mathsf{Share}(f,0)$  is replaced with  $\widehat{\mathsf{Share}}(f,0,h_\iota(z))$ . The description of algorithm  $\widehat{\mathsf{Share}}$  is presented in Fig 7.  $\mathsf{G}_{\mathsf{M0}}^{(\zeta,\ell)\mathsf{-KE-ind}}$  is the same as  $\mathsf{H}^{h_L}$ , and  $\mathsf{G}_{\mathsf{M1}}^{(\zeta,\ell)\mathsf{-KE-ind}}$  is

```
\overline{\omega \leftarrow \mathsf{Param}}(\mathsf{par}), \ \mathbb{G} \leftarrow \mathfrak{G}_{\mathsf{BG}}(1^{\lambda})

\overline{\mathbf{A}}, \overline{\mathbf{B}} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{(k+\zeta) \times (k+\zeta)}, \quad \mathbb{W} = (\mathbf{W}_1, \dots, \mathbf{W}_{\omega}) \leftarrow (\mathbb{Z}_p^{(k+\zeta) \times (k+\zeta)})^{\omega} 

P = (\mathbb{G}, [\mathbf{A}]_{\eta}, [\mathbf{B}]_{3-\eta}, \{\mathbf{a}_i^*\}_{i \in [\ell,\zeta]}, \{\mathbf{b}_i^*\}_{i \in [\ell+1,\zeta]}, \{[\mathbf{W}_i^{\mathsf{T}} \mathbf{A}]_{\eta}, [\mathbf{W}_i \mathbf{B}]_{3-\eta}\}_{i \in [\omega]})

\mathcal{O}_{\bar{\chi}}(\cdot)
 \overline{\text{Input}} \colon x \in \bar{\mathfrak{X}}_{\kappa}
(n_1, n_2, \mathbf{c}(\mathbf{s}, \hat{\mathbf{s}}, \mathbf{w})) \leftarrow \mathsf{EncCt}(x)
\mathbf{c}_0 \leftarrow \mathsf{span}(\mathbf{A}, \mathbf{a}_1, \dots, \mathbf{a}_\ell), \ \ \mathbf{s}_1, \dots, \mathbf{s}_{n_1} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^k, \ \ \hat{\mathbf{s}}_1, \dots, \hat{\mathbf{s}}_{n_2} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{k+\zeta}
\mathbf{S} = (\mathbf{c}_0, \mathbf{A}\mathbf{s}_1, \dots, \mathbf{A}\mathbf{s}_{n_1}), \ \mathbf{\hat{S}} = (\hat{\mathbf{s}}_1, \dots, \hat{\mathbf{s}}_{n_2})
Output: ([\mathbf{S}]_{\eta}, [\mathbf{c}(\mathbf{S}, \widehat{\mathbf{S}}, \mathbb{W})]_{\eta})
O_{\bar{y}}(\cdot,\cdot)
 Input: y = ((y_1, \dots, y_n), f) \in \bar{\mathcal{Y}}_{\kappa} and \mathbf{h} \in \mathbb{Z}_p^{k+\zeta}
 (m_1, m_2, \mathbf{k}(\mathbf{r}^{(i)}, \hat{\mathbf{r}}^{(i)}, \mathbf{w})) \leftarrow \mathsf{EncKey}(y_i)
\mu \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p, \quad \mathbf{r}_1^{(i)}, \dots, \mathbf{r}_{m_1}^{(i)} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^k, \quad \hat{\mathbf{r}}_1^{(i)}, \dots, \hat{\mathbf{r}}_{m_2}^{(i)} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{k+\zeta}
\mathbf{h}_1, \dots, \mathbf{h}_n \leftarrow \mathsf{Share}(f, \mathbf{h} + \mid \beta \mu \mathbf{a}_{\ell}^* \mid)
                              \mathbf{h}_1', \dots, \mathbf{h}_n' \leftarrow \mathsf{Share}(f, \mathbf{h}),
                          \mu_1, \dots, \mu_n \leftarrow \mathsf{Share}(f, \beta \mu)
\mathbf{R}^{(i)} = (\mathbf{Br}_1^{(i)}, \dots, \mathbf{Br}_{m_1}^{(i)}), \ \ \widehat{\mathbf{R}}^{(i)} = (\mathbf{h}_i, \hat{\mathbf{r}}_1^{(i)}, \dots, \hat{\mathbf{r}}_{m_2}^{(i)})
Output: \{([\mathbf{R}^{(i)}]_{3-\eta}, [\mathbf{k}(\mathbf{R}^{(i)}, \widehat{\mathbf{R}}^{(i)}, \mathbb{W})]_{3-\eta})\}_{i \in [n]}
```

<span id="page-26-0"></span>**Fig 6.**  $(\zeta, \ell)$ -KE-ind game for KBF1-Trans $(\Gamma)$ .

#### $\mathsf{Share}(f,\mathbf{z},u)$

Input: A monotone Boolean formula f = (n, w, m, G) with depth  $d \leq B$ ,  $\mathbf{z} \in \mathbb{Z}_p^{\gamma}$ , and  $u \in \{0, 1\}^{3B}$ .

- 1. Set a vector  $\sigma_{out} = \mathbf{z}$  on the output wire.
- 2. Interpret u as a pebbling configuration on f.
- 3. For each gate g with a pebble that has incoming wires a, b and an outgoing wire c where a vector  $\sigma_c$  is set on c, choose  $\mathbf{u}_{g,1}, \mathbf{u}_{g,2} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{\gamma}$  and set  $\sigma_a = \mathbf{u}_{g,1}$  and  $\sigma_b = \mathbf{u}_{g,2}$  on a and b, respectively.
- 4. For each AND gate g with no pebble that has incoming wires a, b and an outgoing wire c where a vector  $\boldsymbol{\sigma}_c$  is set on c, choose  $\mathbf{u}_g \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{\gamma}$  and set  $\boldsymbol{\sigma}_a = \boldsymbol{\sigma}_c \mathbf{u}_g$  and  $\boldsymbol{\sigma}_b = \mathbf{u}_g$  on a and b, respectively.
- 5. For each OR gate g with no pebble that has incoming wires a, b and an outgoing wire c where a vector  $\sigma_c$  is set on c, set  $\sigma_a = \sigma_c$  and  $\sigma_b = \sigma_c$  on a and b, respectively.
- 6. For each input wire i with a pebble, replace  $\sigma_i$  with a random vector  $\mathbf{u}_i \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_n^k$ , i.e.,  $\sigma_i = \mathbf{u}_i$ .
- 7. Output shares  $\sigma_1, \ldots, \sigma_n$ , which are set on the input wires  $1, \ldots, n$ .

<span id="page-26-1"></span>Fig 7. Description of Share

the same as  $\mathsf{G}_{\mathsf{M}0}^{(\zeta,\ell)\text{-KE-ind}}$  except that  $\mathsf{Share}(f,0,h_L(z))$  is replaced with  $\mathsf{Share}(f,\mu,h_L(z))$ . The behaviors of  $\mathfrak{O}_{\bar{\mathbb{Y}}}$  in these hybrids are summarized in Fig 8.

We prove that

$$\begin{split} & - \ \mathsf{G}_0^{(\zeta,\ell)\text{-KE-ind}} \approx_c \mathsf{G}_{\mathsf{M}0}^{(\zeta,\ell)\text{-KE-ind}}, \\ & - \ \mathsf{G}_{\mathsf{M}0}^{(\zeta,\ell)\text{-KE-ind}} = \mathsf{G}_{\mathsf{M}1}^{(\zeta,\ell)\text{-KE-ind}}, \\ & - \ \mathsf{G}_{\mathsf{M}1}^{(\zeta,\ell)\text{-KE-ind}} \approx_c \mathsf{G}_1^{(\zeta,\ell)\text{-KE-ind}}. \end{split}$$

First, we prove item 2, then prove item 1. We omit the proof of item 3 because it is almost the same as that of item 1. Then, we are done.

```
 \mathsf{G} \in \left\{ \mathsf{G}_0^{(\zeta,\ell)\text{-KE-ind}}, \boxed{\widehat{\mathbf{H}}^{h_\iota}}, \boxed{\mathsf{G}_{\mathsf{M}0}^{(\zeta,\ell)\text{-KE-ind}}}, \boxed{\mathsf{G}_{\mathsf{M}1}^{(\zeta,\ell)\text{-KE-ind}}} \right\}   \underbrace{\begin{array}{l} \underbrace{\mathbb{O}_{\bar{y}}(\cdot,\cdot)}{\mathrm{Input:}} \ y = ((y_1,\ldots,y_n),f) \in \bar{\mathbb{y}}_\kappa \ \text{and} \ \mathbf{h} \in \mathbb{Z}_p^{k+\zeta} \\ (m_1,m_2,\mathbf{k}(\mathbf{r}^{(i)},\hat{\mathbf{r}}^{(i)},\mathbf{w})) \leftarrow \mathrm{EncKey}(y_i) \\ \mu \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p, \ \mathbf{r}_1^{(i)},\ldots,\mathbf{r}_{m_1}^{(i)} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^k, \ \hat{\mathbf{r}}_1^{(i)},\ldots,\hat{\mathbf{r}}_{m_2}^{(i)} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{k+\zeta}, \ \mathbf{h}_1',\ldots,\mathbf{h}_n' \leftarrow \mathrm{Share}(f,\mathbf{h}) \\ \mu_1,\ldots,\mu_n \leftarrow \mathrm{Share}(f,0), \ \mu_1,\ldots,\mu_n \leftarrow \widehat{\mathrm{Share}}(f,0,h_\iota(z)) \\ \hline \mu_1,\ldots,\mu_n \leftarrow \widehat{\mathrm{Share}}(f,0,h_L(z)), \ \mu_1,\ldots,\mu_n \leftarrow \widehat{\mathrm{Share}}(f,\mu,h_L(z)) \\ \hline \mathbf{h}_i = \mathbf{h}_i' + \mu_i \mathbf{a}_\ell^* \\ \mathbf{R}^{(i)} = (\mathbf{B}\mathbf{r}_1^{(i)},\ldots,\mathbf{B}\mathbf{r}_{m_1}^{(i)}), \ \widehat{\mathbf{R}}^{(i)} = (\mathbf{h}_i,\hat{\mathbf{r}}_1^{(i)},\ldots,\hat{\mathbf{r}}_{m_2}^{(i)}) \\ \mathrm{Output:} \ \{([\mathbf{R}^{(i)}]_{3-\eta},[\mathbf{k}(\mathbf{R}^{(i)},\hat{\mathbf{R}}^{(i)},\mathbb{W})]_{3-\eta})\}_{i \in [n]} \\ \hline \end{array}
```

<span id="page-27-0"></span>**Fig 8.** Description of  $\mathcal{O}_{\bar{y}}$  in hybrids.

 $G_{M0}^{(\zeta,\ell)\text{-KE-ind}} = G_{M1}^{(\zeta,\ell)\text{-KE-ind}}$ . Recall that the difference between the two games lies in the input of Share, namely,  $(f,0,h_L(z))$  or  $(f,\mu,h_L(z))$ . First, we note that  $u=h_L(z)$  is a constant that specifies the pebbling configuration on f where a pebble is placed on only the output gate. In this case, it is not difficult to see that the output of Share is independent of the second argument of the input. This is because the values set on the two incoming wires of the output gate are chosen independently of  $\sigma_{\text{out}}$  when a pebble is placed on the output gate (see item 3 in Fig 7). Then, the values to be set on the rest of wires are computed based on these values set on the incoming wires of the output gate. Thus, the output of Share is identically distributed in both games, and the claim holds.

 $\underline{\mathsf{G}_0^{(\zeta,\ell)\text{-}\mathsf{KE}\text{-}\mathsf{ind}}} \approx_c \underline{\mathsf{G}_{\mathsf{M}0}^{(\zeta,\ell)\text{-}\mathsf{KE}\text{-}\mathsf{ind}}}. \quad \text{Following Lemma 1, we prove the two properties:}$ 

```
 \begin{array}{l} 1. \ \mathsf{G}_0^{(\zeta,\ell)\text{-KE-ind}} = \mathsf{H}^{h_0} \ \mathrm{and} \ \mathsf{H}^{h_L} = \mathsf{G}_{\mathsf{M}0}^{(\zeta,\ell)\text{-KE-ind}}, \\ 2. \ \widehat{\mathsf{H}}_1^{h_{\iota-1}} \approx_c \widehat{\mathsf{H}}_0^{h_{\iota}} \ \mathrm{for} \ \iota \in [L]. \end{array}
```

where  $\widehat{\mathsf{H}}_{\beta}^{h_i}$  for  $\beta \in \{0,1\}$  is defined in Section 2.3. For item 1, the latter holds because we defined  $\mathsf{G}_{\mathsf{M}0}^{(\zeta,\ell)\text{-KE-ind}}$  in such a way. To show the former, we need to confirm that the output of  $\mathsf{Share}(f,0)$  and  $\mathsf{Share}(f,0,h_0(z))$  is identically distributed. Recall that  $h_0$  is a constant function that specifies the pebbling configuration where no pebbles on it. In this case, no gates correspond to item 3 or 6 in Fig 7, and the remaining procedures are exactly the same as  $\mathsf{Share}(f,0)$ . Thus, the former also holds.

The remaining thing is to prove  $\widehat{\mathsf{H}}_1^{h_{\iota-1}} \approx_c \widehat{\mathsf{H}}_0^{h_{\iota}}$ . Formally, we prove Lemma 11, which allows us to conclude the proof of Theorem 7 from the observation so far and Lemma 1.

<span id="page-27-1"></span>**Lemma 11.** For all PPT adversaries A, there exists a PPT adversary B such that

$$|\Pr[\langle \mathcal{A}, \widehat{\mathsf{H}}_1^{h_{\iota-1}} \rangle = 1] - \Pr[\langle \mathcal{A}, \widehat{\mathsf{H}}_0^{h_{\iota}} \rangle = 1]| \leq \mathsf{Adv}_{\mathcal{B}, \varGamma}^{(\zeta, \ell)\text{-KE-ind}}(\lambda).$$

Proof. We denote the pebbling configuration on f that is specified by a bit string u by C(f,u). Let  $u_0$  and  $u_1$  be the committed values by  $\mathcal{A}$ , which correspond to  $h_{\iota-1}(z)$  and  $h_{\iota}(z)$  for z chosen by  $\mathcal{A}$ . Then,  $C(f,u_0)$  and  $C(f,u_1)$  are adjacent pebbling configurations for some input  $b \in \{0,1\}^n$  for f. In other words, there exists b such that  $u_0$  and  $u_1$  correspond to  $r_{\iota-1}$  and  $r_{\iota}$  where  $(r_0,\ldots,r_L) = \mathsf{PebRec}(f,b)$ . Thus,  $C(f,u_0)$  can be changed to  $C(f,u_1)$  in one step following the rule defined in Definition 6. Recall that the difference between  $\widehat{\mathsf{H}}_1^{h_{\iota-1}}$  and  $\widehat{\mathsf{H}}_0^{h_{\iota}}$  is the input of  $\widehat{\mathsf{Share}}$ . That is, the input is  $(f,0,u_0)$  in  $\widehat{\mathsf{H}}_1^{h_{\iota-1}}$  and  $(f,0,u_1)$  in  $\widehat{\mathsf{H}}_0^{h_{\iota}}$ . Thus, in case of  $u_0=u_1$ ,  $\widehat{\mathsf{H}}_1^{h_{\iota-1}}$  and  $\widehat{\mathsf{H}}_0^{h_{\iota}}$  are clearly identical. In the following, we consider the case of  $u_0 \neq u_1$ .

Let an object O be either a gate  $g^*$  with incoming wires a, b and an outgoing c or an input wire  $i^*$  in which the difference between  $C(f, u_0)$  and  $C(f, u_1)$  lies. In what follows, we only consider the case

where a pebble is placed on O when we move from  $C(f,u_0)$  to  $C(f,u_1)$ . Note that we can similarly analyze the opposite case, where a pebble is removed, by just considering the reverse of the former case. When O is a gate  $g^*$ ,  $\widehat{\mathsf{Share}}(f,0,u_0)$  and  $\widehat{\mathsf{Share}}(f,0,u_1)$  are identically distributed, and thus  $\widehat{\mathsf{H}}_1^{h_{\iota-1}}$  and  $\widehat{\mathsf{H}}_0^{h_{\iota}}$  are identical. We explain the reason in the following.

Consider the case where  $g^*$  is an AND gate with incoming wires a,b and an outgoing wire c, and at least one of its incoming wires comes from a gate or input wire with a pebble, say O'. This follows from the pebbling rule. Without loss of generality, we can assume that the wire a comes from O'. The difference between  $\mathsf{Share}(f,0,u_0)$  and  $\mathsf{Share}(f,0,u_1)$  is whether  $\sigma_a = \sigma_c - \sigma_b$  or  $\sigma_a = u$  where  $u \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p$  is set on the wire a. The crucial fact is that the procedure for O' is independent of  $\sigma_a$ . That is, if O' is a gate g' with a pebble, the values set to its incoming wires are independent of  $\sigma_a$  (see item 3 in Fig 7). If O' is an input wire i' with a pebble, the value set to the input wire is independent of  $\sigma_a$  (see item 6 in Fig 7). Thus, the outputs of  $\mathsf{Share}(f,0,u_0)$  and  $\mathsf{Share}(f,0,u_1)$  are identically distributed. We can easily observe that similar argument holds if  $g^*$  is an OR gate.

The remaining case is when O is an input wire  $i^* \in [n]$ . In this case, we show that the outputs of  $\mathcal{O}_{\bar{\mathbb{y}}}$  in  $\widehat{\mathsf{H}}_1^{h_{\iota-1}}$  and  $\widehat{\mathsf{H}}_0^{h_{\iota}}$  are computationally indistinguishable if the PES  $\Gamma$  for  $\mathsf{P}_{\kappa}$  satisfies  $(\zeta,\ell)$ -KE-ind. The difference between these games is that  $\mu_{i^*}$  is exactly one of the output of  $\widehat{\mathsf{Share}}(f,0,u_0)$  in  $\widehat{\mathsf{H}}_1^{h_{\iota-1}}$ , whereas  $\mu_{i^*}$  is a random elements in  $\mathbb{Z}_p$  in  $\widehat{\mathsf{H}}_0^{h_{\iota}}$ . This is because a pebble is not placed on  $i^*$  in the configuration  $C(f,u_0)$  but is placed on  $i^*$  in the configuration  $C(f,u_1)$ . Thus, the output of  $\widehat{\mathsf{Share}}(f,0,u_1)$  is the same as that of  $\widehat{\mathsf{Share}}(f,0,u_0)$  except that  $\mu_{i^*}$  is replaced with a random element (see item 6 in Fig 7).

We construct a PPT adversary  $\mathcal{B}$  against  $(\zeta, \ell)$ -KE-ind of  $\Gamma$  that internally runs a PPT distinguisher  $\mathcal{A}$  between  $\widehat{\mathsf{H}}_1^{h_{\iota-1}}$  and  $\widehat{\mathsf{H}}_0^{h_{\iota}}$ .  $\mathcal{B}$  behaves as follows.

- 1.  $\mathcal{A}$  commits  $(u_0, u_1)$  to  $\mathcal{B}$ .
- 2.  $\mathcal{B}$  is given a parameter  $(\mathbb{G}, [\mathbf{A}]_{\eta}, [\mathbf{B}]_{3-\eta}, \{\mathbf{a}_{i}^{*}\}_{i \in [\ell,\zeta]}, \{\mathbf{b}_{i}^{*}\}_{i \in [\ell+1,\zeta]}, \{[\mathbf{W}_{i}^{\top}\mathbf{A}]_{\eta}, [\mathbf{W}_{i}\mathbf{B}]_{3-\eta}\}_{i \in [\omega]})$  from the  $(\zeta, \ell)$ -KE-ind game for  $\Gamma$  and gives it to  $\mathcal{A}$  as its input.
- 3. For  $\mathcal{A}$ 's query to  $\mathcal{O}_{\bar{\mathfrak{X}}}$ ,  $\mathcal{B}$  just relays the query to its own oracle  $\mathcal{O}_{\mathfrak{X}}$  and the reply to  $\mathcal{A}$ .
- 4. For  $\mathcal{A}$ 's query to  $\mathcal{O}_{\bar{\mathbb{y}}}$  on  $y = ((y_1, \dots, y_n), f)$  and  $\mathbf{h}$ ,  $\mathcal{B}$  computes  $\mu_1, \dots, \mu_n \leftarrow \widehat{\mathsf{Share}}(f, 0, u_0)$  and  $\mathbf{h}_i$  for all  $i \in [n]$  using  $\mathbf{a}^*_{\ell}$  as shown in Fig 8. Then,  $\mathcal{B}$  queries its own oracle  $\mathcal{O}_{\mathbb{y}}$  on  $y_{i^*}$  and  $\mathbf{h}_{i^*}$  and obtains  $[\mathbf{R}^{(i^*)}]_{3-\eta}$  and  $[\mathbf{k}(\mathbf{R}^{(i^*)}, \widehat{\mathbf{R}}^{(i^*)}, \mathbb{W})]_{3-\eta}$ .  $\mathcal{B}$  also computes all terms in  $\mathbf{R}^{(i)} = (\mathbf{Br}_1^{(i)}, \dots, \mathbf{Br}_{m_1}^{(i)})$  and  $\widehat{\mathbf{R}}^{(i)} = (\mathbf{h}_i, \widehat{\mathbf{r}}_1^{(i)}, \dots, \widehat{\mathbf{r}}_{m_2}^{(i)})$  for all  $i \in [n] \setminus i^*$  and  $\{[\mathbf{k}(\mathbf{R}^{(i)}, \widehat{\mathbf{R}}^{(i)}, \mathbb{W})]_{3-\eta}\}_{i \in [n] \setminus i^*}$  by itself.  $\mathcal{B}$  replies  $\{([\mathbf{R}^{(i)}]_{3-\eta}, [\mathbf{k}(\mathbf{R}^{(i)}, \widehat{\mathbf{R}}^{(i)}, \mathbb{W})]_{3-\eta}\}_{i \in [n]}$  to  $\mathcal{A}$ .
- 5.  $\mathcal{B}$  outputs  $\mathcal{A}$ 's output as it is.

Observe that if  $\beta = 0$  in the  $(\zeta, \ell)$ -KE-ind game of  $\Gamma$ , the first element of  $\widehat{\mathbf{R}}^{(i^*)}$  is  $\mathbf{h}_{i^*}$ , and thus  $\mathcal{A}$ 's view corresponds to  $\widehat{\mathbf{H}}_{1}^{h_{\iota-1}}$ . On the other hand, if  $\beta = 1$  in the  $(\zeta, \ell)$ -KE-ind game of  $\Gamma$ , the first element of  $\widehat{\mathbf{R}}^{(i^*)}$  is  $\mathbf{h}_{i^*} + \widehat{\mu} \mathbf{a}_{\ell}^* = \mathbf{h}'_{i^*} + \mu_{i^*} \mathbf{a}_{\ell}^* + \widehat{\mu} \mathbf{a}_{\ell}^*$ , where  $\widehat{\mu}$  is a random element in  $\mathbb{Z}_p$  chosen by  $\mathcal{O}_{\mathcal{Y}}$ . It means that  $\mu_{i^*}$  is randomized by  $\widehat{\mu}$ , and  $\mathcal{A}$ 's view corresponds to  $\widehat{\mathbf{H}}_0^{h_{\iota}}$ . This concludes the proof.

**Ciphertext-Policy Augmentation.** Analogously to [9], for a predicate family P, we define its CP augmentation predicate—denoted as CBF1[P]—as the dual of KBF1[P'] where P' is the dual of P. Therefore, we can use the dual conversion—applying two times—sandwiching KBF1-Trans, to obtain a PES conversion for CBF1[P].

**Definition 15 (Ciphertext-Policy Augmentation).** A predicate family for ciphertext-policy Boolean formula augmentation of a predicate family  $P_{\kappa}: \mathcal{X}_{\kappa} \times \mathcal{Y}_{\kappa} \to \{0,1\}$ , denoted by  $\mathsf{CBF1}[P_{\kappa}]: \bar{\mathcal{X}}_{\kappa} \times \bar{\mathcal{Y}}_{\kappa} \to \{0,1\}$ , is define as follows:

```
-\bar{\mathfrak{X}}_{\kappa} = \bigcup_{i \in \mathbb{N}} (\mathfrak{X}_{\kappa}^{i} \times \mathfrak{F}_{i}), where \mathfrak{F}_{i} consists of all monotone Boolean formulae with input length i. -\bar{\mathfrak{Y}}_{\kappa} = \mathfrak{Y}_{\kappa}.
```

- For  $x = ((x_1, \ldots, x_n), f) \in \bar{\mathcal{X}}_{\kappa}$  and  $y \in \bar{\mathcal{Y}}_{\kappa}$  where  $f : \{0, 1\}^n \to \{0, 1\}$ , we define  $b = (b_1, \ldots, b_n) \in \{0, 1\}^n$  as  $b_i = \mathsf{P}_{\kappa}(x_i, y)$ . Then,  $\mathsf{CBF1}[\mathsf{P}_{\kappa}](x, y) = 1 \Leftrightarrow f(b) = 1$ .

Additionally,  $\mathsf{CBF1}_{\mathsf{OR}}[\mathsf{P}_{\kappa}]$  and  $\mathsf{CBF1}_{\mathsf{AND}}[\mathsf{P}_{\kappa}]$  are defined in the same way as KP augmentation.

**PES for** CBF1[ $P_{\kappa}$ ]. Let  $\Gamma = (Param, EncCt, EncKey, Pair)$  be a PES for  $P_{\kappa}$ . It is not hard to see that CBF1[ $P_{\kappa}$ ] = Dual[KBF1[Dual[ $P_{\kappa}$ ]]]. Therefore, we can obtain a PES for CBF1[ $P_{\kappa}$ ], denoted by CBF1-Trans( $\Gamma$ ) = (Param', EncCt', EncKey', Pair'), from Dual-Trans and KBF1-Trans. That is,

$$\mathsf{CBF1\text{-}Trans}(\varGamma) = \mathsf{Dual\text{-}Trans}(\mathsf{KBF1\text{-}Trans}(\mathsf{Dual\text{-}Trans}(\varGamma))).$$

### <span id="page-29-0"></span>4.4 Conforming PES for ABE

We can apply our transformations, namely, direct sum, dual, and key-policy augmentation, to a predicate family set  $\mathcal{P}_{\kappa}$  multiple times to obtain a new predicate family  $\mathsf{P}_{\kappa}$ . When we apply a PES to construct an ABE scheme,  $(\zeta',\zeta')$ -KE-ind for some constant  $\zeta'$  implies the adaptive security of the resulting ABE scheme. The following theorem says that if we have predicate families  $\mathcal{P}_{\kappa} = (\mathsf{P}_{\kappa_1}^{(1)},\ldots,\mathsf{P}_{\kappa_d}^{(d)})$  that satisfy  $(\zeta,\ell)$ -KE-ind for all constants  $\ell,\zeta\in\mathbb{N}$ , we can construct an ABE scheme for a predicate family  $\mathsf{P}_{\kappa}$  obtained by applying the above transformations to  $\mathcal{P}_{\kappa}$  arbitrarily many times.

To state the theorem formally, we define a composed predicate set  $f_c(\mathcal{P}_{\kappa})$  for a predicate family set  $\mathcal{P}_{\kappa} = (\mathsf{P}_{\kappa_1}^{(1)}, \dots, \mathsf{P}_{\kappa_d}^{(d)})$ . Let  $\bar{\mathcal{P}}_{\kappa}$  be a predicate family set that consists of all predicate families obtained by applying one of transformations, (DS, Dual, KBF1), to  $\mathcal{P}_{\kappa}$ . That is,  $\bar{\mathcal{P}}_{\kappa} = (\mathsf{DS}[\mathcal{P}_{\kappa}], \{\mathsf{Dual}[\mathsf{P}_{\kappa_i}^{(i)}]\}_{i \in [d]}, \{\mathsf{KBF1}[\mathsf{P}_{\kappa_i}^{(i)}]\}_{i \in [d]})$  (we do not consider DS for a subset of  $\mathcal{P}_{\kappa}$ , because it can be embedded into  $\mathsf{DS}[\mathcal{P}_{\kappa}]$ ). Let f be a deterministic procedure defined as  $f(\mathcal{P}_{\kappa}) = \mathcal{P}_{\kappa} \cup \bar{\mathcal{P}}_{\kappa}$ . Denote  $f \circ \ldots \circ f(\mathcal{P}_{\kappa})$  where f appears c times by  $f_c(\mathcal{P}_{\kappa})$ . Then, we have the following theorem.

<span id="page-29-2"></span>**Theorem 8.** For all constant c and predicate family sets  $\mathfrak{P}_{\kappa} = (\mathsf{P}_{\kappa_1}^{(1)}, \ldots, \mathsf{P}_{\kappa_d}^{(d)})$ , each of whose elements has a corresponding PES with  $(\zeta, \ell)$ -KE-ind for all constants  $\zeta, \ell \in \mathbb{N}$ , there exists a constant  $\zeta'$  such that  $\mathsf{P}_{\kappa} \in f_c(\mathfrak{P}_{\kappa})$  has a PES that satisfies  $(\zeta', \zeta')$ -KE-ind under the  $\mathfrak{D}_k$ -MDDH assumption.

*Proof.* Let  $\Gamma = (\Gamma_1, \dots, \Gamma_d)$  be PESs for  $(\mathsf{P}_{\kappa_1}^{(1)}, \dots, \mathsf{P}_{\kappa_d}^{(d)})$ , respectively. We can construct a PES  $\Gamma$  for P by applying PES transformations in Sections 4.1 to 4.3 to  $\Gamma$  multiple times. Let  $\delta$  be the maximum number of Dual-Trans that is applied to each single PES  $\Gamma_i$  to obtain  $\Gamma$ . For instance,  $\delta$  in the following PES is 2 because the first  $\Gamma_2$  is transformed by Dual-Trans twice, and the others are transformed by Dual-Trans less that twice.

KBF1-Trans (DS-Trans (Dual-Trans (DS-Trans 
$$(\Gamma_1, Dual-Trans (\Gamma_2))), \Gamma_2, \Gamma_3)$$
).

Then, it is not hard to see that we can construct  $\Gamma$  with  $(\zeta', \zeta')$ -KE-ind for  $\zeta' = \delta + 1$ . This directly follows from Theorems 5 to 7.

Corollary 2. Let  $\mathfrak{P}_{\kappa} = (\mathsf{P}_{\kappa_1}^{(1)}, \dots, \mathsf{P}_{\kappa_d}^{(d)})$  be predicate families that have a PES with single-variable PMH. Then, we have a PES for  $\mathsf{P}_{\kappa} \in f_c(\mathfrak{P}_{\kappa})$  with  $(\zeta', \zeta')$ -KE-ind for a constant  $\zeta'$  under the  $\mathfrak{D}_k$ -MDDH assumption, where  $\zeta' - 1$  is the maximum number of Dual applied to each single predicate  $\mathsf{P}_{\kappa_i}^{(i)}$  to obtain  $\mathsf{P}_{\kappa}$ .

This corollary directly follows from Theorems 4 and 8.

## <span id="page-29-1"></span>5 ABE from PES

In this section, we present our ABE scheme. We can construct an ABE scheme for any predicate family  $P_{\kappa}$  and a corresponding PES obtained in our framework if the PES satisfies  $(\zeta, \zeta)$ -KE-ind for some constant  $\zeta \in \mathbb{N}$ .

**Construction.** Let  $\Gamma = (\mathsf{Param}, \mathsf{EncCt}, \mathsf{EncKey}, \mathsf{Pair})$  be a PES with  $(\zeta, \zeta)$ -KE-ind for a predicate family  $\mathsf{P}_\kappa : \mathcal{X}_\kappa \times \mathcal{Y}_\kappa \to \{0,1\}$ . Then, we can construct an ABE scheme for predicate  $\mathsf{P}_\kappa$  as follows.

Setup $(1^{\lambda}, \kappa)$ : Parse par from  $\kappa$ . It outputs pk and msk as follows.

$$\begin{split} & \omega \leftarrow \mathsf{Param}(\mathsf{par}), \ \ \mathbb{G} \leftarrow \mathcal{G}_{\mathsf{BG}}(1^{\lambda}), \ \ \overline{\mathbf{A}}, \overline{\mathbf{B}} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{(k+\zeta)\times(k+\zeta)}, \ \ \mathbf{h} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{k+\zeta}, \\ & \mathbb{W} = (\mathbf{W}_1, \dots, \mathbf{W}_{\omega}) \leftarrow (\mathbb{Z}_p^{(k+\zeta)\times(k+\zeta)})^{\omega}, \\ & \mathsf{pk} = (\mathbb{G}, [\mathbf{A}]_1, [\mathbf{W}_1^{\top} \mathbf{A}]_1, \dots, [\mathbf{W}_{\omega}^{\top} \mathbf{A}]_1, [\mathbf{A}^{\top} \mathbf{h}]_{\mathsf{T}}), \ \ \mathsf{msk} = (\mathbf{B}, \mathbf{h}, \mathbf{W}_1, \dots, \mathbf{W}_{\omega}). \end{split}$$

Enc(pk, x, M): It takes pk,  $x \in \mathcal{X}_{\kappa}$ , and  $M \in G_{\mathsf{T}}$  as inputs, and outputs  $\mathsf{ct}_x$  by computing as follows.

$$\begin{split} &(n_1,n_2,\mathbf{c}(\mathbf{s},\hat{\mathbf{s}},\mathbf{w})) \leftarrow \mathsf{EncCt}(x), \ \ \mathbf{s}_0,\mathbf{s}_1,\dots,\mathbf{s}_{n_1} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^k, \ \ \hat{\mathbf{s}}_1,\dots,\hat{\mathbf{s}}_{n_2} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{k+\zeta} \\ &\mathbf{S} = (\mathbf{A}\mathbf{s}_0,\mathbf{A}\mathbf{s}_1,\dots,\mathbf{A}\mathbf{s}_{n_1}), \ \ \hat{\mathbf{S}} = (\hat{\mathbf{s}}_1,\dots,\hat{\mathbf{s}}_{n_2}) \\ &\mathsf{ct}_x = (\mathsf{ct}_1,\mathsf{ct}_2,\mathsf{ct}_3) = ([\mathbf{S}]_1,[\mathbf{c}(\mathbf{S},\hat{\mathbf{S}},\mathbb{W})]_1,[\mathbf{s}_0^{\top}\mathbf{A}^{\top}\mathbf{h}]_{\mathsf{T}}M). \end{split}$$

KeyGen(pk, msk, y): It takes pk, msk, and  $y \in \mathcal{Y}_{\kappa}$  as inputs, and outputs  $\mathsf{sk}_y$  by computing as follows.

$$\begin{split} &(m_1,m_2,\mathbf{k}(\mathbf{r},\hat{\mathbf{r}},\mathbf{w})) \leftarrow \mathsf{EncKey}(y), \ \mathbf{r}_1,\dots,\mathbf{r}_{m_1} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^k, \ \hat{\mathbf{r}}_1,\dots,\hat{\mathbf{r}}_{m_2} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{k+\zeta} \\ &\mathbf{R} = (\mathbf{Br}_1,\dots,\mathbf{Br}_{m_1}), \ \hat{\mathbf{R}} = (\mathbf{h},\hat{\mathbf{r}}_1,\dots,\hat{\mathbf{r}}_{m_2}) \\ &\mathsf{sk}_y = (\mathsf{sk}_1,\mathsf{sk}_2) = ([\mathbf{R}]_2,[\mathbf{k}(\mathbf{R},\hat{\mathbf{R}},\mathbb{W})]_2). \end{split}$$

 $\mathsf{Dec}(\mathsf{pk},\mathsf{ct}_x,\mathsf{sk}_y)$ : It takes  $\mathsf{pk}$ ,  $\mathsf{ct}_x = (\mathsf{ct}_1,\mathsf{ct}_2,\mathsf{ct}_3)$ , and  $\mathsf{sk}_y = (\mathsf{sk}_1,\mathsf{sk}_2)$  such that  $\mathsf{P}_\kappa(x,y) = 1$ . Let  $(\mathbf{E},\overline{\mathbf{E}}) \leftarrow \mathsf{Pair}(x,y)$ . It outputs  $M' = \mathsf{ct}_3/\Omega$  where

$$\Omega = \prod_{\substack{i \in [n_1+1] \\ j \in [m_3]}} e(\mathsf{ct}_{1,i}, \mathsf{sk}_{2,j})^{e_{i,j}} \cdot \prod_{\substack{i \in [n_3] \\ j \in [m_1]}} e(\mathsf{ct}_{2,i}, \mathsf{sk}_{1,j})^{\bar{e}_{i,j}}, \tag{4}$$

and where  $\mathsf{ct}_{i,j}$  and  $\mathsf{sk}_{i,j}$  refer to the j-th element of  $\mathsf{ct}_i$  and  $\mathsf{sk}_i$ , respectively, and  $e_{i,j}$  and  $\bar{e}_{i,j}$  refer to the (i,j)-th element of  $\mathbf{E}$  and  $\overline{\mathbf{E}}$ , respectively.

Correctness. Let  $\mathbf{c} = (c_1, \dots, c_{n_3})$  and  $\mathbf{k} = (k_1, \dots, k_{m_3})$  be the outputs of  $\mathsf{EncCt}(x)$  and  $\mathsf{EncKey}(y)$ , respectively, where

$$\begin{split} c_i &= \sum_{z \in [n_2]} \theta_{i,z} \hat{s}_z + \sum_{t \in [n_1]^+, f \in [\omega]} \theta_{i,t,f} w_f s_t \\ k_j &= \phi_j \alpha + \sum_{u \in [m_2]} \phi_{j,u} \hat{r}_u + \sum_{v \in [m_1], z \in [\omega]} \phi_{j,v,z} w_z r_v. \end{split}$$

Then, we have

$$\begin{split} e(\mathsf{ct}_{1,i},\mathsf{sk}_{2,j})^{e_{i,j}} &= \left[ e_{i,j} \mathbf{s}_{i-1}^{\intercal} \mathbf{A}^{\intercal} \left( \phi_{j} \mathbf{h} + \sum_{u \in [m_{2}]} \phi_{j,u} \hat{\mathbf{r}}_{u} + \sum_{v \in [m_{1}],z \in [\omega]} \phi_{j,v,z} \mathbf{W}_{z} \mathbf{B} \mathbf{r}_{v} \right) \right]_{\mathsf{T}} \\ e(\mathsf{ct}_{2,i},\mathsf{sk}_{1,j})^{\bar{e}_{i,j}} &= \left[ \bar{e}_{i,j} \left( \sum_{z \in [n_{2}]} \theta_{i,z} \hat{\mathbf{s}}_{z}^{\intercal} + \sum_{t \in [n_{1}]^{+},f \in [\omega]} \theta_{i,t,f} \mathbf{s}_{t}^{\intercal} \mathbf{A}^{\intercal} \mathbf{W}_{f} \right) \mathbf{B} \mathbf{r}_{j} \right]_{\mathsf{T}}. \end{split}$$

From the correctness of the pair encoding scheme, we have

$$\sum_{\substack{i \in [n_1+1] \\ j \in [m_3]}} e_{i,j} s_{i-1} k_j + \sum_{\substack{i \in [n_3] \\ j \in [m_1]}} \bar{e}_{i,j} c_i r_j = \alpha s_0.$$

This corresponds to the following equation:

$$\prod_{\substack{i \in [n_1+1]\\j \in [m_3]}} e(\mathsf{ct}_{1,i},\mathsf{sk}_{2,j})^{e_{i,j}} \cdot \prod_{\substack{i \in [n_3]\\j \in [m_1]}} e(\mathsf{ct}_{2,i},\mathsf{sk}_{1,j})^{\bar{e}_{i,j}} = [\mathbf{s}_0^\top \mathbf{A}^\top \mathbf{h}]_\mathsf{T}.$$

<span id="page-30-0"></span>Hence, we can see that M = M'.

**Theorem 9.** Suppose  $\Gamma$  satisfies  $(\zeta, \zeta)$ -KE-ind. Then, our ABE scheme is adaptively secure under the  $\mathcal{D}_k$ -MDDH assumption. Let  $q_{\mathsf{sk}}$  be the maximum number of  $\mathcal{A}$ 's queries to KeyGen. For any PPT adversary  $\mathcal{A}$ , there exist PPT adversaries  $\mathcal{B}_1$  and  $\mathcal{B}_2$  such that

<span id="page-31-1"></span>
$$\mathsf{Adv}^{\mathsf{ABE}}_{\mathcal{A}}(\lambda) \leq \mathsf{Adv}^{\mathcal{D}_k\text{-}\mathsf{MDDH}}_{\mathcal{B}_1}(\lambda) + q_{\mathsf{sk}}\mathsf{Adv}^{(\zeta,\zeta)\text{-}\mathsf{KE-ind}}_{\mathcal{B}_2,\varGamma}(\lambda).$$

*Proof.* The proof follows the dual system methodology [39]. We consider a series of hybrids  $\mathsf{H}_1$  and  $\mathsf{H}_{2,j}$  for  $j \in [q_{\mathsf{sk}}]$ . To define each hybrid, we introduce a so-called semi-functional (SF) ciphertext and secret key, which are generated differently from normal ones. Specifically, an SF-ciphertext is generated as

$$\begin{split} &(n_1,n_2,\mathbf{c}(\mathbf{s},\hat{\mathbf{s}},\mathbf{w})) \leftarrow \mathsf{EncCt}(x), \ \ \mathbf{s}_1,\dots,\mathbf{s}_{n_1} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^k, \ \ \boxed{\mathbf{c}_0}, \hat{\mathbf{s}}_1,\dots,\hat{\mathbf{s}}_{n_2} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{k+\zeta}, \\ &\mathbf{S} = (\boxed{\mathbf{c}_0},\mathbf{A}\mathbf{s}_1,\dots,\mathbf{A}\mathbf{s}_{n_1}), \ \ \widehat{\mathbf{S}} = (\hat{\mathbf{s}}_1,\dots,\hat{\mathbf{s}}_{n_2}), \\ &\mathsf{ct}_x = (\mathsf{ct}_1,\mathsf{ct}_2,\mathsf{ct}_3) = ([\mathbf{S}]_1,[\mathbf{c}(\mathbf{S},\widehat{\mathbf{S}},\mathbb{W})]_1,[\boxed{\mathbf{c}_0^\top}\mathbf{h}]_\mathsf{T}M). \end{split}$$

An SF-secret key is generated as

$$(m_1, m_2, \mathbf{k}(\mathbf{r}, \hat{\mathbf{r}}, \mathbf{w})) \leftarrow \operatorname{EncKey}(y), \ \mathbf{r}_1, \dots, \mathbf{r}_{m_1} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^k, \ \hat{\mathbf{r}}_1, \dots, \hat{\mathbf{r}}_{m_2} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{k+\zeta},$$

$$\boxed{\mu \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p}, \ \mathbf{R} = (\mathbf{B}\mathbf{r}_1, \dots, \mathbf{B}\mathbf{r}_{m_1}), \ \hat{\mathbf{R}} = (\mathbf{h} + \boxed{\mu \mathbf{a}_{\zeta}^*}, \hat{\mathbf{r}}_1, \dots, \hat{\mathbf{r}}_{m_2}),$$

$$\operatorname{sk}_y = (\operatorname{sk}_1, \operatorname{sk}_2) = ([\mathbf{R}]_2, [\mathbf{k}(\mathbf{R}, \hat{\mathbf{R}}, \mathbb{W})]_2).$$
(5)

In the hybrids, the distribution of secret keys and the challenge ciphertext are modified as follows:

 $H_1$ : Same as the original game G except that the challenge ciphertext is SF.  $H_{2,j}(j \in [q_{sk}])$ : Same as  $H_1$  except that the first j secret keys given to A are SF.

We prove that  $G \approx_c H_1 \approx_c H_{2,1} \approx_c, \ldots, \approx_c H_{2,q_{sk}}$  and  $\mathcal{A}$ 's advantage in  $H_{2,q_{sk}}$  is statistically close to 0. We capture these as Lemmata 12 to 14. From these and the fact  $Adv_{\mathcal{A}}^{\mathsf{ABE}}(\lambda) = |\Pr[\langle \mathcal{A}, \mathsf{G} \rangle = \beta] - 1/2|$ , we have that Theorem 9 holds.

<span id="page-31-0"></span>**Lemma 12.** For all PPT adversaries A, there exists a PPT adversary B such that

$$|\Pr[\langle \mathcal{A},\mathsf{G}\rangle = \beta] - \Pr[\langle \mathcal{A},\mathsf{H}_1\rangle = \beta]| \leq \mathsf{Adv}_{\mathcal{B}}^{\mathcal{D}_k\text{-MDDH}}(\lambda).$$

*Proof.* To show this, we describe  $\mathcal{B}$ , which is given an instance of the  $\mathcal{U}_{k+\zeta,k}$ -MDDH problem  $(\mathbb{G}, [\mathbf{A}]_1, [\mathbf{t}_{\beta}]_1)$ . Note that we can write  $\mathbf{t}_0 = \mathbf{A}\mathbf{s}_0$  and  $\mathbf{t}_1 = \mathbf{c}_0$  where  $\mathbf{s}_0 \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^k$  and  $\mathbf{c}_0 \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{k+\zeta}$ .

- 1.  $\mathcal{B}$  generates  $\overline{\mathbf{B}}$ ,  $\mathbf{h}$ , and  $\mathbf{W}_1, \dots, \mathbf{W}_{\omega}$  by itself.
- 2.  $\mathcal{B}$  computes  $\mathsf{pk} = (\mathbb{G}, [\mathbf{A}]_1, [\mathbf{W}_1^{\top} \mathbf{A}]_1, \dots, [\mathbf{W}_{\omega}^{\top} \mathbf{A}]_1, [\mathbf{A}^{\top} \mathbf{h}]_{\mathsf{T}})$  and gives it to  $\mathcal{A}$ .
- 3. For queries  $\mathsf{KeyGen}(\mathsf{pk},\mathsf{msk},y)$ ,  $\mathcal B$  computes  $\mathsf{sk}_y$  honestly. This is possible because  $\mathcal B$  generates all elements in  $\mathsf{msk}$  by itself.
- 4. For the challenge query with messages  $(M_0, M_1)$  and an attribute  $x^*$ ,  $\mathcal{B}$  flips the coin  $\delta \leftarrow \{0, 1\}$  and generates  $\mathsf{ct}_{x^*}$  as

$$(n_1, n_2, \mathbf{c}(\mathbf{s}, \hat{\mathbf{s}}, \mathbf{w})) \leftarrow \mathsf{EncCt}(x), \ \mathbf{s}_1, \dots, \mathbf{s}_{n_1} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^k, \ \hat{\mathbf{s}}_1, \dots, \hat{\mathbf{s}}_{n_2} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{k+\zeta}$$

$$\mathbf{S} = (\mathbf{t}_{\beta}, \mathbf{A}\mathbf{s}_1, \dots, \mathbf{A}\mathbf{s}_{n_1}), \ \hat{\mathbf{S}} = (\hat{\mathbf{s}}_1, \dots, \hat{\mathbf{s}}_{n_2})$$

$$\mathsf{ct}_x = (\mathsf{ct}_1, \mathsf{ct}_2, \mathsf{ct}_3) = ([\mathbf{S}]_1, [\mathbf{c}(\mathbf{S}, \hat{\mathbf{S}}, \mathbb{W})]_1, [\mathbf{t}_{\beta}^{\mathsf{T}} \mathbf{h}]_{\mathsf{T}} M_{\delta}).$$

5.  $\mathcal{B}$  outputs true( $\delta = \delta'$ ), where  $\delta'$  is an output of  $\mathcal{A}$ .

Clearly, the case  $\beta = 0$  corresponds to G and the case  $\beta = 1$  corresponds to  $H_1$ .

**Lemma 13.** Let  $H_{2,0} = H_1$ . For all PPT adversaries  $\mathcal{A}$  and  $j \in [q_{sk}]$ , there exists a PPT adversary  $\mathcal{B}$  such that

$$|\Pr[\langle \mathcal{A}, \mathsf{H}_{2,j-1} \rangle = \beta] - \Pr[\langle \mathcal{A}, \mathsf{H}_{2,j} \rangle = \beta]| \leq \mathsf{Adv}_{\mathcal{B}, \Gamma}^{(\zeta, \zeta)\text{-KE-ind}}(\lambda).$$

*Proof.* To show this, we describe  $\mathcal{B}$ , which is given an input of  $(\zeta, \zeta)$ -KE-ind game for  $\eta = 1$ ,  $(\mathbb{G}, [\mathbf{A}]_1, [\mathbf{B}]_2, \mathbf{a}_{\zeta}^*, \{[\mathbf{W}_i^{\top} \mathbf{A}]_1, [\mathbf{W}_i \mathbf{B}]_2\}_{i \in [\omega]})$ .

- 1.  $\mathcal{B}$  samples  $\mathbf{h} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{k+\zeta}$  and computes  $[\mathbf{A}^{\top} \mathbf{h}]_{\mathsf{T}}$ .
