- 2.  $\mathcal{B}$  gives  $\mathsf{pk} = (\mathbb{G}, [\mathbf{A}]_1, [\mathbf{W}_1^\top \mathbf{A}]_1, \dots, [\mathbf{W}_{\omega}^\top \mathbf{A}]_1, [\mathbf{A}^\top \mathbf{h}]_\mathsf{T})$  to  $\mathcal{A}$ .
- 3. For the first j-1 queries KeyGen(pk, msk, y),  $\mathcal{B}$  computes a SF key sk<sub>y</sub> as shown in Eq. (5) using h,  $\mathbf{a}_{\zeta}^{*}$ ,  $[\mathbf{B}]_{2}$ , and  $\{[\mathbf{W}_{i}\mathbf{B}]_{2}\}_{i\in[\omega]}$ .
- 4. For the j-th query  $\mathsf{KeyGen}(\mathsf{pk},\mathsf{msk},y)$ ,  $\mathcal{B}$  queries  $\mathcal{O}_{\mathcal{Y}}$  on y and  $\mathbf{h}$ , and obtains  $([\mathbf{R}]_2,[\mathbf{k}(\mathbf{R},\widehat{\mathbf{R}},\mathbb{W})]_2)$ , where the first element of  $\widehat{\mathbf{R}}$  is  $\mathbf{h} + \beta \mu \mathbf{a}_{\zeta}^*$ .  $\mathcal{B}$  returns  $\mathsf{sk}_y = ([\mathbf{R}]_2,[\mathbf{k}(\mathbf{R},\widehat{\mathbf{R}},\mathbb{W})]_2)$  to  $\mathcal{A}$ .
- 5. For the rest of queries KeyGen(pk, msk,  $\hat{y}$ ),  $\mathcal{B}$  computes a normal secret key  $\mathsf{sk}_y$  using  $\mathbf{h}$ ,  $[\mathbf{B}]_2$ , and  $\{[\mathbf{W}_i\mathbf{B}]_2\}_{i\in[\omega]}$ .
- 6. For the challenge query with  $x^*$  and  $(M_0, M_1)$ ,  $\mathcal{B}$  flip the coin  $\delta \leftarrow \{0, 1\}$  and queries  $\mathcal{O}_{\mathcal{X}}$  on  $x^*$ .  $\mathcal{B}$  obtains the reply  $([\mathbf{S}]_1, [\mathbf{c}(\mathbf{S}, \widehat{\mathbf{S}}, \mathbb{W})]_1)$  and gives  $\mathsf{ct}_{x^*} = ([\mathbf{S}]_1, [\mathbf{c}(\mathbf{S}, \widehat{\mathbf{S}}, \mathbb{W})]_1, [\mathbf{c}_0^\top \mathbf{h}]_\mathsf{T} M_\delta)$ , where  $\mathbf{c}_0$  is the first element of  $\mathbf{S}$ .
- 7.  $\mathcal{B}$  outputs true( $\delta = \delta'$ ), where  $\delta'$  is an output of  $\mathcal{A}$ .

Observe that the j-th secret key is identically distributed to the normal key if  $\beta = 0$  and the SF-key otherwise. Thus, the case  $\beta = 0$  corresponds to  $\mathsf{H}_{2,j-1}$  and the case  $\beta = 1$  corresponds to  $\mathsf{H}_{2,j}$ .

<span id="page-32-2"></span>**Lemma 14.** For all PPT adversaries A, we have

$$|\Pr[\langle \mathcal{A}, \mathsf{H}_{2,q_{\mathsf{ch}}} \rangle = \beta] - 1/2| \le 2^{-\Omega(\lambda)}.$$

Proof. Because  $(\mathbf{A}^*||\mathbf{a}_1^*||\dots||\mathbf{a}_{\zeta}^*)$  forms a basis of  $\mathbb{Z}_p^{k+\zeta}$ , redefining  $\mathbf{h}$  as  $\mathbf{h} = \mathbf{A}^*\mathbf{z} + \sum_{i \in [\zeta]} z_i \mathbf{a}_i^*$  where  $\mathbf{z} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^k$ ,  $z_i \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p$  does not change its distribution. Recall that the information on  $\mathbf{h}$  that  $\mathcal{A}$  obtains throughout the game is  $\mathbf{A}^{\top}\mathbf{h}$  in  $\mathsf{pk}$ ,  $\mathbf{h} + \mu\mathbf{a}_{\zeta}^*$  in  $\mathsf{sk}_y$ , and  $\mathbf{c}_0^{\top}\mathbf{h}$  in  $\mathsf{ct}_{x^*}$ .  $\mathbf{A}^{\top}\mathbf{h}$  does not contain the information on  $z_{\zeta}$  because  $\mathbf{A}^{\top}\mathbf{a}_{\zeta}^* = \mathbf{0}$ . Similarly, each  $\mathbf{h} + \mu\mathbf{a}_{\zeta}^*$  in secret keys also does not contain the information on  $z_{\zeta}$  because it is masked by the fresh randomness  $\mu$ . Thus,  $\mathbf{c}_0^{\top}\mathbf{h} = \mathbf{c}_0^{\top}(\mathbf{A}^*\mathbf{z} + \sum_{i \in [\zeta]} z_i \mathbf{a}_i^*)$  is randomly distributed in  $\mathbb{Z}_p$  for  $\mathcal{A}$  unless  $\mathbf{c}_0^{\top}\mathbf{a}_{\zeta}^* = 0$  because  $z_{\zeta}$  is randomly distributed for  $\mathcal{A}$ . Since  $\mathbf{c}_0$  is randomly chosen from  $\mathbb{Z}_p^{k+\zeta}$ ,  $\mathbf{c}_0^{\top}\mathbf{a}_{\zeta}^* = 0$  with a probability  $2^{-\Omega(\lambda)}$ . If it is not the case,  $\mathsf{ct}_{x^*}$  does not have information on  $\beta$  because  $\mathsf{ct}_3$  is randomly distributed in  $G_{\mathsf{T}}$ .

#### <span id="page-32-0"></span>6 Extensions, Instantiations, and Applications

In this section, we provide extensions, instantiations, and applications of our framework. We first provide an overview.

#### <span id="page-32-1"></span>6.1 Overview

We obtain many applications in an analogous manner to the applications in [9].

**Extended Framework.** On the framework level, we obtain key-policy augmentation over a set of predicate families, denoted KBF, which is more powerful than the augmentation over a single predicate family (KBF1), as done in §4.3. This follows exactly the same modular approach as in [9]. That is, in our context, we can show that KBF is implied by KBF1 together with the direct sum and CBF1<sub>OR</sub>. We explain this in §6.2. Moreover, more applications such as nested-policy ABE can also be obtained analogously to [9].

**New Instantiations.** On the instantiation level, we have showed the result overview in the introduction. Here, we briefly describe how to obtain such instantiations. The full details follow from §6.3.

- Completely unbounded ABE for monotone Boolean formulae. Analogously to [9], we have that this predicate (in the key-policy flavor) is exactly KBF1[PIBBE], where PIBBE is the predicate for ID-based broadcast encryption. IBBE can then be augmented from IBE, of which we know a PMH-secure PES from e.g., [7]. The CP flavor is obtained by the dual conversion.
- Completely unbounded ABE for non-monotone Boolean formulae (the OSW type). This is also analogous to [9], where we consider two-mode IBBE (TIBBE), which can be then obtained by IBE and its negated predicate.
- Non-monotone KP-ABE with constant-size ciphertexts. A monotone variant is obtained by simply using the PMH-secure PES for IBBE with constant-size ciphertext encodings. Such a PES can be extracted from the PES for doubly spatial predicate in [7]. Since our KBF1-Trans preserves ciphertext encoding sizes, the converted scheme also obtains constant-size ciphertext encodings. For the non-monotone case, such a PES for TIBBE can be obtained by the disjunction of IBBE and negated IBBE (NIBBE). The latter can be viewed as a special case of negated doubly spatial predicate in [7], of which PES with constant-size encodings was reported. In §6.7, we directly construct a new TIBBE, which is two times efficient than the generic one from the disjunction.
- CP-ABE with constant-size ciphertexts. First note that we consider schemes with some bound on the size of policies (Boolean formulae), which the same requirement as CP-ABE with constant-size ciphertexts of [1,9,10]. We obtain this by two steps. First we show that, when considering small-universe, KP-ABE implies CP-ABE (for Boolean formulae, with the bounded condition). We use the depth-universal circuit [18] in this conversion. Second we show that CP-ABE with small universe implies CP-ABE with large universe (again for Boolean formulae, with the bounded condition). To the best of our knowledge, these conversions were not known and can be of an independent interest, as they are applied to ABE in general (not necessarily to PES). Note that we cannot do that as Attrapadung et al. [10] did, who considered similar implications in the case of more powerful span programs.
- ABE with constant-size keys. CP/KP-ABE with constant-size keys is obtained by the dual of KP/CP-ABE with constant-size ciphertexts, respectively.

As examples, we provide the descriptions of three concrete instantiations in §B.

**New Applications.** As a new application, we provide a new unified predicate related to nonmonotone ABE. Previously, there are two types of non-monotone ABE: the OSW type (Ostrovsky, Sahai, and Waters [34]) and the OT type (Okamoto and Takashima [33]). In the OSW type, a subpredicate P(y,X) amounts to check if an attribute is not in a set, e.g., if  $y \notin X$ , while the OT type, a label tag is also attached, but a sub-predicate  $P'((tag, y), (\overline{tag}, x))$  only checks the inequality on the same tag, e.g., if tag =  $\overline{\tan} \wedge y \neq x$ . Intuitively, the OSW type has a disadvantage in that the nonmembership test takes the complement over the whole universe and this may be too much for some applications, where we would like to consider multiple sub-universe and confine the complement to only in the related sub-universe. On the other hand, the OT type confines the non-membership to those with the same tag, but the non-membership test is enabled only with the set of single element, e.g.,  $\{x\}$ . We unify both types to overcome both disadvantages; that is, a sub-predicate P'((tag, y), (tag, X)) would check if  $tag = \overline{tag} \land y \notin X$ . We remark that when considering large-universe monotone ABE, there is no benefit to consider multiple spaces, since  $\mathbb{Z}_p$  is already exponentially large, and we can just treat a hashed value H(tag, y) as an attribute in  $\mathbb{Z}_p$ . In non-monotone ABE, we have to check the equality (of tags) and the non-membership at once, and the approach by hashing does not work. We motivate more on the unified non-monotone ABE, and provide definitions and constructions in §6.4.

#### <span id="page-33-0"></span>6.2 Augmentation over Predicate Sets

Following the composition framework of [9], we can also analogously define key-policy Boolean formula augmentations over a *set* of predicate families, rather than only a *single* predicate family, as done in Definition 14.

Some Terminology. Throughout this subsection, let  $\mathcal{P} = \{\mathsf{P}^{(1)}, \dots, \mathsf{P}^{(k)}\}$  be a set of predicate families. Each family  $\mathsf{P}^{(j)} = \{\mathsf{P}^{(j)}_{\kappa_j}\}_{\kappa_j}$  is indexed by  $\kappa_j = (N, \mathsf{par}_j)$ . The domain for each predicate is specified by  $\mathsf{P}^{(j)}_{\kappa_j} : \mathcal{X}^{(j)}_{\kappa_j} \times \mathcal{Y}^{(j)}_{\kappa_j} \to \{0,1\}$ . Unless specified otherwise, we define the combined index as  $\kappa = (N, \mathsf{par}) = (N, (\mathsf{par}_1, \dots, \mathsf{par}_k))$ . Let  $\mathbb{X}_{\kappa} \coloneqq \bigcup_{i \in [k]} (\{i\} \times \mathcal{X}^{(i)}_{\kappa_i})$  and  $\mathbb{Y}_{\kappa} \coloneqq \bigcup_{i \in [k]} (\{i\} \times \mathcal{Y}^{(i)}_{\kappa_i})$ .

<span id="page-34-1"></span>**Definition 16 (Key-Policy Augmentation over Predicate Sets).** Let  $\mathcal{P} = \{\mathsf{P}^{(1)}, \dots, \mathsf{P}^{(k)}\}$  be a set of predicate families. We define the predicate for *key-policy Boolean formula augmentation over set*  $\mathcal{P}$  as  $\mathsf{KBF}[\mathcal{P}] = \{\overline{\mathsf{P}}_{\kappa}\}_{\kappa}$  where  $\overline{\mathsf{P}}_{\kappa} : \bar{\mathcal{X}}_{\kappa} \times \bar{\mathcal{Y}}_{\kappa} \to \{0,1\}$  by letting

- $\bar{\mathfrak{X}}_{\kappa} = 2^{\mathbb{X}_{\kappa}}.$
- $-\bar{\mathcal{Y}}_{\kappa} = \bigcup_{i \in \mathbb{N}} (\mathbb{Y}_{\kappa}^{i} \times \mathcal{F}_{i})$ , where  $\mathcal{F}_{i}$  consists of all monotone Boolean formulae with input length i.
- For  $X \in \bar{\mathfrak{X}}_{\kappa}$  and  $Y = (((j_1, y_1), \dots, (j_n, y_n)), f) \in \bar{\mathfrak{Y}}_{\kappa}$  where  $f : \{0, 1\}^n \to \{0, 1\}$ , we define  $b = (b_1, \dots, b_n) \in \{0, 1\}^n$  by setting

$$b_i = 1$$
 iff  $\exists (j_i, x) \in X$  s.t.  $\mathsf{P}_{\kappa_{j_i}}^{(j_i)}(x, y_i) = 1$ 

We then define  $\overline{\mathsf{P}}_{\kappa}(X,y) = 1 \Leftrightarrow f(b) = 1$ .

**Unbounded/Dynamic/Static.** Similarly to [9], we consider (confined) variants of the predicate KBF[P] as follows. Consider the domain of  $((j_1,\ldots,j_n),f)$ , which specifies a policy over predicates. We denote their full domain as D, which can be inferred from Definition 16. For a class  $C \subseteq D$ , the predicate KBF[P] with the domain of  $((j_1,\ldots,j_n),f)$  being confined to C is denoted by KBF<sub>C</sub>[P] and is also called *dynamic Boolean formula composition with class* C. It is called *unbounded* if C = D. It is called *static* if |C| = 1. We will use a terminology  $P^{(1)} \vee P^{(2)}$  and  $P^{(1)} \wedge P^{(2)}$  to naturally denote the static OR and AND composition over  $\{P^{(1)}, P^{(2)}\}$ , respectively.

We have the following lemma, which follows analogously to the case of span programs in [9].

**Lemma 15.**  $KBF[\mathcal{P}]$  can be embedded into  $KBF1[CBF1_{OR}[DS[\mathcal{P}]]]$ .

#### <span id="page-34-0"></span>6.3 Basic Predicates

In the following subsections, we describe a modular approach similarly to [9] in obtaining our ABE instantiations from simpler basic predicates. We first recapitulate the following basic predicates as follows. For abbreviations, IBE is for ID-based encryption; NIBE is for negated IBE, IBBE is for ID-based broadcast encryption [19]; IBR is for ID-based revocation [11]; and TIBBE is for two-mode IBBE [42]. Let the universe in these predicates be  $\mathcal{U} = \mathbb{Z}_p$ .

```
 \begin{array}{l} - \ \mathsf{P}^{\mathsf{IBE}} : \mathcal{U} \times \mathcal{U} \to \{0,1\} \ \text{defined as } \mathsf{P}^{\mathsf{IBE}}(x,y) = 1 \Leftrightarrow x = y. \\ - \ \mathsf{P}^{\mathsf{NIBE}} : \mathcal{U} \times \mathcal{U} \to \{0,1\} \ \text{defined as } \mathsf{P}^{\mathsf{NIBE}}(x,y) = 1 \Leftrightarrow x \neq y. \\ - \ \mathsf{P}^{\mathsf{IBBE}} : 2^{\mathcal{U}} \times \mathcal{U} \to \{0,1\} \ \text{defined as } \mathsf{P}^{\mathsf{IBBE}}(X,y) = 1 \Leftrightarrow y \in X. \\ - \ \mathsf{P}^{\mathsf{IBR}} : 2^{\mathcal{U}} \times \mathcal{U} \to \{0,1\} \ \text{defined as } \mathsf{P}^{\mathsf{IBR}}(X,y) = 1 \Leftrightarrow y \notin X. \\ - \ \mathsf{P}^{\mathsf{TIBBE}} : 2^{\mathcal{U}} \times (\{1,2\} \times \mathcal{U}) \to \{0,1\} \ \text{defined as} \\ & \qquad \qquad \qquad \qquad \qquad \qquad \qquad \qquad \qquad \qquad \qquad \qquad \qquad \qquad \qquad \qquad \qquad \qquad
```

It is straightforward to see that  $P^{IBBE}$  can be embedded into  $CBF1_{OR}[P^{IBE}]$ , while  $P^{IBR}$  can be embedded into  $CBF1_{AND}[P^{NIBE}]$ , and  $P^{TIBBE}$  can be embedded into  $CBF1_{OR}[P^{IBBE} \odot P^{IBR}]$ . Now since we have a PES instantiation for  $P^{IBE}$  and  $P^{NIBE}$  that is secure in the sense of perfect master-key hiding from [7] and [6], respectively, we can instantiate ABE for these predicates via our transformations.

#### <span id="page-35-0"></span>6.4 Completely Unbounded ABE for Monotone Formulae

We denote by P KP-MBF the predicate of key-policy ABE for monotone boolean formulae (MBF) where all the parameters (the policy size, the attribute set size, the number of allowed multi-use of attributes in one policy) are unbounded and the attribute universe U is super-polynomially large. Its precise definition can be obtained modularly as

$$\mathsf{P}^{\mathsf{KP}\text{-}\mathsf{MBF}} \coloneqq \mathsf{KBF1}[\mathsf{P}^{\mathsf{IBBE}}],$$

or equivalently, it is KBF[P IBE]. The ciphertext-policy flavor is its dual, namely, P CP-MBF := Dual[P KP-MBF]. Kowalczyk and Wee [\[29\]](#page-43-6) recently proposed such an unbounded KP-ABE under the MDDH assumption; however, the ciphertext-policy variant has remained as an open problem. By using our modular transformation KBF1-Trans and Dual-Trans to the PES for P IBBE (which is obtained via transformations to the IBE of [\[7\]](#page-42-5), respectively), we obtain the first such unbounded CP-ABE under the MDDH assumption.

## <span id="page-35-1"></span>6.5 Completely Unbounded ABE for Non-Monotone Formulae

Due to De Morgan's Law, any non-monotone boolean formula (NBF) can be expressed by another formula where all the NOT gates are applied only at the input values. Using this fact, we can define the predicate for the completely-unbounded (key-policy) ABE for non-monotone Boolean formulae, denoted by P KP-NBF-OSW, as

$$\mathsf{P}^{\mathsf{KP}\text{-}\mathsf{NBF}\text{-}\mathsf{OSW}} \coloneqq \mathsf{KBF1}[\mathsf{P}^{\mathsf{TIBBE}}].$$

This type of ABE for NBF was defined by Ostrovsky, Sahai and Waters [\[34\]](#page-43-3), and hence we call it the OSW-type. It is crucial to note that, when we consider large-universe schemes, ABE for NBF is not trivially implied from ABE for MBF. One trivial implementation (that does not work) prepares the negative version of all attributes in the universe and requires any attribute set, say S, to include all negative attributes, say ¯x, if x is not in S; however, this is not possible due to the super-polynomial size universe.

The Okamoto-Takashima type [\[33\]](#page-43-5) of ABE for NBF was defined differently. Its modular definition was captured in [\[9\]](#page-42-6), and we recap it here. Let L = Z<sup>p</sup> be the "label" universe and U be the attribute universe. First define

$$\mathfrak{X}^{\mathsf{OT}} = \{ \{ (a_1, x_1), \dots, (a_t, x_t) \} \mid a_i \in \mathcal{L}, x_i \in \mathcal{U}, t \in \mathbb{N}, \text{if } i \neq j \text{ then } a_i \neq a_j \}.$$

We then define P OT : X OT × ({1, 2} × L × U) → {0, 1} by

$$\mathsf{P}^{\mathsf{OT}}\big(\left\{(a_1,x_1),\ldots,(a_t,x_t)\right\},\ (i,\ell,y)\big) = 1 \iff \big(i=1 \land (\exists j: a_j = \ell \land x_j = y)\big) \lor \big(i=2 \land (\exists j: a_j = \ell \land x_j \neq y)\big).$$

The OT-type ABE for NBF can then be defined as

$$\mathsf{P}^{\mathsf{KP}\text{-}\mathsf{NBF}\text{-}\mathsf{OT}} \coloneqq \mathsf{KBF1}[\mathsf{P}^\mathsf{OT}].$$

Disadvantages of the Previous Two Types of Non-monotonicity. Intuitively, we can consider that there is one large space U as a ciphertext-attribute universe in P KP-NBF-OSW, whereas there are multiple spaces U (1) , . . . , U (t) in P KP-NBF-OT. When we consider monotone ABE, there is no benefit to consider multiple spaces because U is already exponentially large, which concequently yields large universe ABE. However, the situation is different when we consider non-monotone ABE. That is, the negation in P KP-NBF-OSW is for the entire attribute universe U, whereas that in P KP-NBF-OT is for only a fraction of attribute universe, i.e., U (i) .

This is a critical difference in practice as pointed out by Tomida et al. [38]. Considering an example is the best way to describe the difference. Suppose that an attribute consists of a label and value, like YEAR:1991-2000, where YEAR is a label and 1991-2000 is a value. This is quite natural because each record in a typical relational database has this structure. Then, we consider the case where we handle two labels YEAR and CATEGORY. The negation in PKP-NBF-OSW (OSW-negation) can be described as (NOT YEAR:1991-2000) while negation in PKP-NBF-OT (OT-negation) is like (YEAR:NOT 1991-2000). Semantically, the former implies that the policy is satisfied if attribute YEAR:1991-2000 does not exist in a attribute set. On the other hand, the latter implies that the policy is satisfied if an attribute set has an attribute on label YEAR and its attribute is not 1991-2000.

This semantical difference arises from the structural difference of attribute universes in P<sup>KP-NBF-OSW</sup> and P<sup>KP-NBF-OT</sup>. In P<sup>KP-NBF-OSW</sup>, one needs to embed the information on both label and value into  $\mathcal{U}$ . On the other hand, in P<sup>KP-NBF-OT</sup>, one can associate the label with an index  $i \in \mathcal{L}$  of the attribute universe and embed only the information on a value into  $\mathcal{U}^{(i)}$ .

For typical applications of ABE, the structure of the universe in OT-nagation is more desirable. Consider the case to increase labels in ABE system that is in operation. If the system is based on OSW-negation, some inconvenience arises. That is, a secret key whose policy is negation of an attribute whose label is a new one that the system has not supported before can decrypt all ciphertexts generated so far. Let one of the new labels be ARTIST. If an authority issues a key whose policy is (NOT ARTIST:The Beatles), all previous ciphertexts are decrypted by the key even if the underlying content is by The Beatles because they do not have an attribute on label ARTIST. On the other hand, OT-negation does not cause this inconvenience because a key whose policy is (ARTIST:NOT The Beatles) is useless to decrypt ciphertexts without an attribute on label ARTIST.

Nevertheless, OT-non-monotonicity is not still almighty. If we carefully look at the definition of PKP-NBF-OT, we can see that each attribute sets can have at most one value for each label. That is, it does not allow attributes such as CATEGORY:Rock, Blues, R&B. This is also inconvenient when we consider labels that naturally takes multiple values per record or instance. This inconvenience motivate us to consider the following new type of non-monotone ABE, which does not cause the above problems.

New Unified Type of ABE for Non-Monotone Boolean Formulae. We propose a new "hybrid" type that combines and unifies both types (OSW,OT) above. First define

$$\mathfrak{X}^{\mathsf{OSWOT}} = \{ \{ (a_1, X_1), \dots, (a_t, X_t) \} \mid a_i \in \mathcal{L}, X_i \subseteq \mathcal{U}, t \in \mathbb{N}, \text{if } i \neq j \text{ then } a_i \neq a_j \}.$$

We then define  $\mathsf{P}^\mathsf{OSWOT}: \mathfrak{X}^\mathsf{OSWOT} \times (\{1,2\} \times \mathcal{L} \times \mathcal{U}) \to \{0,1\}$  by

$$\mathsf{P}^{\mathsf{OSWOT}}\big(\{(a_1,X_1),\ldots,(a_t,X_t)\},\;(i,\ell,y)\,\big) = 1 \;\Leftrightarrow \big(i = 1 \land (\exists j: a_j = \ell \land y \in X_j)\big) \lor \big(i = 2 \land (\exists j: a_j = \ell \land y \not\in X_j)\big).$$

The unified type ABE for NBF can then be defined as

$$\mathsf{P}^{\mathsf{KP}\text{-}\mathsf{NBF}\text{-}\mathsf{OSWOT}} \coloneqq \mathsf{KBF1}[\mathsf{P}^{\mathsf{OSWOT}}].$$

We can instantiate ABE for NBF (in all types). For this purpose, it is sufficient to instantiate PES for P<sup>OSWOT</sup>. Now, using the idea similar to [9], it is not difficult to see that the above P<sup>OSWOT</sup> can be embedded into

$$\mathsf{CBF1}_{\mathsf{OR}}[\mathsf{CBF1}_{\mathsf{OR}}[\mathsf{P}^{\mathsf{IBE}} \wedge \mathsf{P}^{\mathsf{IBBE}}] \odot \mathsf{CBF1}_{\mathsf{OR}}[\mathsf{P}^{\mathsf{IBE}} \wedge \mathsf{P}^{\mathsf{IBR}}]].$$

#### <span id="page-36-0"></span>6.6 Unified Definition for Bounded ABE for Boolean Formulae

<span id="page-36-1"></span>Towards constructing ABE with constant-size ciphertexts or keys, we will set bounds on some parameters. In this subsection, we give the following unified definition that can deal with combinations of bounds.

Definition 17 (Predicate variants of KP-ABE for MBF). The predicate family of KP-ABE for MBF in the xx variant, denoted by  $\mathsf{P}_{\kappa}^{\mathsf{KP-MBF-xx}}: \mathcal{X}_{\kappa} \times \mathcal{Y}_{\kappa} \to \{0,1\}$ , is define as follows. Each variant is indexed by a sub-vector of  $\kappa = (U,T,N,M,D,\varphi) \in \mathbb{N}^6$  (see more below). Denote the attribute universe as  $\mathcal{U}$  and let  $U = |\mathcal{U}|$ .

- $\mathfrak{X}_{\kappa} := \binom{\mathfrak{U}}{< T} = \{ X \in 2^{\mathfrak{U}} : |X| \le T \}.$
- $\begin{array}{l} -\ \mathcal{Y}_{\kappa}\coloneqq \overline{\bigcup_{n\leq N}}(\mathcal{V}_{n,\varphi}\times \mathcal{F}_{n,M,D}), \text{ where} \\ \bullet \ \mathcal{V}_{n,\varphi}\coloneqq \{\mathbf{y}\in \mathcal{U}^n\,|\, \text{The same element can appear at most }\varphi \text{ times in }\mathbf{y}.\}. \end{array}$ 
  - $\mathcal{F}_{n,M,D}$  consists of all monotone Boolean formulae with input length n, and size at most M, depth at most D.
- For  $X \in \mathfrak{X}_{\kappa}$  and  $Y = ((y_1, \ldots, y_n, f) \in \mathfrak{Y}_{\kappa}$  where  $f : \{0, 1\}^n \to \{0, 1\}$ , we set  $b_j = 1$  iff  $y_j \in X$ . Define  $\mathsf{P}_{\kappa}^{\mathsf{FP-MBF-xx}}(X, Y) = 1 \Leftrightarrow f(b_1, \ldots, b_n) = 1$ .

The index  $\kappa$  shows bounds regarding the domains  $\mathfrak{X}_{\kappa}, \mathfrak{Y}_{\kappa}$ . For a predicate variant where some parameters are unbounded, we write - in  $\kappa$ ; for example, a predicate with no bound T will be indexed by  $(U, -, N, M, D, \varphi)$ . Note that if U is unbounded, we set  $\mathcal{U}$  as a super-polynomial-size space, in particular,  $\mathcal{U} = \mathbb{Z}_p$  (such a variant is called "large-universe"). In this way, we can define a variant by the combination of the bounds, hence obtain up to 64 variants (some might be subsumed by others). We use  $xx \in \{0, \ldots, 63\}$  to name each variant by using the position of 1 in  $(xx)_2$  to mean that there is a bound in the corresponding position in  $\kappa$ . We will particularly consider the following variants.

- PKP-MBF-0: the completely-unbounded predicate (i.e., PKP-MBF).
- PKP-MBF-16, indexed by  $\kappa = (-, T, -, -, -, -)$ , is a predicate with the bounded attribute set size t. PKP-MBF-31, indexed by  $\kappa = (-, T, N, M, D, \varphi)$ , is a predicate with large universe.
- PKP-MBF-63: the completely-bounded predicate.

We can also analogously define the variants for NBF,  $P^{KP-NBF-T-xx}$ , where  $T \in \{OSW, OT, OSWOT\}$  in a natural manner (details are omitted).

### <span id="page-37-0"></span>**KP-ABE** with Constant-Size Ciphertexts

Monotone KP-ABE with Constant-Size Ciphertexts. We consider the bounded-attribute-setsize predicate, more precisely,  $\mathsf{P}^{\mathsf{KP-MBF-16}}$ . It can be interpreted as  $\mathsf{KBF1}[\mathsf{P}^{\mathsf{IBBE}'}]$ , where we define the predicate family  $\mathsf{P}^{\mathsf{IBBE}'} = \{\mathsf{P}^{\mathsf{IBBE}'}_T\}$  indexed by  $T \in \mathbb{N}$  by confining the domain  $2^{\mathfrak{U}}$  in  $\mathsf{P}^{\mathsf{IBBE}'}$  to  $\binom{\mathfrak{U}}{\leq T}$ .

Since our KBF1-Trans preserves the ciphertext encoding size, to obtain a PES for PKP-MBF-16 with constant-size ciphertext encodings, it suffices to construct such a PES for P<sup>IBBE'</sup>. For a set  $X \subseteq \mathbb{Z}_p$ , write

$$p_X(z) = \prod_{i \in X} (z - i) = a_0 + a_1 z + \dots + a_T z^T$$

and define  $\mathbf{v}_X \coloneqq (a_0, \dots, a_T)^\top \in \mathbb{Z}_p^{T+1}$  and  $\mathbf{v}_X' = (1, a_0, \dots, a_T)^\top \in \mathbb{Z}_p^{T+2}$ . For an element  $y \in \mathbb{Z}_p$ , define  $\mathbf{M}_y \in \mathbb{Z}_p^{(T+1) \times T}$ ,  $\mathbf{M}_y' \in \mathbb{Z}_p^{(T+2) \times (T+1)}$  as

$$\mathbf{M}_y \coloneqq \begin{pmatrix} \mathbf{m}_y^\top \\ \mathbf{I}_T \end{pmatrix} \coloneqq \begin{pmatrix} -y - y^2 & \cdots & -y^T \\ 1 & 1 & & \\ & \ddots & \\ & & 1 \end{pmatrix}, \qquad \qquad \mathbf{M}_y' \coloneqq \begin{pmatrix} 1 & 0 \\ 0 & \mathbf{M}_y \end{pmatrix}.$$

It can be shown that  $y \in X$  iff  $p_X(y) = 0$  iff  $\mathbf{v}_X$  is in the column span of  $\mathbf{M}_y$ . A PES for  $\mathsf{P}^{\mathsf{IBBE}'}$  is constructed as follows.<sup>5</sup>

<span id="page-37-1"></span> $<sup>^{5}</sup>$  Note that this PES can be viewed as a special case extracted from the PES for doubly spatial encryption predicate in [7].

- Param(T) = T + 2 = |w|.
- $\mathsf{EncCt}(X) = (0,0,c)$  where  $c = s\mathbf{w}^{\top}\mathbf{v}_X'$ , where the non-lone variable is s.
- EncKey $(y) = (1, 0, \mathbf{k})$  where  $\mathbf{k} = (\alpha, \mathbf{0}) + r\mathbf{w}^{\top}\mathbf{M}'_y$ , where the non-lone variable is r.
- $\mathsf{Pair}(X,y) = (\mathbf{e},\bar{\mathbf{e}}) \text{ where } \mathbf{e} = -(1,a_1,\ldots,a_T)^\top \text{ and } \bar{\mathbf{e}} = 1.$

The correctness amounts to prove  $s\mathbf{e}^{\top}\mathbf{k}^{\top} + c\bar{\mathbf{e}}\,r = \alpha s$ , which can be shown as follows. From  $y \in X$  we have  $p_X(y) = 0$  and hence, by inspection, we have  $\mathbf{M}_y' \mathbf{e} = -(1, a_0, \dots, a_T)^\top = -\mathbf{v}_X'$ , and this leads to

**Lemma 16.** The above PES for P<sup>IBBE'</sup> satisfies perfect master-key hiding.

*Proof.* Suppose  $\mathsf{P}^{\mathsf{IBBE}'}(X,y) = 0$ , i.e.,  $y \notin X$ . The encoding construction implies a system of equations with unknown  $\alpha$ , **w**:

$$\begin{pmatrix} 1 & r & 0 \\ 0 & 0 & r\mathbf{M}_{y}^{\top} \\ 0 & s & s\mathbf{v}_{X}^{\top} \end{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \boldsymbol{\alpha} \\ \mathbf{w} \end{pmatrix} = \begin{pmatrix} \mathbf{k}^{\top} \\ \mathbf{c}^{\top} \end{pmatrix}$$

From  $y \notin X$ , we have  $\mathbf{v}_X \notin \text{span}(\mathbf{M}_y)$ . Hence  $(1,0,\ldots,0)$  is not in the row span of the matrix on the left-hand side. Therefore,  $\alpha$  is completely hidden.

Non-Monotone KP-ABE with Constant-Size Ciphertexts. Here, we consider the predicate  $\mathsf{P^{KP\text{-}NBF\text{-}OSW\text{-}16}}.$  Similarly as above, it is equivalent to  $\mathsf{KBF1}[\mathsf{P^{TIBBE'}}],$  where  $\mathsf{P^{TIBBE'}}$  is defined analogously (confining to the attribute sets of size  $\leq T$ ). We define  $\mathbf{V}_X \in \mathbb{Z}_p^{(T+3) \times 2}, \, \mathbf{M}_y^{(1)} \in \mathbb{Z}_p^{(T+3) \times (T+1)},$  $\mathbf{M}_{n}^{(2)} \in \mathbb{Z}_{p}^{(T+3)\times(T+2)}$  as

$$\mathbf{V}_X \coloneqq \begin{pmatrix} 1 & 0 \\ 0 & \mathbf{v}_X \\ 0 & 1 \end{pmatrix}, \qquad \qquad \mathbf{M}_y^{(1)} \coloneqq \begin{pmatrix} 1 & 0 \\ 0 & \mathbf{M}_y \\ 1 & 0 \end{pmatrix}, \qquad \qquad \mathbf{M}_y^{(2)} \coloneqq \begin{pmatrix} 1 & 0 & 0 \\ 1 & \mathbf{m}_y^\top & 0 \\ 0 & \mathbf{I}_T & 0 \\ 0 & 0 & 1 \end{pmatrix}.$$

A PES for P<sup>TIBBE'</sup> is constructed as follows.

- $\operatorname{Param}(T) = T + 3 = |\mathbf{w}|.$
- $\mathsf{EncCt}(X) = (0,0,\mathbf{c})$  where  $\mathbf{c} = s\mathbf{w}^{\top}\mathbf{V}_X$ , where the non-lone variable is s.
- EncKey $(i, y) = (1, 0, \mathbf{k})$  where  $\mathbf{k} = (\alpha, \mathbf{0}) + r\mathbf{w}^{\mathsf{T}}\mathbf{M}_{y}^{(i)}$ , where the non-lone variable is r.
- $-\ \mathsf{Pair}(X,(i,y)) = (\mathbf{e},\bar{\mathbf{e}}), \text{ where we recall that we have the two following cases when } \mathsf{P}^{\mathsf{TIBBE'}}(X,(i,y)) = (\mathbf{e},\bar{\mathbf{e}}), \text{ where we recall that we have the two following cases when } \mathsf{P}^{\mathsf{TIBBE'}}(X,(i,y)) = (\mathbf{e},\bar{\mathbf{e}}), \text{ where we recall that we have the two following cases when } \mathsf{P}^{\mathsf{TIBBE'}}(X,(i,y)) = (\mathbf{e},\bar{\mathbf{e}}), \text{ where we recall that we have the two following cases when } \mathsf{P}^{\mathsf{TIBBE'}}(X,(i,y)) = (\mathbf{e},\bar{\mathbf{e}}), \text{ where we recall that we have the two following cases when } \mathsf{P}^{\mathsf{TIBBE'}}(X,(i,y)) = (\mathbf{e},\bar{\mathbf{e}}), \text{ where we recall that we have the two following cases when } \mathsf{P}^{\mathsf{TIBBE'}}(X,(i,y)) = (\mathbf{e},\bar{\mathbf{e}}), \text{ where } \mathsf{P}^{\mathsf{TIBBE'}}(X,(i,y)) = (\mathbf{e},\bar{\mathbf{e}}), \text{ where } \mathsf{P}^{\mathsf{TIBBE'}}(X,(i,y)) = (\mathbf{e},\bar{\mathbf{e}}), \text{ where } \mathsf{P}^{\mathsf{TIBBE'}}(X,(i,y)) = (\mathbf{e},\bar{\mathbf{e}}), \text{ where } \mathsf{P}^{\mathsf{TIBBE'}}(X,(i,y)) = (\mathbf{e},\bar{\mathbf{e}}), \text{ where } \mathsf{P}^{\mathsf{TIBBE'}}(X,(i,y)) = (\mathbf{e},\bar{\mathbf{e}}), \text{ where } \mathsf{P}^{\mathsf{TIBBE'}}(X,(i,y)) = (\mathbf{e},\bar{\mathbf{e}}), \text{ where } \mathsf{P}^{\mathsf{TIBBE'}}(X,(i,y)) = (\mathbf{e},\bar{\mathbf{e}}), \text{ where } \mathsf{P}^{\mathsf{TIBBE'}}(X,(i,y)) = (\mathbf{e},\bar{\mathbf{e}}), \text{ where } \mathsf{P}^{\mathsf{TIBBE'}}(X,(i,y)) = (\mathbf{e},\bar{\mathbf{e}}), \text{ where } \mathsf{P}^{\mathsf{TIBBE'}}(X,(i,y)) = (\mathbf{e},\bar{\mathbf{e}}), \text{ where } \mathsf{P}^{\mathsf{TIBBE'}}(X,(i,y)) = (\mathbf{e},\bar{\mathbf{e}}), \text{ where } \mathsf{P}^{\mathsf{TIBBE'}}(X,(i,y)) = (\mathbf{e},\bar{\mathbf{e}}), \text{ where } \mathsf{P}^{\mathsf{TIBBE'}}(X,(i,y)) = (\mathbf{e},\bar{\mathbf{e}}), \text{ where } \mathsf{P}^{\mathsf{TIBBE'}}(X,(i,y)) = (\mathbf{e},\bar{\mathbf{e}}), \text{ where } \mathsf{P}^{\mathsf{TIBBE'}}(X,(i,y)) = (\mathbf{e},\bar{\mathbf{e}}), \text{ where } \mathsf{P}^{\mathsf{TIBBE'}}(X,(i,y)) = (\mathbf{e},\bar{\mathbf{e}}), \text{ where } \mathsf{P}^{\mathsf{TIBBE'}}(X,(i,y)) = (\mathbf{e},\bar{\mathbf{e}}), \text{ where } \mathsf{P}^{\mathsf{TIBBE'}}(X,(i,y)) = (\mathbf{e},\bar{\mathbf{e}}), \text{ where } \mathsf{P}^{\mathsf{TIBBE'}}(X,(i,y)) = (\mathbf{e},\bar{\mathbf{e}}), \text{ where } \mathsf{P}^{\mathsf{TIBBE'}}(X,(i,y)) = (\mathbf{e},\bar{\mathbf{e}}), \text{ where } \mathsf{P}^{\mathsf{TIBBE'}}(X,(i,y)) = (\mathbf{e},\bar{\mathbf{e}}), \text{ where } \mathsf{P}^{\mathsf{TIBBE'}}(X,(i,y)) = (\mathbf{e},\bar{\mathbf{e}}), \text{ where } \mathsf{P}^{\mathsf{TIBBE'}}(X,(i,y)) = (\mathbf{e},\bar{\mathbf{e}}), \text{ where } \mathsf{P}^{\mathsf{TIBBE'}}(X,(i,y)) = (\mathbf{e},\bar{\mathbf{e}}), \text{ where } \mathsf{P}^{\mathsf{TIBBE'}}(X,(i,y)) = (\mathbf{e}$ 

  - If i = 1 and  $y \in X$ , we set  $\mathbf{e} = (1, a_1, \dots, a_T)^{\top}$  and  $\bar{\mathbf{e}} = (-1, -1)^{\top}$ . If i = 2 and  $y \notin X$ , we set  $\mathbf{e} = (1, \frac{a_1}{\delta}, \dots, \frac{a_T}{\delta}, \frac{1}{\delta})^{\top}$  and  $\bar{\mathbf{e}} = (-1, -\frac{1}{\delta})^{\top}$ , where  $\delta := p_X(y) \neq 0$ .

The correctness amounts to prove  $s\mathbf{e}^{\mathsf{T}}\mathbf{k}^{\mathsf{T}} + c\bar{\mathbf{e}}\,r = \alpha s$ , which can be shown as follows.

- Suppose i = 1 and  $y \in X$ . Then, the above holds since

$$\mathbf{M}_{y}^{(1)}\mathbf{e} = (1, a_{0}, \dots, a_{T}, 1)^{\top}$$
  $\mathbf{V}_{X}\bar{\mathbf{e}} = -(1, a_{0}, \dots, a_{T}, 1)^{\top},$ 

which implies  $\mathbf{M}_{y}^{(1)}\mathbf{e} + \mathbf{V}_{X}\bar{\mathbf{e}} = 0$ , and hence the claim.

- Suppose i=2 and  $y \notin X$ . Then, the above holds since

$$\mathbf{M}_{y}^{(2)}\mathbf{e} = (1, 1 - \frac{a_{1}y + \cdots a_{T}y^{t}}{\delta}, \frac{a_{1}}{\delta}, \dots, \frac{a_{T}}{\delta}, \frac{1}{\delta})^{\top}$$
$$\mathbf{V}_{X}\bar{\mathbf{e}} = (-1, -\frac{a_{0}}{\delta}, \dots, -\frac{a_{T}}{\delta}, -\frac{1}{\delta})^{\top},$$

which implies  $\mathbf{M}_{y}^{(2)}\mathbf{e} + \mathbf{V}_{X}\bar{\mathbf{e}} = 0$ , and hence the claim.

**Lemma 17.** The above PES for P<sup>TIBBE'</sup> satisfies perfect master-key hiding.

*Proof.* Suppose  $\mathsf{P}^{\mathsf{TIBBE'}}(X,(i,y)) = 0$ . We have two cases.

– Case i=1 and  $y \notin X$ . The encoding construction implies a system of equations with unknown  $\alpha, \mathbf{w}$ :

$$\begin{pmatrix} 1 & r & 0 & r \\ 0 & 0 & r \mathbf{M}_y^\top & 0 \\ 0 & s & 0 & 0 \\ 0 & 0 & s \mathbf{v}_X^\top & s \end{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \alpha \\ \mathbf{w} \end{pmatrix} = \begin{pmatrix} \mathbf{k}^\top \\ \mathbf{c}^\top \end{pmatrix}$$

From  $y \notin X$ , we have  $\mathbf{v}_X \notin \mathsf{span}(\mathbf{M}_y)$ . Hence  $(1,0,\ldots,0)$  is not in the row span of the matrix on the left-hand side. Therefore,  $\alpha$  is completely hidden.

– Case i=2 and  $y\in X.$  The encoding construction implies a system of equations with unknown  $\alpha, \mathbf{w}$ :

$$\begin{pmatrix} 1 & r & r & 0 & 0 \\ 0 & 0 & r\mathbf{m}_y & r\mathbf{I}_t & 0 \\ 0 & 0 & 0 & 0 & r \\ 0 & s & 0 & 0 & 0 \\ 0 & 0 & s\mathbf{v}_{X,0}^\top & s\mathbf{v}_{X,1\to T}^\top & s \end{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \boldsymbol{\alpha} \\ \mathbf{w} \end{pmatrix} = \begin{pmatrix} \mathbf{k}^\top \\ \mathbf{c}^\top \end{pmatrix},$$

where we write  $\mathbf{v}_X^{\top} = \mathbf{v}_{X,0}^{\top} || \mathbf{v}_{X,1 \to T}^{\top} = a_0 || (a_1 \dots, a_T)$ . By inspection, we have that  $(r, 0, \dots, 0)$  is not in the row span of  $(r\mathbf{m}_y, r\mathbf{I}_T)$ . Moreover, since  $y \in X$ , we have  $\mathbf{v}_X \in \mathsf{span}(\mathbf{M}_y)$ . Hence,  $(r, 0, \dots, 0)$  is also not in the row span of

$$\begin{pmatrix} r\mathbf{M}_y^\top \\ s\mathbf{v}_X^\top \end{pmatrix} = \begin{pmatrix} r\mathbf{m}_y & r\mathbf{I}_T \\ s\mathbf{v}_{X,0}^\top & s\mathbf{v}_{X,1\to T}^\top \end{pmatrix}$$

Hence  $(1,0,\ldots,0)$  is not in the row span of the matrix on the left-hand side. Therefore,  $\alpha$  is completely hidden.

This concludes the proof.

### <span id="page-39-0"></span>6.8 CP-ABE with Constant-Size Ciphertexts

**CP-ABE** with Constant-Size Ciphertexts. We next construct a PES for the predicate P<sup>CP-MBF-31</sup> (bounded formula sizes and attribute sets, but large-universe) with constant-size ciphertext encodings. We achieve this by the following two lemma.

<span id="page-39-2"></span>**Lemma 18.** P<sup>CP-MBF-63</sup> can be embedded into P<sup>KP-MBF-63</sup>.

<span id="page-39-3"></span>We use the *depth-universal circuit* of Cook and Hoover [18], where we recapitulate in the following proposition. It implies a universal circuit for NC1 (log-depth circuits), or equivalently Boolean formulae.

**Proposition 1** ([18]). For any k, M, D there is a universal circuit  $\bigcup_{k,M,D}$  that can simulate any circuit C having k inputs, of size at most M and depth at most D, and  $\bigcup_{k,M,D}$  has depth  $D_D = O(D)$  and size  $S_{M,D} = O(M^3D/\log M)$ . The input to the circuit  $\bigcup_{k,M,D}$  consists of the regular input k bits and  $C_M = O(M^2 \log M)$  bits representing the description of the simulated circuit C.

<span id="page-39-1"></span> $<sup>^6</sup>$  Exactly the same bound requirements are analogously assumed for the previous CP-ABE schemes (for monotone span programs) with constant-size ciphertexts [1,10].

Proof (of Lemma 18). Consider  $\mathsf{P}_{\kappa}^{\mathsf{CP-MBF-63}}: \mathcal{Y}_{\kappa} \times \mathcal{X}_{\kappa} \to \{0,1\}$  and  $\mathsf{P}_{\kappa'}^{\mathsf{KP-MBF-63}}: \mathcal{X}_{\kappa'} \times \mathcal{Y}_{\kappa'} \to \{0,1\}$  (see Definition 17). We assume w.l.o.g. that  $\mathcal{U} = [u]$ . We map  $\kappa = (U,T,N,M,D,\varphi) \mapsto \kappa' = (U',T',N',M',D',\varphi')$  by setting  $U' = T' = N' = \mathsf{C}_{\tilde{M}},\ M' = \mathsf{S}_{\tilde{M},\tilde{D}},\ D' = \mathsf{D}_{\tilde{D}},\ \varphi' = 1$ , where  $\tilde{M} = O(M+U), \tilde{D} = O(D+\log U+\log \varphi)$  are set as below.

Towards using the universal circuit, we first map the ciphertext attribute  $Y = (\mathbf{y}, f) \in \mathcal{Y}_{\kappa}$  of CP-ABE (which consists of the input label  $\mathbf{y} \in \mathcal{U}^n$  and a boolean formula  $f : \{0,1\}^n \to \{0,1\}$ ) to its corresponding boolean formula  $g_Y : \{0,1\}^{\varphi U+1} \to \{0,1\}$  (now with globally-fixed input labels), and map the key attribute  $X \in \mathcal{X}_{\kappa}$  of CP-ABE to its corresponding bit string  $\mathbf{b}_X \in \{0,1\}^{\varphi U+1}$ , so that we will have

<span id="page-40-0"></span>
$$g_Y(\mathbf{b}_X) = \mathsf{P}_{\kappa}^{\mathsf{CP-ABE-63}}(Y, X). \tag{6}$$

This can be done as follows. Consider a new universe  $\mathcal{U}' = [U] \times [\varphi] \cup \{\mathsf{dummy}\}$  and assume some lexicographical order in  $\mathcal{U}'$ .

- From  $\mathbf{y} \in \mathcal{U}^n$ , we define  $\mathbf{y}' \in (\mathcal{U}')^n$  by setting  $y_j' = (y_j, q)$  if  $y_j$  is the q-th appearance of the same attribute in  $\mathbf{y}$ , i.e.,  $q = |\{\iota \in [j]|y_\iota = y_j\}|$ . We construct  $g_Y$  to be the same as f except with the following modifications. First the input labels are modified from  $\mathbf{y}$  to  $\mathbf{y}'$ . Then we re-order the input wires so that they are in a lexicographical order in  $\mathcal{U}'$ . We next add an input wire labelled dummy. Then for all  $b \in \mathcal{U}'$  where x does not appear in  $\mathbf{y}'$ , we add an input wire labelled and take an AND over them and the dummy input wire then take an OR over the output of this AND gate and the output wire, and output it as a new output wire. We expand the AND gate into many AND gates with fan-in 2 in depth  $O(\log \varphi U)$ . This completes the specification of  $g_Y$ , which always have all input wires labelled fully by  $\mathcal{U}'$  (in the lexicographical order). By inspection,  $g_Y$  has depth  $\tilde{D} = O(D + \log U + \log \varphi)$  and size  $\tilde{M} = O(M + U)$ .
- For  $X \in \mathfrak{X}_{\kappa}$ , we set  $\mathbf{b}_{X} = (b_{j})_{j \in \mathfrak{U}'} \in \{0,1\}^{\varphi U+1}$  (in the lexicographical order) as follows. Let  $b_{\mathsf{dummy}} = 0$ . For each  $j \in \mathfrak{U}' \setminus \{\mathsf{dummy}\}$  we parse  $j = (\iota, q)$  and for all  $q \in [\varphi]$  we set  $b_{j} = 1$  iff  $\iota \in X$ .

It is straightforward to see that Eq. (6) holds.

Now that we have the set of globally fixed input labels, we can use a depth-universal circuit (Proposition 1)  $\mathsf{U} \coloneqq \mathsf{U}_{\varphi U+1,\tilde{M},\tilde{D}}$ . For a boolean formula  $g_Y: \{0,1\}^{\varphi U+1} \to \{0,1\}$ , we write its description as a bit string  $\mathsf{desc}(g_Y) \in \{0,1\}^{\mathsf{C}_{\tilde{M}}}$  where  $\mathsf{C}_{\tilde{M}} = O(\tilde{M}^2 \log \tilde{M})$  (by using the extended encoding in [18]). The universal circuit  $\mathsf{U}: \{0,1\}^{\mathsf{C}_{\tilde{M}}} \times \{0,1\}^{\varphi U+1} \to \{0,1\}$  has the following property:

$$\mathsf{U}(\mathsf{desc}(g_Y), \mathbf{b}_X) = g_Y(\mathbf{b}_X). \tag{7}$$

We then view  $\mathsf{U}(\cdot,\mathbf{b}_X)$  as a boolean formula  $h_X:\{0,1\}^{\mathsf{C}_{\tilde{M}}}\to\{0,1\}$  with the input labels being  $1,\ldots,\mathsf{C}_{\tilde{M}}$ . This yields

$$h_X(\mathsf{desc}(g_Y)) = \mathsf{U}(\mathsf{desc}(g_Y), \mathbf{b}_X) \tag{8}$$

We can finally map

$$Y \mapsto A_Y = \{ \iota \in [\mathsf{C}_{\tilde{M}}] \mid \text{The } \iota\text{-th element in } \mathsf{desc}(g_Y) \text{ is } 1 \} \in \mathfrak{X}'_{\kappa}, \\ X \mapsto B_X = ([\mathsf{C}_{\tilde{M}}], h_X) \in \mathfrak{Y}'_{\kappa},$$

where we consider the attribute universe  $[C_{\tilde{M}}]$  in KP-ABE. From the definition of  $P_{\kappa'}^{\mathsf{KP-MBF-63}}$  we have

$$\mathsf{P}_{\kappa'}^{\mathsf{KP-MBF-63}}(A_Y,B_X) = h_X(\mathsf{desc}(g_Y)) \tag{9}$$

<span id="page-40-3"></span><span id="page-40-2"></span><span id="page-40-1"></span>

From Eq. (6), Eq. (7), Eq. (8), Eq. (9), we thus have

$$\mathsf{P}_{\kappa}^{\mathsf{CP\text{-}MBF-63}}(Y\!,X) = 1 \Leftrightarrow \mathsf{P}_{\kappa'}^{\mathsf{KP\text{-}MBF-63}}(A_Y,B_X) = 1.$$

This concludes the lemma.

Lemma 19. PCP-MBF-31 can be embedded into PCP-MBF-63.

Proof. Consider  $\mathsf{P}_{\kappa}^{\mathsf{CP-MBF-31}}: \mathcal{Y}_{\kappa} \times \mathcal{X}_{\kappa} \to \{0,1\}$  and  $\mathsf{P}_{\kappa'}^{\mathsf{CP-MBF-63}}: \mathcal{Y}_{\kappa'}' \times \mathcal{X}_{\kappa'}' \to \{0,1\}$  and  $(cf.\ \text{the keypolicy version of definition in Definition 17.})$ . We map  $\kappa = (-,T,N,M,D,\varphi) \mapsto \kappa' = (U',T',N',M',D',\varphi')$  as follows. In the large universe CP-ABE, the universe is  $\mathbb{Z}_p$  where  $\lambda = \lceil \log p \rceil$  is the security parameter. We set  $U' = 2T\lambda, \ T' = T\lambda, \ N' = NT\lambda, \ M' = M + 2T\lambda - 1, \ D' = D + \lceil \log T \rceil + \lceil \log \lambda \rceil,$  and  $\varphi' = \varphi$ . We set a new universe as  $\mathcal{U}' = [T] \times [\lambda] \times \{0,1\}$ . We map as follows.

- From  $Y = (\mathbf{y}, f) \in \mathcal{Y}_{\kappa}$ , we construct  $Y' = (\mathbf{y}', f') \in \mathcal{Y}'_{\kappa'}$  as follows. Parse  $\mathbf{y} = (y_1, \dots, y_n)$ . For each  $y_j$  in  $\mathbf{y}$ , denote the bit decomposition of  $y_j$  as  $(y_{j,1}, \dots, y_{j,\lambda}) \in \{0,1\}^{\lambda}$ . For  $k \in [T], j \in [n]$ , define

$$\mathbf{y}_{k,j} \coloneqq ((k,1,y_{j,1}),\ldots,(k,\lambda,y_{j,\lambda})) \in (\mathcal{U}')^{\lambda}.$$

We set the new input wires y' as

$$\mathbf{y}' = \mathbf{y}_{1,1}||\cdots||\mathbf{y}_{1,i}||\mathbf{y}_{2,1}||\cdots||\mathbf{y}_{2,i}||\cdots||\mathbf{y}_{T,1}||\cdots||\mathbf{y}_{T,i},$$

where || is the concatenation. Note that if the maximum repetition in  $\mathbf{y}$  is  $\varphi$ , then the maximum repetition in  $\mathbf{y}'$  is also  $\varphi$  (hence we set  $\varphi' = \varphi$ ). We construct f' to be exactly the same as f except that for each input wire  $y_i$  of f, we add the following (depth-2, large fan-in) sub-circuit:

$$\bigvee_{k=1}^{T} \bigwedge_{\iota=1}^{\lambda} (k, \iota, y_{j,\iota})$$

in such a way that its output wire connects to the wire  $y_j$ . Note that now we have that the input labels of f' are exactly  $\mathbf{y}'$ . This sub-circuit can be then straightforwardly converted to an equivalent fan-in-2 circuit with depth  $\lceil \log T \rceil + \lceil \log \lambda \rceil$  (by expanding the OR and the AND). As a result, f' is a Boolean formulae with depth  $D' = D + \lceil \log T \rceil + \lceil \log \lambda \rceil$ , size  $M' = M + 2T\lambda - 1$ , and input length  $nT\lambda$  (recall that D, M is the depth and the size of f, respectively).

- From  $X \in \mathcal{X}_{\kappa}$ , we construct  $X' \in \mathcal{X}'_{\kappa'}$  as follows. Parse  $X = \{x_1, \dots, x_t\}$ . For each  $x_j \in X$ , denote the bit decomposition of x as  $(x_{j,1}, \dots, x_{j,\lambda})$ . We set

$$X' = \bigcup_{j=1}^{t} \{ (j, 1, x_{j,1}), \dots, (j, \lambda, x_{j,\lambda}) \}.$$

Note that we have  $X' \in {\mathcal{U} \choose < T'}$ , where we let  $T' = T\lambda$ . This is since  $t \leq T$ .

We claim that

$$\mathsf{P}_{\kappa}^{\mathsf{CP\text{-}MBF\text{-}31}}(Y,X) = \mathsf{P}_{\kappa'}^{\mathsf{CP\text{-}MBF\text{-}63}}(Y',X').$$

This holds since the functionality of the above sub-circuit is to compute the satisfiability for  $y_j \in X$ .  $\square$ 

Combining both lemmata, we obtain the following corollary.

Corollary 3. PCP-MBF-31 can be embedded into PKP-MBF-63.

We can inspect the efficiency of the resulting large-universe CP-ABE from the small-universe KP-ABE by combining the parameter mappings in the proofs of both lemmata. That is, if we let  $\kappa$  and  $\kappa''$  be the indexes of the large-universe CP-ABE and the small-universe KP-ABE, respectively, then via the two lemmata we have the combined map that takes  $\kappa = (-, T, N, M, D, \varphi) \mapsto \kappa'' = (U'', T'', N'', M'', D'', \varphi'')$  where  $\varphi'' = 1$  and

$$U'' = T'' = N'' = O((M + T\lambda)^2 \log(M + T\lambda)) = \tilde{O}((M + T\lambda)^2),$$
  

$$M'' = O((M + T\lambda)^3 (D + \log T + \log \lambda + \log \varphi) / \log(M + T\lambda)),$$
  

$$D'' = O(D + \log T + \log \lambda + \log \varphi).$$

Applying the combined conversion in this sub section to the KP-ABE with constant-size ciphertexts of the previous subsection (§6.7), we obtain the large-universe CP-ABE with constant-size ciphertexts. The public key size is  $O(T'') = \tilde{O}((M+T\lambda)^2)$ , while the secret key size is  $O(N''T'') = \tilde{O}((M+T\lambda)^4)$ .

#### <span id="page-42-0"></span>6.9 KP-ABE, CP-ABE with Constant-Size Keys

We apply the dual conversion to ABE with constant-size ciphertexts to obtain the following.

(Non-monotone) CP-ABE with Constant-Size Keys. This can be obtained by applying the dual conversion to the (non-monotone) KP-ABE with constant-size ciphertexts of §[6.7.](#page-37-0) The property of constant-size ciphertexts in KP-ABE becomes the property of constant-size keys in CP-ABE since the size of ciphertexts preserve to the size of keys (and vice versa) via the dual conversion.

KP-ABE with Constant-Size Keys. This can be obtained by applying the dual conversion to the CP-ABE with constant-size ciphertexts of §[6.8.](#page-39-0)

## <span id="page-44-0"></span>A More Related Works

ABE for DFA and more. Many recent works proposed ABE for DFA (and beyond). We explore them here in three aspects: Can we use some of our instantiations in their schemes? Can we use their schemes as ABE components casted in our framework so as to combine with other ABE for other predicates? and Can we generalize their techniques so as to have a new DFA composition framework over basic predicates, based on k-Lin? Note that the only known DFA composition framework in ABE is given by Attrapadung [\[9\]](#page-42-6) based on the q-ratio assumption.

At TCC'19, Agrawal, Maitra, and Yamada [\[5\]](#page-42-14) proposed a generic conversion from unbounded multiuse KP-ABE and CP-ABE for monotone span programs (MSP) to ABE for DFA. Unfortunately, our instantiations on unbounded multi-use KP-ABE/CP-ABE are for Boolean formulae, which are less generic than MSP. Hence, we cannot use our instantiations in their conversions. Note that their instantiations use selective<sup>∗</sup> secure unbounded multi-use CP-ABE for MSP to obtain selective<sup>∗</sup> secure ABE for DFA, where selective<sup>∗</sup> security is an intermediate notion between semi-adaptive and very selective security. When extracting their ABE as a PES, it likely does not satisfy KE-ind since otherwise their original ABE instantiation would be proved adaptive secure. Therefore, we cannot cast their scheme into our framework to combine with other ABE. At Crypto'19, Gong, Waters, and Wee [\[22\]](#page-43-13) proposed selectively secure ABE for DFA from k-Lin. Again, the extracted PES from this likely does not satisfy KE-ind. Finally, it also seems difficult to use techniques from these works [\[5,](#page-42-14)[22\]](#page-43-13) to obtain a new DFA composition framework, since they do not achieve adaptive security in the first place. Note that it may possible to consider compositions in weaker settings such as selectively secure ones, but we do not pursue them here. At Crypto'19, Agrawal, Maitra, and Yamada [\[4\]](#page-42-2) proposed ABE for NFA from LWE, and hence is not compatible with our pairing-based framework.

Concurrently and very recently, at Eurocrypt'20, Gong and Wee [\[23\]](#page-43-14) proposed adaptively secure ABE for DFA from k-Lin, while Lin and Luo [\[31\]](#page-43-15) proposed adaptively secure ABE for ABP, DFA, NFA, L, NL from k-Lin (with the last two, L/NL, being in some relaxed settings). First, Gong and Wee [\[23\]](#page-43-14) constructed their scheme based on a similar design concept to the line of works on ABE for DFA from pairings [\[7,](#page-42-5) [22,](#page-43-13) [40\]](#page-44-2) (but of course with distinguished tricks to achieve adaptive security under k-Lin). Hence, it can be captured, at least syntactically, by a PES. Therefore, it might be possible to take their scheme into our framework. However, this needs careful analysis to confirm that the PES representing their scheme satisfies KE-ind, which seems not a simple task at a first glance. Similarly, we consider that using their technique to realize policy augmentations with DFA policies, as considered in [\[9\]](#page-42-6), also may be possible, while it may also require more analysis. We leave them as a future research direction. Second, Lin and Luo [\[31\]](#page-43-15) introduced a completely new method to construct adaptively secure ABE schemes. Ciphertexts and secret keys of their schemes comprise those of an inner product functional encryption scheme, and thus it seems not possible to capture them by the PES framework. Hence, we consider that it might be difficult to apply their work to our framework.

On Combining ABE. As a related work regarding combining functionalities into one scheme, we can view the "bundling functionalities" transformation of [25] as the direct sum of parametrized predicates  $\{P_n\}_{n\in\mathbb{N}}$  of the same family. Syntactically, our direct sum offers more: bundling predicates of different families. Moreover, our KP augmentation can provide dynamic policies (boolean formulae) among the bundled predicates. In the aspect of applicability, their scheme is more general in the sense that their transformation applies to any ABE or FE, while ours applies to ABE that can be casted as PES (that satisfies KE-ind). One more difference is that [25] achieves semi-adaptive security, while ours is adaptively secure.

More on Unbounded ABE. In the relation to other unbounded ABE in the literature, continued from the discussion in Section 1.3, it is also worth remark that unbounded ABE by Okamoto and Takashima has a large universe [33]. Thus, if we can apply the KW framework to their scheme, we would also obtain an alternative completely unbounded ABE scheme, but it seems not so straightforward.

#### <span id="page-45-0"></span> $\mathbf{B}$ Concrete Descriptions of Our Instantiations

For self-containment, as examples, we provide the concrete descriptions of three schemes that are newly obtained by our framework, namely, completely unbounded KP/CP-ABE for monotone Boolean formulae and KP-ABE with constant-size ciphertexts for monotone Boolean formulae.

### <span id="page-45-1"></span>Completely Unbounded KP-ABE for Monotone Formulae

A predicate for completely unbounded KP-ABE for monotone Boolean formulae,  $P^{\mathsf{KP-MBF}}: \mathfrak{X} \times \mathfrak{Y} \to \mathbb{R}$  $\{0,1\}$ , is defined as follows:

- $\mathfrak{X} = 2^{\mathbb{Z}_p}.$
- $\begin{array}{l} \mathcal{X} = \mathcal{Y} = \bigcup_{i \in \mathbb{N}} (\mathbb{Z}_p^i \times \mathcal{F}_i), \text{ where } \mathcal{F}_i \text{ consists of all monotone Boolean formulae with input length } i. \\ -\text{ For } X = \{x_1, \dots, x_t\} \in \mathcal{X} \text{ and } Y = ((y_1, \dots, y_n), f) \in \mathcal{Y} \text{ where } f: \{0, 1\}^n \to \{0, 1\}, \text{ we set } b_i = 1 \text{ iff } y_i \in X. \text{ Then, we define } \mathsf{P}^{\mathsf{KP-MBF}}(X, Y) = 1 \Leftrightarrow f(b_1, \dots, b_n) = 1. \end{array}$

In our framework, the predicate  $\mathsf{P}^{\mathsf{KP-MBF}}$  can be embedded into

$$\mathsf{KBF1}[\mathsf{P}^\mathsf{IBBE}] = \mathsf{KBF1}[\mathsf{Dual}[\mathsf{KBF1}_\mathsf{OR}[\mathsf{P}^\mathsf{IBE}]]].$$

Thus, the corresponding PES  $\Gamma^{\mathsf{KP-MBF}}$  is described as follows:

- Param() = 3
- $\mathsf{EncCt}(\{x_1,\ldots,x_t\}) = (t,0,\mathbf{c})$ . Polynomials  $\mathbf{c} = (c_1,\ldots,c_t)$  are defined as follows:

$$c_i = s_0 w_1 - s_i (x_i w_2 + w_3).$$

- EncKey $((y_1,\ldots,y_n),f)=(n,\tau,\mathbf{k})$ , where  $\tau$  is the number of AND gates in f. Let Share, be the algorithm defined in Fig 4. Polynomials  $\mathbf{k} = (k_{1,1}, \dots, k_{1,n}, k_{2,1}, \dots, k_{2,n})$  are defined as follows:

$$\sigma_1, \ldots, \sigma_n \leftarrow \mathsf{Share}_{\mathsf{p}}(f, \alpha, \hat{\mathbf{r}}_{-\alpha} = (\hat{r}_1, \ldots, \hat{r}_{\tau})),$$
  
 $k_{1,i} = \sigma_i - r_i w_1, \ k_{2,i} = r_i (y_i w_2 + w_3).$ 

-  $\mathsf{Pair}(\{x_1,\ldots,x_t\},(y_1,\ldots,y_n),f)=(\mathbf{E},\overline{\mathbf{E}})$ . Let  $S\subseteq\{i\mid y_i\in\{x_1,\ldots,x_t\}\}$  be the set such that  $\sum_{i \in S} \sigma_i = \alpha. \ \mathbf{E} = (e_{i,j})_{i \in [t+1], j \in [2n]} \text{ and } \mathbf{\overline{E}} = (\bar{e}_{i,j})_{i \in [t], j \in [n]} \text{ are defined as the following equation}$ 

$$\mathbf{sEk}^{\top} + \mathbf{c}\overline{\mathbf{E}}\mathbf{r}^{\top} = \sum_{i \in S} (s_0 k_{1,i} + c_{\phi(i)} r_i + s_{\phi(i)} k_{2,i}),$$

where  $\phi: S \to [t]$  is a function such that  $y_i = x_{\phi(i)}$ .

Because  $\Gamma^{\mathsf{KP\text{-}MBF}}$  is obtained by applying the dual conversion once to a PES with single-variable PMH, namely,  $\Gamma^{\mathsf{IBE}}$ ,  $\Gamma^{\mathsf{KP\text{-}MBF}}$  satisfies (2, 2)-KE-ind. Thus, the concrete scheme is described as follows.

Setup( $1^{\lambda}$ ): It takes a security parameter  $1^{\lambda}$  and outputs pk and msk as follows.

$$\begin{split} &\mathbb{G} \leftarrow \mathcal{G}_{\mathsf{BG}}(1^{\lambda}), \ \mathbf{A}, \mathbf{B} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{(k+2) \times k}, \ \mathbf{h} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{k+2}, \ \mathbf{W}_1, \dots, \mathbf{W}_3 \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{(k+2) \times (k+2)} \\ &\mathsf{pk} = (\mathbb{G}, [\mathbf{A}]_1, [\mathbf{W}_1^{\top} \mathbf{A}]_1, \dots, [\mathbf{W}_3^{\top} \mathbf{A}]_1, [\mathbf{A}^{\top} \mathbf{h}]_{\mathsf{T}}) \\ &\mathsf{msk} = (\mathbf{B}, \mathbf{h}, \mathbf{W}_1, \dots, \mathbf{W}_3). \end{split}$$

Enc(pk, X, M): It takes pk, an attribute  $X = \{x_1, \dots, x_t\} \in \mathcal{X}$ , and a message  $M \in G_T$  and outputs  $\mathsf{ct}_X$  as follows. Let Share be an algorithm defined in Fig 5.

$$\mathbf{s}_0, \mathbf{s}_1, \dots, \mathbf{s}_t \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^k$$

$$\mathsf{ct}_{1,i} = [\mathbf{A}\mathbf{s}_i]_1, \ \mathsf{ct}_{2,i} = [\mathbf{W}_1^\top \mathbf{A}\mathbf{s}_0 - (x_i \mathbf{W}_2^\top + \mathbf{W}_3^\top) \mathbf{A}\mathbf{s}_i]_1, \ \mathsf{ct}_3 = [\mathbf{s}_0^\top \mathbf{A}^\top \mathbf{h}]_\mathsf{T} M$$

$$\mathsf{ct}_X = (\{\mathsf{ct}_{1,i}\}_{i \in [t]^+}, \{\mathsf{ct}_{2,i}\}_{i \in [t]}, \mathsf{ct}_3).$$

KeyGen(pk, msk, Y): It takes pk, msk, and a set  $Y = ((y_1, \dots, y_n), f) \in \mathcal{Y}$  and outputs  $\mathsf{sk}_Y$  as follows.

$$\begin{split} \mathbf{r}_1, \dots, \mathbf{r}_n &\leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^k, \quad \boldsymbol{\sigma}_1, \dots, \boldsymbol{\sigma}_n \leftarrow \mathsf{Share}(f, \mathbf{h}) \\ \mathsf{sk}_{1,i} &= [\mathbf{B}\mathbf{r}_i]_2, \quad \mathsf{sk}_{2,i} = [\boldsymbol{\sigma}_i - \mathbf{W}_1\mathbf{B}\mathbf{r}_i]_2, \quad \mathsf{sk}_{3,i} = [(y_i\mathbf{W}_2 + \mathbf{W}_3)\mathbf{B}\mathbf{r}_i]_2 \\ \mathsf{sk}_Y &= \{\mathsf{sk}_{1,i}, \mathsf{sk}_{2,i}, \mathsf{sk}_{3,i}\}_{i \in [n]}. \end{split}$$

Dec(pk, ct<sub>X</sub>, sk<sub>Y</sub>): It takes pk, ct<sub>X</sub> = ({ct<sub>1,i</sub>}<sub>i∈[t]</sub>, {ct<sub>2,i</sub>}<sub>i∈[t]</sub>, ct<sub>3</sub>), and sk<sub>Y</sub> = {sk<sub>1,i</sub>, sk<sub>2,i</sub>, sk<sub>3,i</sub>}<sub>i∈[n]</sub> such that P<sup>KP-MBF</sup>(X, Y) = 1. Let S and  $\phi$  be the same as those defined in Pair of  $\Gamma$ <sup>KP-MBF</sup>. It outputs M' as follows.

$$M'=\operatorname{ct}_3\bigg/\prod_{i\in S}e(\operatorname{ct}_{1,0},\operatorname{sk}_{2,i})e(\operatorname{ct}_{2,\phi(i)},\operatorname{sk}_{1,i})e(\operatorname{ct}_{1,\phi(i)},\operatorname{sk}_{3,i}).$$

#### <span id="page-46-0"></span>B.2 Completely Unbounded CP-ABE for Monotone Formulae

A predicate for completely unbounded CP-ABE for monotone Boolean formulae,  $P^{\text{CP-MBF}}: \mathfrak{X} \times \mathfrak{Y} \rightarrow \{0,1\}$ , is defined as follows:

- $\mathfrak{X} = \bigcup_{i \in \mathbb{N}} (\mathbb{Z}_p^i \times \mathfrak{F}_i)$ , where  $\mathfrak{F}_i$  consists of all monotone Boolean formulae with input length i.
- $\mathfrak{Z} = 2^{\mathbb{Z}_p}.$
- For  $X=((x_1,\ldots,x_n),f)\in \mathfrak{X}$  and  $Y=\{y_1,\ldots,y_t\}\in \mathfrak{Y}$  where  $f:\{0,1\}^n\to\{0,1\}$ , we set  $b_i=1$  iff  $x_i\in Y$ . Then, we define  $\mathsf{P}^\mathsf{CP-MBF}(X,Y)=1\Leftrightarrow f(b_1,\ldots,b_n)=1$ .

In our framework, the predicate P<sup>CP-MBF</sup> can be embedded into

$$\mathsf{Dual}[\mathsf{KBF1}[\mathsf{P}^\mathsf{IBBE}]] = \mathsf{Dual}[\mathsf{KBF1}[\mathsf{Dual}[\mathsf{KBF1}_\mathsf{OR}[\mathsf{P}^\mathsf{IBE}]]]].$$

Thus, the corresponding PES  $\Gamma^{\mathsf{CP-MBF}}$  is described as follows:

- Param() = 4
- EncCt( $(x_1, \ldots, x_n), f$ ) =  $(n, \tau, \mathbf{c})$ , where  $\tau$  is the number of AND gates in f. Let Share<sub>p</sub> be the algorithm defined in Fig 4. Polynomials  $\mathbf{c} = (c_{1,1}, \ldots, c_{1,n}, c_{2,1}, \ldots, c_{2,n})$  are defined as follows:

$$\sigma_1, \dots, \sigma_n \leftarrow \mathsf{Share}_{\mathsf{p}}(f, s_0 w_1, \hat{\mathbf{s}} = (\hat{s}_1, \dots, \hat{s}_\tau)),$$
  
$$c_{1,i} = \sigma_i - s_i w_2, \quad c_{2,i} = s_i (x_i w_3 + w_4).$$

- EncKey $(\{y_1,\ldots,y_t\})=(t+1,0,\mathbf{k})$ . Polynomials  $\mathbf{k}=(k_0,k_1,\ldots,k_t)$  are defined as follows:

$$k_0 = \alpha - r_0 w_1, \quad k_i = r_0 w_2 - r_i (y_i w_3 + w_4).$$

- Pair( $(x_1,\ldots,x_n),f,\{y_1,\ldots,y_t\}$ ) =  $(\mathbf{E},\overline{\mathbf{E}})$ . Let  $S\subseteq\{i\mid x_i\in\{y_1,\ldots,y_t\}\}$  be the set such that  $\sum_{i\in S}\sigma_i=s_0w_1$ .  $\mathbf{E}=(e_{i,j})_{i\in[n+1],j\in[t+1]}$  and  $\overline{\mathbf{E}}=(\bar{e}_{i,j})_{i\in[2n],j\in[t+1]}$  are defined as the following equation holds:

$$\mathbf{sEk}^{\top} + \mathbf{c}\overline{\mathbf{E}}\mathbf{r}^{\top} = s_0k_0 + \sum_{i \in S} (s_ik_{\phi(i)} + c_{1,i}r_0 + c_{2,i}r_{\phi(i)}),$$

where  $\phi: S \to [t]$  is a function such that  $x_i = y_{\phi(i)}$ .

Because  $\Gamma^{\mathsf{CP-MBF}}$  is obtained by applying the dual conversion twice to a PES with single-variable PMH, namely,  $\Gamma^{\mathsf{IBE}}$ ,  $\Gamma^{\mathsf{CP-MBF}}$  satisfies (3, 3)-KE-ind. Thus, the concrete scheme is described as follows.

Setup( $1^{\lambda}$ ): It takes a security parameter  $1^{\lambda}$  and outputs pk and msk as follows.

$$\mathbb{G} \leftarrow \mathcal{G}_{\mathsf{BG}}(1^{\lambda}), \quad \mathbf{A}, \mathbf{B} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{(k+3)\times k}, \quad \mathbf{h} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{k+3}, \quad \mathbf{W}_1, \dots, \mathbf{W}_4 \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{(k+3)\times (k+3)}$$
$$\mathsf{pk} = (\mathbb{G}, [\mathbf{A}]_1, [\mathbf{W}_1^{\top} \mathbf{A}]_1, \dots, [\mathbf{W}_4^{\top} \mathbf{A}]_1, [\mathbf{A}^{\top} \mathbf{h}]_{\mathsf{T}})$$
$$\mathsf{msk} = (\mathbf{B}, \mathbf{h}, \mathbf{W}_1, \dots, \mathbf{W}_4).$$

Enc(pk, X, M): It takes pk, an attribute  $X = ((x_1, \dots, x_n), f) \in \mathcal{X}$ , and a message  $M \in G_T$  and outputs  $\mathsf{ct}_X$  as follows. Let Share be an algorithm defined in Fig 5.

$$\begin{aligned} \mathbf{s}_0, \mathbf{s}_1, \dots, \mathbf{s}_n &\leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^k, \quad \boldsymbol{\sigma}_1, \dots, \boldsymbol{\sigma}_n \leftarrow \mathsf{Share}(f, \mathbf{W}_1^\top \mathbf{A} \mathbf{s}_0) \\ \mathsf{ct}_{1,i} &= [\mathbf{A} \mathbf{s}_i]_1, \quad \mathsf{ct}_{2,i} &= [\boldsymbol{\sigma}_i - \mathbf{W}_2^\top \mathbf{A} \mathbf{s}_i]_1, \quad \mathsf{ct}_{3,i} &= [(x_i \mathbf{W}_3^\top + \mathbf{W}_4^\top) \mathbf{A} \mathbf{s}_i]_1 \\ \mathsf{ct}_4 &= [\mathbf{s}_0^\top \mathbf{A}^\top \mathbf{h}]_\mathsf{T} M \\ \mathsf{ct}_X &= (\{\mathsf{ct}_{1,i}\}_{i \in [n]^+}, \{\mathsf{ct}_{2,i}, \mathsf{ct}_{3,i}\}_{i \in [n]}, \mathsf{ct}_4). \end{aligned}$$

KeyGen(pk, msk, Y): It takes pk, msk, and a set  $Y = \{y_1, \dots, y_t\} \in \mathcal{Y}$  and outputs  $\mathsf{sk}_Y$  as follows.

$$\begin{split} &\mathbf{r}_0, \mathbf{r}_1, \dots, \mathbf{r}_t \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^k \\ &\mathsf{sk}_{1,i} = [\mathbf{B}\mathbf{r}_i]_2, \ \ \mathsf{sk}_2 = [\mathbf{h} - \mathbf{W}_1 \mathbf{B}\mathbf{r}_0]_2, \ \ \mathsf{sk}_{3,i} = [\mathbf{W}_2 \mathbf{B}\mathbf{r}_0 - (y_i \mathbf{W}_3 + \mathbf{W}_4) \mathbf{B}\mathbf{r}_i]_2 \\ &\mathsf{sk}_Y = (\{\mathsf{sk}_{1,i}\}_{i \in [t]^+}, \mathsf{sk}_2, \{\mathsf{sk}_{3,i}\}_{i \in [t]}). \end{split}$$

 $\begin{aligned} \mathsf{Dec}(\mathsf{pk},\mathsf{ct}_X,\mathsf{sk}_Y) \colon & \text{It takes } \mathsf{pk}, \ \mathsf{ct}_X = (\{\mathsf{ct}_{1,i}\}_{i \in [n]^+}, \{\mathsf{ct}_{2,i},\mathsf{ct}_{3,i}\}_{i \in [n]}, \mathsf{ct}_4), \ \text{and } \mathsf{sk}_Y = (\{\mathsf{sk}_{1,i}\}_{i \in [t]^+}, \mathsf{sk}_2, \\ \{\mathsf{sk}_{3,i}\}_{i \in [t]}) \ \text{such that } \mathsf{P}^\mathsf{CP-MBF}(X,Y) = 1. \ \text{Let } S \ \text{and } \phi \ \text{be the same as those defined in Pair of } \\ & & \Gamma^\mathsf{CP-MBF}. \ \text{It outputs } M' \ \text{as follows}. \end{aligned}$ 

$$M' = \mathsf{ct}_4 \bigg/ e(\mathsf{ct}_{1,0}, \mathsf{sk}_2) \prod_{i \in S} e(\mathsf{ct}_{1,i}, \mathsf{sk}_{3,\phi(i)}) e(\mathsf{ct}_{2,i}, \mathsf{sk}_{1,0}) e(\mathsf{ct}_{3,i}, \mathsf{sk}_{1,\phi(i)}).$$

### <span id="page-47-0"></span>B.3 KP-ABE with Constant-Size Ciphertexts for Monotone Formulae

Following §6.7, we consider ABE for  $\mathsf{P}^{\mathsf{KP-MBF-16}} = \mathsf{KBF1}[\mathsf{P}^{\mathsf{IBBE}'}]$ . The corresponding PES  $\varGamma^{\mathsf{KP-MBF-16}}$  is described as follows:

$$- \operatorname{\mathsf{Param}}(T) = T + 2$$

-  $\mathsf{EncCt}(X) = (0,0,c)$  where  $c = s\mathbf{w}^{\top}\mathbf{v}_X'$ , where the non-lone variable is s.

- EncKey( $(y_1, \ldots, y_n), f$ ) =  $(n, \tau, \mathbf{k})$ , where  $\tau$  is the number of AND gates in f. Let Share<sub>p</sub> be the algorithm defined in Fig 4. Polynomials  $\mathbf{k} = (\mathbf{k}^{(1)}, \ldots, \mathbf{k}^{(n)})$  are defined as follows:

$$\begin{split} & \sigma_1, \dots, \sigma_n \leftarrow \mathsf{Share}_\mathsf{p}(f, \alpha, \hat{\mathbf{r}} = (\hat{r}_1, \dots, \hat{r}_\tau)), \\ & \mathbf{k}^{(i)} = (\sigma_i, \mathbf{0}) + r_i \mathbf{w}^\top \mathbf{M}_{y_i}'. \end{split}$$

- Pair $(X, (y_1, \ldots, y_n), f) = (\mathbf{e}, \bar{\mathbf{e}})$ . Let  $S \subseteq \{i \mid y_i \in X\}$  be the set such that  $\sum_{i \in S} \sigma_i = \alpha$ . Then,  $\mathbf{e} = (e_1, \ldots, e_{n(T+1)})$  and  $\bar{\mathbf{e}} = (\bar{e}_1, \ldots, \bar{e}_n)$  are defined as the following equation holds:

$$s\mathbf{e}\mathbf{k}^{\top} + c\overline{\mathbf{e}}\mathbf{r}^{\top} = \sum_{i \in S} (s\mathbf{k}^{(i)}\mathbf{v}_X'' - r_i c),$$

where  $\mathbf{v}_{X}'' = (1, a_{1}, \dots, a_{T})^{\top}$ .

Note that  $a_i$ ,  $\mathbf{v}_X'$ ,  $\mathbf{v}_X''$  and  $\mathbf{M}_y'$  is defined the same as those in §6.7, and we have  $\mathbf{M}_y'\mathbf{v}_X'' = \mathbf{v}_X'$  iff  $y \in X$ . Because  $\Gamma^{\mathsf{KP-MBF-16}}$  is obtained without the dual conversion,  $\Gamma^{\mathsf{KP-MBF-16}}$  satisfies (1,1)-KE-ind. Thus, the concrete scheme is described as follows.

 $\mathsf{Setup}(1^{\lambda})$ : It takes a security parameter  $1^{\lambda}$  and outputs  $\mathsf{pk}$  and  $\mathsf{msk}$  as follows.

$$\begin{split} &\mathbb{G} \leftarrow \mathcal{G}_{\mathsf{BG}}(1^{\lambda}), \ \mathbf{A}, \mathbf{B} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{(k+1) \times k}, \ \mathbf{h} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{k+1}, \ \mathbf{W}_1, \dots, \mathbf{W}_{T+2} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{(k+1) \times (k+1)} \\ &\mathsf{pk} = (\mathbb{G}, [\mathbf{A}]_1, [\mathbf{W}_1^{\top} \mathbf{A}]_1, \dots, [\mathbf{W}_{T+2}^{\top} \mathbf{A}]_1, [\mathbf{A}^{\top} \mathbf{h}]_{\mathsf{T}}) \\ &\mathsf{msk} = (\mathbf{B}, \mathbf{h}, \mathbf{W}_1, \dots, \mathbf{W}_{T+2}). \end{split}$$

 $\mathsf{Enc}(\mathsf{pk},X,M)$ : It takes  $\mathsf{pk}$ , an attribute  $X\in \mathfrak{X}_\kappa$ , and a message  $M\in G_\mathsf{T}$  and outputs  $\mathsf{ct}_X$  as follows.

$$\mathbf{s} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^k, \ \ \mathsf{ct}_1 = [\mathbf{A}\mathbf{s}]_1, \ \ \mathsf{ct}_2 = \left[\sum_{\ell \in [T+2]} v_{X,\ell}' \mathbf{W}_\ell \mathbf{A}\mathbf{s}\right]_1, \ \ \mathsf{ct}_3 = [\mathbf{s}^\top \mathbf{A}^\top \mathbf{h}]_\mathsf{T} M$$
$$\mathsf{ct}_X = (\mathsf{ct}_1, \mathsf{ct}_2, \mathsf{ct}_3),$$

where  $v'_{X,\ell}$  denotes the  $\ell$ -th element of  $\mathbf{v}'_X$ .

KeyGen(pk, msk, Y): It takes pk, msk, and a predicate  $Y = ((y_1, \ldots, y_n), f) \in \mathcal{Y}_{\kappa}$  and outputs  $\mathsf{sk}_Y$  as follows. Let Share be an algorithm defined in Fig 5.

$$\begin{split} \mathbf{r}_1, \dots, \mathbf{r}_n &\leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^k, \quad \pmb{\sigma}_1, \dots, \pmb{\sigma}_n \leftarrow \mathsf{Share}(f, \mathbf{h}) \\ \mathsf{sk}_{1,i} &= [\mathbf{B}\mathbf{r}_i]_2, \quad \mathsf{sk}_{2,i,j} = \begin{cases} [\pmb{\sigma}_i + \sum_{\ell \in [T+2]} m'_{y_i,\ell,j} \mathbf{W}_\ell \mathbf{B}\mathbf{r}_i]_2 & j = 1 \\ [\sum_{\ell \in [T+2]} m'_{y_i,\ell,j} \mathbf{W}_\ell \mathbf{B}\mathbf{r}_i]_2 & 2 \leq j \leq T+1 \end{cases} \\ \mathsf{sk}_Y &= (\{\mathsf{sk}_{1,i}\}_{i \in [n]}, \{\mathsf{sk}_{2,i,j}\}_{i \in [n], j \in [T+1]}), \end{split}$$

where  $m'_{y,\ell,j}$  denotes the  $(\ell,j)$ -th element of  $\mathbf{M}'_{y_i}$ .

Dec(pk, ct<sub>X</sub>, sk<sub>Y</sub>): It takes pk, ct<sub>X</sub> = (ct<sub>1</sub>, ct<sub>2</sub>, ct<sub>3</sub>), and sk<sub>Y</sub> = ({sk<sub>1,i</sub>}<sub>i∈[n]</sub>, {sk<sub>2,i,j</sub>}<sub>i∈[n],j∈[T+1]</sub>) such that P<sup>KP-MBF-16</sup>(X, Y) = 1. Let S be the same as that defined in Pair of  $\Gamma$ <sup>KP-MBF-16</sup>. It outputs M' as follows.

$$M' = \mathsf{ct}_3 \bigg/ \prod_{i \in S} \left( \left( \prod_{j \in [T+1]} e(\mathsf{ct}_1, \mathsf{sk}_{2,i,j})^{v_{X,j}''} \right) / e(\mathsf{ct}_2, \mathsf{sk}_{1,i}) \right),$$

where  $v_{X,j}''$  is the *j*-th element of  $\mathbf{v}_X''$ .
